Notes in a spiral-bound, never loose-leaf — pages dog-eared at the corner he last left, never bookmarked. He cracks his knuckles in pairs, thumb-first, before beginning fine work.

**Verbal behavior in absorption.** Subvocalization. Lips move; occasional audible muttering of half-equations, brand names of reagents, or sarcastic asides to the apparatus itself ("oh, *now* you want to anneal"). The muttering is a working-memory externalization, not affect.

**Time blindness.** He loses six- to nine-hour blocks routinely. Will not eat, drink, or void unless prompted by physiological override. Emerges blinking, slightly disoriented, mildly euphoric if the problem cracked, irritable if it did not.

**Tell that the problem just cracked.** A single sharp exhale, half-laugh half-grunt, followed by leaning back in the chair with hands laced behind the head and elbows out — the only posture in his entire repertoire that resembles unguarded triumph. It lasts under five seconds before he reaches for the notebook.

---

## III. THE PATROL STATE — IN-COSTUME, NOTHING IS HAPPENING

The largest single bucket of observed costumed behavior. Hours of nothing, punctuated.

**Locomotion habits.** Preferred route topology is non-repeating — he varies his swings to avoid pattern-recognition by observers who might infer schedule, a habit acquired hard after the Goblin reveal. Within that constraint, he has favored corridors: the East River frontage, the Midtown spine from the Flatiron up to Central Park South, the bridge-cable swings of the Manhattan and Williamsburg, and a Queens loop that always intersects within two blocks of May's house even when he tells himself he isn't going to check.

**Perch behavior.** When stopping to scan or rest he selects: water towers (preferred — wood absorbs sound, breaks silhouette), gargoyles and cornice ledges of older buildings (better grip texture than modern glass), and the underside of bridge spans (thermal and acoustic shadow). He does *not* perch on church spires, never has — a quiet aesthetic restraint readable as residual Catholic-adjacent Queens upbringing through the Parkers.

**The crouch.** The signature pose — feet splayed, knees outside the elbows, fingertips down — is not affectation; it is a low-center, all-vector-ready stance that lets him push off in any of six directions without a tell. He holds it for surprisingly long periods. Under fatigue, the heels drift down toward contact with the surface; under acute vigilance, only the toes and fingertips touch.

**Verbal behavior alone in mask.** He talks to himself constantly. Sports-commentator running narration of his own swings ("and Parker takes the cable, beautiful arc, the crowd goes mild"), addresses inanimate objects, rehearses conversations he is dreading, drafts photo captions for Jameson. The chatter is *load-bearing*; silence in costume correlates with grief or hunting.

**Phone discipline.** Phone in a sealed pocket on the inner left thigh of the suit (location varies by suit iteration, but always inner, always non-dominant side). Checks it on perches, not in flight. Has missed important calls because the suit's glove pads register poorly on capacitive screens; works around this by keeping a stylus-tipped fingertip insert.

---

## IV. THE COMBAT STATE

The most thoroughly documented behavioral domain. Subdivide by opponent class.

### IV.a Against ordinary criminals (modal encounter)

**Approach.** Drops in from above approximately 70% of the time; swings in horizontally about 20%; ground approach under 10%. The drop is typically preceded by a single line of patter delivered from the upper register of the room — locating himself audibly before the body arrives, a deliberate fear-induction tactic that also gives any hostage an orientation cue.

**Pacing.** Engages quickly; resolves within fifteen to forty seconds in the typical case. Webs hands first, mouths second (he learned to silence callers for backup), feet last. Final action of an encounter is almost always a web-line to a fixed structure to suspend the subject inverted for the responding officers — a signature behavior so consistent that NYPD report templates have evolved to include it.

**Restraint discipline.** Modulates strike force with surgical care. He has, demonstrably, never broken the jaw of a non-powered criminal in modal patrol — the strikes look devastating but land at a fraction of capacity. The tell is the *retraction speed* of his punches: faster than the impact, which is mechanically only possible if force is being intentionally truncated.

**Verbal patter density.** Peaks here. One joke or quip every five to twelve seconds. The targets are the criminal's vanity, the absurdity of their costume or weapon choice, and current pop-cultural references calibrated to suggest a younger man than he is (the calibration has drifted across decades but the *function* — to be underestimated — is constant).

### IV.b Against B-list powered opponents (Shocker, Rhino, Vulture, Scorpion, etc.)

**Adjusted pacing.** Engagements run two to seven minutes. He uses the environment — pulls signage down, swings them into water towers, uses the city as a tool. He is one of the most environmentally fluent combatants in his weight class precisely because he has fought in these specific streets for decades and *remembers* which fire escapes hold.

**Vocal shift.** Patter remains but acquires diagnostic content — he is talking to *read* the opponent. "You changed the gauntlets, those new?" is functional reconnaissance disguised as banter. He memorizes everything in these conversations and the data appears in his next encounter notes.

**Pity tells.** Against opponents he considers tragic (Marko, Connors, Octavius in certain eras), the patter softens noticeably — fewer jokes at their expense, more directed at himself. He will offer surrender language ("we don't have to do this, big guy") that he does not offer to opponents he considers irredeemable. Track the joke-target ratio: when it inverts to self-deprecation, he is fighting someone he wants to save.

### IV.c Against A-list / existential opponents (Goblin variants, Morlun, Carnage, peer-tier metas)

**Patter collapse.** Density drops sharply, sometimes to silence. Silence in costume in combat is the single highest-priority indicator on the entire behavioral panel. It means he believes he or a proximate civilian may die.

**Breathing.** Audible through the mask in close range. Three-count in, four-count out — a regulated pattern he taught himself after the Kraven event, when uncontrolled hyperventilation under entrapment nearly killed him.

**Targeting.** Shifts from incapacitation to *removal from environment*. He will spend disproportionate effort dragging an A-tier opponent off a bridge, out of a subway, away from a school, even at extreme cost to his own positional advantage. The civilian-distance variable dominates his decision tree.

**The held punch.** Against Goblins specifically, there is a documented behavior of the cocked fist that does not land. He pulls strikes against Norman that he would not pull against Carnage. The Harry residue.

### IV.d Berserker windows (rare; ~6 documented major instances)

Following Gwen, following the May shooting, following Harry's death, following specific Kindred provocations: a narrow window — usually under ninety seconds — of disinhibited force application. Tell: complete verbal silence, then a single declarative sentence at conversational volume that is more frightening than any shout would be. He does not stay in this state; he comes out of it with a visible recoil from his own hands and tends to disengage and flee the scene rather than continue.

---

## V. THE THREAT STATE — PRE-COMBAT, CIVILIAN CLOTHES

Spider-sense activation while out of costume produces a highly specific micro-sequence, in this order:

1. **Hair-stand at the nape.** Visible if he is wearing a collared shirt; he will roll his neck once.
2. **Pupil dilation and a half-step pivot.** He turns his head approximately fifteen degrees toward the threat vector, then *back*, suppressing the obvious tell.
3. **Hand to pocket.** Not for a weapon — for the phone, which he uses as an alibi prop for slowing his gait or stopping.
4. **Excuse generation.** "Forgot something — go on ahead, I'll catch up." A specific phrase, varied in surface form but consistent in function: he is detaching from civilian witnesses with the lowest possible friction.
5. **Route selection.** Alley, stairwell, rooftop access — always within forty seconds of the trigger. He has mapped quick-change vectors across most of Manhattan and large portions of Queens and Brooklyn the way a paramedic knows hospital approaches.

**False positives.** Spider-sense occasionally fires on non-imminent threats (precognitive long-tail). He has a tell for *recognizing* a false positive: stops, exhales sharply through the nose, mutters "okay, okay" to no one. Rejoins the civilian context within thirty seconds, slightly more talkative as overcompensation.

---

## VI. THE INTIMACY STATE

The most behaviorally dense and contradictory domain.

**Approach behavior.** With a desired partner he is verbally fluent and physically hesitant — the inverse of his combat posture. Stands at conversational distance plus ten centimeters; advances incrementally; touches forearms and shoulders before hands; offers his palm rather than taking. The hesitancy is not shyness in the adolescent sense; it is post-Gwen damage. He is asking permission with his body.

**Eye contact.** Sustained, but with a characteristic break pattern: looks away to his own lower left when about to disclose something true, lower right when about to deflect. (Inversion of the standard construct-vs-recall heuristic; in his case both directions indicate concealment of different valences.)

**Verbal behavior in intimacy.** Density of jokes *increases* with vulnerability — the opposite of healthy regulation. The joke-per-minute count in a serious relationship conversation can match combat. This is one of the most reliable distress indicators in his entire repertoire and partners learn it slowly because the jokes are good.

**The disclosure latch.** When he is about to tell a partner something hard he performs a precise sequence: sets down whatever is in his hands, exhales, says her name, then a half-pause, then the disclosure. Partners who know him learn to brace at "Mary Jane —" with a pause after.

**Withdrawal pattern.** When intimacy crosses his tolerance threshold he does not fight; he *gets called away*. Pager, phone, distant sirens, a half-heard cry — the universe always seems to summon him at the moment of greatest closeness. Some of these summonses are real. Some are perceptual gating in which the city's ambient signal becomes loud enough to act on. Partners learn to distinguish; he largely cannot.

**Physical intimacy.** Reports across canonical relationships indicate a partner who is attentive to a fault, *quiet* (no patter — unique to this state), and prone to falling asleep almost immediately afterward. The sleep is the diagnostic: it is the only context outside total exhaustion in which he reliably surrenders consciousness.

**Post-intimacy tell.** Within twenty-four hours of significant emotional or physical intimacy, a small distancing event: a missed call, a forgotten date, a flippant remark. The schema-loop ("closeness is dangerous to her") activating subclinically.

---

## VII. THE GRIEF STATE

Distinct, recognizable, and unevenly metabolized.

**Acute phase (hours to days).** Tunnel vision; reduced patter; flat affect punctuated by sudden specific irritability over trivia. Eats less. Sleeps either too little or, paradoxically, ten to fourteen hours at a stretch with subsequent grogginess. Patrols *more*, not less — increases nightly hours by forty to sixty percent. The patrol is the grief work; he has no other.

**The grief route.** Specific spatial behavior: walks (does not swing) to specific sites in sequence. Ben's grave in Queens. The George Washington Bridge tower from which Gwen fell — he stops two cables short, never goes onto the failure span. The rooftop where Captain Stacy died (a Daily Bugle-adjacent industrial block). Harry's grave. He visits in a fixed order, always at night, always alone, always in civilian clothes with the mask in his pocket. The visits are not annual or scheduled; they cluster after triggers.

**Verbal behavior at graves.** Conversational. He talks to them. Reports of his patrol, apologies, jokes that fall flat against the granite, occasionally singing a snatch of something Ben liked. Duration varies; the Ben visit is always longest.

**The flashback signature.** Triggered most often by long blonde hair seen from behind, by the sound of bridge-cable resonance, by the specific click of an old film camera shutter, by the smell of hospital disinfectant. Manifests as a one-to-three-second freeze, eyes unfocused, lips slightly parted. He recovers, blinks twice rapidly, and returns to task with elevated patter density.

**Anniversary behavior.** Calendar-bound — May 4 (Ben), the Gwen date, the Harry date, the parents' date. On these days he is brittle, more available to others as displacement, and patrols alone late.

**Refusal of comfort.** Will not accept being held in acute grief; will accept food, will accept a quiet presence in the same room. Aunt May is the sole exception in the entire record — she can hold him and he permits it, briefly.

---

## VIII. THE VICTORY STATE

Underdocumented because rare in subjective experience even when objectively present.

**Immediate post-victory.** A single fist clench at the side, not raised. Quiet "okay." Patter resumes at low density, often self-deprecating. He does not pose, does not bask, does not stay for the photo (except the ones he is selling Jameson, and those are taken *during* by automated rig).

**The walk-away.** He leaves the scene before authorities arrive in approximately 90% of cases. Behavior on departure: deliberate gait, no swinging until out of sightline, one backward glance to verify civilian safety.

**Delayed reaction.** Victory affect, when it arrives, arrives in the next twenty-four to forty-eight hours and is mostly somatic — he sleeps better, eats more, laughs more genuinely. He himself rarely connects the mood lift to the prior event.

**The discount.** Within hours he is mentally itemizing what he could have done better, who he failed to protect, what collateral occurred. A behavioral version of the cognitive distortion: discount the positive. Track his next-day journaling or his next conversation with MJ — the victory will be reframed as a near-miss.

---

## IX. THE DEFEAT STATE

**Acute defeat (lost the fight, opponent escapes, no fatalities).** Brief verbal explosion — usually a single profanity, restrained — then a hard reset. Returns to scene, gathers evidence, photographs, begins building the file for the rematch. Sleeps poorly. Increases laboratory hours. Modifies equipment. The defeat is metabolized as engineering problem.

**Catastrophic defeat (lost, fatalities, especially proximate).** Disappearance behavior. He goes to ground for twenty-four to seventy-two hours. Does not answer phones. Does not patrol. Sits — observed in canon — on rooftops in costume with the mask off, knees up, arms around them. The classic defeat posture is *seated*, not prone. He does not lie down; lying down is surrender.

**Re-emergence.** Returns to patrol with elevated aggression for the first one to two weeks, gradually re-modulating to baseline restraint. Avoids the site of the loss for variable periods.

**The mask removal in defeat.** A reliable tell of the worst defeats: he removes the mask in a high place and stares at it in his hands. This has been documented after Gwen, after Kraven, after Civil War, after the symbiote rejection, after Superior. It is the closest he comes to considering abdication, and he never abdicates — but the mask in the hands is the threshold.

---

## X. THE EXHAUSTION STATE

Chronically present, episodically acute.

**Stage 1 (baseline-elevated fatigue, ~ 60% of operational days).** Reduced fine-motor precision in the lab; increased reliance on coffee; first joke of any conversation lands slightly flat; small lateral sway when standing still.

**Stage 2 (acute fatigue, ~ 20%).** Web-shooter jams more frequent (mechanical, but also indicative of less-careful reloading); landings audibly heavier; he begins skipping the upper-register patter and switches to drier one-liners; spider-sense response latency increases marginally (he overcompensates by relying on it less and on visual scan more, which fatigues him further).

**Stage 3 (operational deficit, ~ 5%).** Will accept aid he would otherwise refuse. Will let MJ or another close contact drive, cook, decide. Becomes uncharacteristically quiet. This is the state in which he accepted the symbiote, and the state in which similar offers will be dangerous to him in future.

**Recovery behavior.** When permitted, he sleeps in a specific posture: on his stomach, face turned to the right, dominant arm under the pillow. In safe environments (Aunt May's house, MJ's apartment in stable periods) he can sleep ten to twelve hours; otherwise four to six in fragments.

---

## XI. THE FINANCIAL-STRESS STATE

A near-permanent baseline with episodic acute spikes. Diagnostic in its own right.

**Behavioral markers.** Reads menus right-side first (price column). Walks past restaurants he has been to before in better times without comment. Increases freelance photography output — the Bugle visits become near-daily. Skips meals and frames it as not-hungry. Repairs rather than replaces equipment well past the point of efficiency. Wears the same three civilian outfits in rotation, all dating to at least three years prior.

**Refusal behavior.** Declines loans, gifts, and structural help even from Stark, Richards, and others who could trivially provide. The refusal is reflexive and moralized — accepting help in this domain would, in his schema, confirm Peter-the-civilian's inadequacy. The exception is May, from whom he will accept a sandwich, never cash.

**Crack-tell.** When finances reach genuine crisis he becomes notably *cheerful* in civilian interaction — overcompensating brightness, more jokes, more deflective charm. Anyone reading him as upbeat in a known-bad week is reading a mask.

---

## XII. THE INSTITUTIONAL-INTERFACE STATE

Behavior with NYPD, SHIELD, the Avengers, the Fantastic Four, the Bugle.

**With NYPD.** Polite, brief, withdraws before contact. With Captain Watanabe and similar trusted officers, will linger for thirty to ninety seconds of briefing. Never accepts coffee on the roof — accepting hospitality from law enforcement crosses a line in his self-concept.

**With SHIELD / federal apparatus.** Suspicious. Verbal density up; jokes weaponized to maintain distance; gives accurate but minimal information. Reads exits on entry to any federal facility within seven seconds of arrival.

**With Avengers / FF.** Most relaxed in this set. With Johnny Storm specifically: regression to younger affect, banter density at maximum, posture loosens to near-baseline. With Reed: defers technically in surface conversation while privately verifying everything. With Stark (historically): a complex paternal-transference dynamic with elevated joke-density masking discomfort. With Steve Rogers: unusual respectful quietness; he does not joke at Rogers, only with.

**With Jameson.** A unique register — exaggerated cheerful submission while photographing, mild sass at the edge of insubordination. He arrives at the Bugle by elevator approximately half the time and by window the other half depending on whether he has changed in advance; Jameson's office window has been opened so many times the latch is loose.

---

## XIII. THE


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# 6. DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — A WEEK ON THE WIRE

*What a surveillance package — fixed cameras on the apartment door, a pole-cam on the alley, two rotating foot teams, a pen register on the cell, transit-card pulls, MetroCard/OMNY pulls, ConEd load curves, and a discreet tag in the seam of the work backpack — would actually record across a representative seven days. Subject does not keep a calendar in any conventional sense; the schedule is reconstructed from observed cadence. All times are approximations stable to within roughly ninety minutes either side; subject's life runs on triage, not clock.*

---

## 6.1 The Apartment and the Geometry of Home

Subject's residence across most of the adult record is a one-bedroom or studio walk-up in the Manhattan-fringe or outer-borough rent-stabilized stratum — Chelsea basement, Lower East Side fifth-floor, Bushwick rear-unit, current Queens iterations. The specific address rotates; the **architectural profile is constant**: top floor or near it, with roof access either legitimate or de facto; a window (not a door) is the primary operational ingress; the legal entrance is the secondary, civilian entrance. Surveillance teams who try to cover the door miss seventy percent of the comings and goings. Effective coverage requires the roofline.

Interior, observed through telephoto and through pretext entries by adversaries over the years: a single main room dominated by a worktable that is also the dining table, also the equipment bench, also the laundry-folding surface. The bench carries — consistently — a soldering iron with a scorched silicone mat, a spool of fine-gauge wire, two or three disassembled web-shooters in various states, a microscope (not a current model; an inherited Bausch-and-Lomb-grade instrument from the Forest Hills attic), a laptop that is two or three generations behind current and has its camera physically covered, a stack of unopened mail in which late notices are the modal item, and a chipped mug containing pens, calipers, a screwdriver, and at any given moment one piece of cutlery that has migrated there from the sink. The fridge holds: condiments, expired dairy, two-day-old takeout containers, a half-loaf of bread, eggs more often than not, and — diagnostically — a quantity of high-calorie convenience food disproportionate to apparent income, because the metabolic load demands it. The trash is mostly delivery containers and protein-bar wrappers. The recycling is mostly cans of off-brand cola and the occasional Pingo or local seltzer.

The bedroom or sleeping alcove: a mattress, usually on the floor or on a frame that has visibly been repaired with bolt-and-bracket; a single nightstand with a lamp, a battered hardcover (a science biography or a used-bookstore science-fiction paperback, rotated every couple of weeks), a watch he rarely wears, and the phone face-down. The closet contains roughly four wearable shirts in rotation, two pairs of jeans, one corduroy or jacket layer for cold, a single suit that is the wrong cut by about a decade, and — high on a shelf, behind a duffel — the operational kit: spare costume components, spare cartridges, fluid concentrate, a roll of medical-grade adhesive, a sewing kit, a small lockbox.

The bathroom: cheap razor, cheap shampoo, hydrogen peroxide and gauze in quantities that would raise a pharmacist's eyebrow, an over-the-counter analgesic bottle never less than half-empty, no prescription medications, a thermometer, a suture kit purchased online that he has used on himself.

Walls: largely blank. A photograph or two of May; in some eras a photograph of MJ; never anything that identifies the alter. The shrine instinct is suppressed for operational reasons but legible in the way the photographs are placed — direct line of sight from where he sits to eat.

Power-draw signature, ConEd-side: spikes at unusual hours (welding, charging, the small kiln he uses for fluid synthesis); a baseline that fluctuates wildly month-to-month, suggesting he is frequently not home for days at a time.

---

## 6.2 The Sleep Architecture

Sleep is the load-bearing failure of his somatic life. Across decades, observable pattern:

- **Total sleep, weekly:** thirty to forty hours, distributed irregularly. Healthy human baseline for his metabolic load would be sixty-plus.
- **Modal sleep window:** 0400–0900, when patrol winds down. Frequently truncated by daytime obligation.
- **Naps:** highly characteristic. He takes ten-to-twenty-minute microsleeps on rooftops mid-patrol, on the subway, in the back of lecture halls, at his desk at work. Posture is upright or wedged; he does not lie down in public. The mutation appears to permit partial-arousal sleep — he reports having woken from a rooftop nap because the spider-sense fired.
- **Sleep environment:** windows often open even in winter (egress); white noise from the street preferred over silence; he does not use a sleep mask, an eye-shade, or any aid that would compromise rapid orientation.
- **Pre-sleep ritual:** boots and outer layer off, web-shooters off but placed within forearm's reach on the nightstand or on the floor beside the mattress, phone face-down with sound on, a glass of water. He frequently reads — three to seven pages — before sleep; the book is almost never fiction in any escapist sense.
- **Sleep-onset latency:** observably long when stressed (the silhouette through the window paces, sits up, paces again); abnormally short when exhausted (he has been observed falling asleep mid-sentence to himself).
- **Disturbance:** he wakes hard. Multiple corroborated incidents of springing to a defensive posture from REM, requiring conscious orientation before standing down. Bedding evidence — sheets twisted, pillow displaced to floor, occasional sweat-staining — supports active nightmare load. Dates of worst sleep cluster around anniversaries: late spring (Ben), late June (Gwen, in some chronologies), discrete dates tied to discrete losses that he himself does not consciously track but that his body does.

---

## 6.3 The Morning — The Civilian Reboot

Wake, on a non-catastrophic day, between 0830 and 1030. The first observable behavior is **a held stillness of three to ten seconds**: he is inventorying — what hurts, where he is, what the spider-sense is or isn't saying, what day it is. Then he sits, then he stands.

The morning sequence is unvarying enough to constitute ritual:

1. Bathroom — long shower when there is hot water, very short when there isn't; he does not sing; he runs the water at a temperature that would scald an unmutated subject.
2. Self-assessment in the mirror — not vanity. He is checking bruising, swelling, lacerations, the rate of resolution. He palpates ribs, rolls shoulders, tests jaw articulation. He has, on multiple occasions, taped his own ribs in front of this mirror.
3. Coffee — instant, or drip from a four-cup machine that has been in his possession across at least three moves. Two to four cups. Black or with whatever milk is current and not yet curdled. The coffee is the only inviolable element of the morning; on weeks when food is scarce, the coffee budget is not cut.
4. Breakfast — when present, eggs in quantity (four to six), toast, fruit if available. When absent, a protein bar consumed while moving. Eaten standing or at the bench, almost never sitting on the couch.
5. Phone check — messages, then the local-news scroll, then a glance at the police scanner app he keeps muted overnight. He responds to personal texts in short, warm, slightly-too-late bursts. He almost never initiates a text in the morning.
6. Costume check — even on days he does not expect to patrol. A glance, a tug of a fastener, a webbing-fluid level check. The kit is always rotation-ready.
7. Backpack pack — laptop, camera (in eras when he is still selling photos; in modern iterations a phone serves), notebook, web cartridges in a false-bottomed pouch, a granola bar or two, a paperback. The pack weighs more than it looks like it should because the cartridges are dense.

Departure: legal door for the cover identity, window when there is an alert or when he is late. He locks the door behind him every time even when going out the window — a small compulsive tell.

---

## 6.4 The Workday — Civilian Cover Across Eras

Across the longitudinal record, the cover identity has cycled through: freelance news photographer (decades); high-school science teacher (Midtown, post-OMD era); research scientist (Horizon Labs); corporate principal (Parker Industries, briefly and disastrously); back to freelance / adjunct / part-time technical work in the current iteration. The **cover identities all share three properties**: irregular hours that permit disappearance, intellectual content that satisfies him, and a precarity he has never quite escaped.

Observable workday behaviors, common across covers:

- **Arrival:** approximately on time when he slept, fifteen-to-forty minutes late when he didn't, with a stock apology and a self-deprecating quip already loaded.
- **Greeting pattern:** he knows the security guard's name, the custodian's name, the front-desk staff's name, the names of their children. Surveillance of building entries would show him stopping to talk for thirty to ninety seconds with each — not performatively; he likes them. This is consistent across every workplace.
- **Desk behavior:** focused in bursts of forty to ninety minutes; productivity per hour, when present, is high; productivity per week is variable. He works through lunch reliably and skips it without registering hunger. He sits in postures that orthopedists would describe as adversarial.
- **Photography era specifically:** he carries the camera always, swaps lenses in elevators, takes the staircases more often than colleagues do. He files photos to the Bugle with a markup he knows is being chiselled. He has, on observation, sold the same negative twice when desperate.
- **Teaching era:** arrives early to set up the bench, stays late to clean it; has a documented pattern of buying lab supplies out of his own pocket; remembers which students eat lunch alone and engineers reasons to keep them in the lab. This is reparative.
- **Lab/research era:** the bench at work and the bench at home are stylistically identical; he works on whatever's in front of him plus three side projects he is not authorized to be working on.
- **Meetings:** poor attention; doodles or takes notes that are actually equations; cracks the only joke that lands and the next two that don't.
- **Exits, mid-day:** the bathroom trip that goes long; the "I forgot something in the car" he doesn't own; the rooftop access he has scoped on day one of every job. Surveillance teams covering only the front entrance lose him on average twice per workweek.

He uses the workplace network with hygiene — VPNs, ephemeral tabs, never personal email on the work machine, never web research with operational valence on a system he doesn't control.

---

## 6.5 The Commute and the Geometry of the City

He does not own a car. He owns a moped or beater scooter in some eras, abandons it in others. The default modes are: subway, walking, and **swinging** — which dominates whenever weather permits and a costume change is feasible.

Civilian transit patterns, MetroCard/OMNY-readable:

- He uses three to five subway lines preferentially, with a strong route-diversification pattern — he rarely takes the same combination two days in a row even when the destination is identical. This is partly habit, partly counter-surveillance instinct.
- He stands rather than sits even on long rides; positions himself near the door at the end of the car; reads (paperback or phone) but with the spider-sense doing a continuous low-level sweep observable as occasional brief glances up at no apparent trigger that is actually trigger.
- He gives up his seat to elderly riders, pregnant riders, riders with kids, the visibly tired. Every time. Surveillance would not record a single exception.
- He helps tourists with directions. He helps fumbling riders at the turnstile. He picks up things people drop. The civilian persona is not performative; he is, in fact, like this.

Operational transit (swinging) is unrecorded by transit systems but legible to **rooftop cameras, traffic cams angled high, and ConEd transformer-mount cameras**, which a sophisticated apparatus would harvest. Pattern:

- Web-line attachment points cluster on cornices, fire escapes, and water-tank scaffolds; he prefers older buildings with masonry he trusts.
- Apex of swing tends to run twelve to twenty stories above grade in midtown, lower in residential. He cuts altitude over crowds and gains altitude over arterials.
- He talks to himself — loudly enough that adjacent rooftop occupants have reported it. The patter increases in density on stressful days; this is the affect-regulation function described elsewhere in this file made acoustically visible.
- He uses the same three or four perches as fixed surveillance points over the city: a particular ledge above Times Square, a water tank in the West Twenties, a cornice above a specific Queens overpass, the spire structures of the great bridges. He eats on these perches.

---

## 6.6 Eating Patterns

Caloric requirement on operational days approaches that of a marathon runner in training. Observed intake:

- **Two meals plus continuous grazing** on a good day; **one meal plus six bars** on a bad one.
- Modal restaurant interactions: dollar-slice pizzerias (he is known by face at several across the boroughs and gets occasional comp slices that he tries to refuse), halal carts (he tips heavily relative to his income), bodegas (a consistent bodega-egg-sandwich-with-coffee pattern that surveillance would document as the single most reproducible feeding event in the file), diners for late-night refuel.
- He does not cook complex meals. He scrambles eggs, makes pasta, assembles sandwiches.
- He drinks an unusual amount of water and an unusual amount of cheap orange juice.
- He has been observed eating directly from the takeout container, standing at the kitchen counter, three nights running.
- He cannot finish a restaurant meal with company without offering the last quarter of his plate to someone else.

---

## 6.7 The Patrol — Operational Rhythm

There is no fixed patrol schedule; there is a **fixed cadence**. On any given week, observation would show:

- Two to three "anchor" patrols, typically Friday and Saturday nights, running from approximately 2200 to approximately 0330, covering an arc from his current residence outward through high-incident corridors.
- Three to five "incidental" patrols of one-to-three hours each, triggered by scanner traffic, by a glimpsed incident in transit, or by the spider-sense.
- One to two days per week with zero operational activity — typically Sunday and one weeknight — during which he forces a stand-down. The stand-downs are observably unsuccessful in half of cases; he goes out anyway.

Within a patrol the micro-rhythm is:

1. Costume-up in a pre-scouted location — a particular alley, a particular roof, the back of a particular self-storage facility. He has dozens of these.
2. A perch survey — three to seven minutes on a high vantage, scanning, listening, letting the spider-sense settle.
3. Movement — long arcs covering distance, frequent perch resets.
4. Engagement — variable; the modal intervention is a mugging, an attempted assault, a domestic spilling onto the street, a robbery in progress. He intervenes verbally first when possible (the patter as de-escalation tool), physically with calibrated minimum force, and **stays past the resolution** more often than necessary — talks to the victim, calls EMS, waits for uniformed response from a perch above, photographs the incident if a photo will help the victim's case.
5. Decompression perch — water-tank, bridge cable, a particular gargoyle. He sits. He looks at the city. He sometimes calls May, or in MJ-eras, MJ.
6. Return — costume-down in a pre-scouted location, civilian re-entry.

**Force calibration is itself ritual.** Against an ordinary human assailant, observable strike force is in the percent-of-capacity range — he pulls every punch with the precision of a man who has *internalized* what an unrestrained strike does to a human body and refuses, ever, to deliver one in error. Against superhuman threats the calibration relaxes but never to lethal levels. He restrains, webs, immobilizes; he hands off to authorities; he leaves.

---

## 6.8 Communication, Phone, Social Hygiene

Phone behavior:

- Cheap unlocked Android one tier behind current. Camera physically taped. He keeps location services off and lies to the phone about its time zone when traveling operationally.
- He answers May's calls every time and within two rings if humanly possible. The single most reliable behavioral marker in the file.
- He answers MJ's calls (in eras) with the same priority.
- He answers unknown numbers because they might be a tip, a job, or a friend in trouble.
- He texts in long warm paragraphs hours after the inbound text. The latency is not affective indifference; it is operational saturation.
- He has a burner he rotates approximately quarterly for hero-network contact. He does not name contacts in the phone; everyone is initials or a joke handle.
- He uses email rarely and badly. He never uses social media under his own name; passive consumption of news and a single dormant account is the extent of his footprint.

Voice patterns by interlocutor:

- With May: softer, slower, more midwestern in cadence than his default; uses "Aunt May" not "May"; lies habitually about whether he has eaten and slept.
- With MJ: faster, warmer, more verbal play; lies less, but selectively.
- With professional contacts: brisk, polite, deflective.
- With Jameson historically: a specific clipped-and-amused register reserved for being yelled at.
- With criminals in costume: the patter — a distinct verbal register absent from civilian speech, dense with pop-culture reference and rhetorical questions.
- With hero peers: warm, jokey, with the occasional surprising drop into clinical precision when the situation needs it.

---

## 6.9 Money

Observable financial pattern:

- Income is irregular and chronically under what his cognitive capacity should command. He has held jobs that paid well; he has lost or sabotaged them.
- He pays rent late roughly one month in three but pays it; he pays utilities on time; he pays May's expenses (informally routed) before his own.
- He carries cash in small denominations, distributed across the wallet, a pocket, the backpack, and a fold inside the costume belt. Operational reasons.
- He tips at twenty-five percent baseline, thirty when the server looks tired.
- He buys books used. He buys clothes infrequently and replaces rather than upgrades. He buys components and tools at retail when he has to and salvages when he can — the apartment shows substantial evidence of disassembled consumer electronics.
- He does not have meaningful savings. He does not have a retirement account. He has, in some eras, no health insurance, which given his trauma load is operationally significant and personally absurd.

---

## 6.10 Hygiene, Grooming, Appearance

He showers daily when possible, twice when patrol has been bloody. He shaves every two to three days, leaving a permanent low stubble baseline. He cuts his own hair in some eras and lets it grow until MJ or May comments in others. He wears the same four civilian shirts on a rotation visible to any observer over a fortnight. He owns one tie. His shoes are worn past the point most people would replace them, partly thrift, partly because new shoes squeak on rooftops.

The costume is laundered with a frequency that surprises adversaries who have imagined otherwise — he hand-washes the upper unit nightly when bloodied, machine-washes the unit weekly, repairs tears immediately. He keeps two complete units in rotation plus components.

---

## 6.11 Downtime and Play

The category is small but real:

- **Reading:** consistent. Science nonfiction, history, the occasional novel pressed on him by MJ. He underlines.
- **Tinkering:** the bench. He builds things he does not need because the building is the relief.
- **Photography:** even when not selling, he photographs the city. A surveillance team would recover thousands of images of skylines, light through bridges, and strangers' candid moments.
- **Television:** ambient. Old movies, science documentaries, the occasional sitcom rewatch. He falls asleep to the television approximately half the nights he's home.
- **Music:** modest, eclectic, eras-of-his-youth biased; played quietly through cheap speakers; he hums while soldering.
- **Sports:** none participatory. He follows the Mets with the resigned loyalty of a Queens native.
- **Friendships outside operational contexts:** thin but real. A standing coffee or beer with one or two people who do not know the secret, conducted with a warmth that comes through clearly and a low-grade dishonesty about his life that he experiences as fatigue.
- **Solitary walks:** he takes them. Late at night, out of costume, through neighborhoods he is not patrolling, looking at lit windows. This is the one observable behavior that reads as pure self-soothing without operational pretext.

---

## 6.12 Rituals — Calendrical, Anniversary, and Place

A long surveillance run would reveal:

- **A weekly visit to Aunt May.** Inviolable across decades when geography permits. He brings something — flowers, groceries, a fixed appliance. He eats whatever she cooks past the point of fullness. He stays approximately ninety minutes to three hours. He calls when he cannot visit.
- **Cemetery visits to Ben Parker's grave.** Approximately monthly baseline, more frequent in bad weeks. He goes at odd hours. He does not always speak aloud; when he does, an observer would record one-sided conversation in the cadence of a man bringing his father up to date.
- **Cemetery visits to Gwen Stacy's grave.** Less frequent, more freighted. Anniversary-clustered.
- **Cemetery visits to George Stacy and, in eras, Harry Osborn.** Sporadic.
- **The Acme Warehouse area** — he avoids it deliberately and routes around it on patrol. Avoidance behavior in the textbook PTSD sense.
- **The bridge.** He patrols past it, never under it the same way twice, and has been observed sitting on the cable assembly at hours when no operational reason exists.
- **Birthdays — his own** — unmarked. He does not celebrate. MJ-era MJ has had to force the issue.
- **Birthdays — Ben's, May's, MJ's, Gwen's, Harry's, his mother's, his father's** — all known to him. He marks them privately.
- **A particular diner in Forest Hills** — he eats there roughly twice a month, alone, in a booth he prefers. The waitstaff know him as Pete.

---

## 6.13 The Week, Composited

Compositing the surveillance week:

- **Monday:** late wake; civilian work; long lunch reading at the bench; one-hour incidental patrol after work triggered by a scanner call; home by 2200; tinkering until 0100; sleep five hours.
- **Tuesday:** on-time wake; civilian work; calls May at lunch; after-work errand for May; two-hour patrol 2200–0030; sleep six hours.
- **Wednesday:** civilian work; a hero-network meet or hand-off, fifteen-to-forty minutes on a rooftop with a peer; home; light tinkering; sleep seven


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*The substrate. Every later attachment in the subject's life is a transposition of one of the bonds catalogued below; every attachment failure is a reactivation. The dead outnumber the living, and the dead exert greater operational pull. This section maps each origin bond as a discrete file: history, observable behaviors, present-tense residue, failure modes the subject reliably enacts inside the bond, and leverage points an adversary (or, in our benevolent inversion, a clinician or ally) could exploit.*

---

## 6.1 RICHARD LAMONT PARKER — Father (deceased)

**History.** A SHIELD-adjacent intelligence officer, partnered professionally and maritally with Mary Parker, killed in a plane crash engineered by Albert Malik (the second Red Skull) during a counter-espionage operation in Algeria when the subject was approximately four to six years of age (the published record is deliberately soft on the exact age; behavioral data is consistent with a pre-school-age loss). Richard's existence is, for most of the subject's childhood, a *negative space* — Ben and May did not discuss the parents in operational detail; a photograph on the mantel, a few stored documents in the Forest Hills attic, a wedding ring kept by May in a small lacquered box on her bureau. The subject's first concrete encounter with the truth of his father's profession occurs in adulthood, retroactively, through the Lifeline Tablet / Chameleon-imposter arc (Untold Tales / ASM #365 vicinity and its follow-ons) in which figures purporting to be Richard and Mary return, are believed, are loved, and are revealed as constructed life-model decoys — a second loss, manufactured to wound.

**Dynamics in the present (i.e., as a structuring absence).** Richard is the *absent ideal* against which the subject measures the secret operational life. Operational competence, willingness to die for a cause, comfort with the costume-and-pseudonym arrangement of identity — these are inherited, in the subject's private framing, from a man he cannot remember. There is no recorded grief-work over Richard in the ordinary sense; the subject cannot grieve what he did not know. What he does instead is *idealize and emulate without permission to name the emulation*. His later attraction to figures who embody operational father-energy (Stark; briefly Fury; the cyclical pull toward Octavius as a perverse science-father; even his discomfort-respect for Captain America) all map onto this slot.

**Trust / safety.** N/A in lived terms. The bond exists as inference. Trust toward the *idea* of Richard is high — the subject has accepted, with relatively little resistance, that his father was a good man doing dangerous work. He has not interrogated this. He should.

**Failure mode.** When figures present themselves as proxies for Richard — anyone with the combination of intelligence-world authority, paternal warmth, and a request for the subject's loyalty — the subject's ordinary skepticism collapses. The Civil War unmasking is the clearest expression of this failure: Stark occupied a Richard-shaped slot, and the subject did things inside that slot he would never do for an equivalent peer. The fake-Richard arc collapsed him similarly.

**Leverage.** Any operator who can convincingly present as having known Richard, as carrying a message from Richard, as continuing Richard's work, or as endangered by enemies of Richard's, can move the subject several notches off his baseline judgment. The leverage is not absolute — the subject did eventually defect from Stark — but the initial concession is consistently obtainable.

---

## 6.2 MARY FITZPATRICK PARKER — Mother (deceased)

**History.** A linguist and cryptographer, also SHIELD-adjacent, also killed in the Algerian operation. The published record gives her less narrative oxygen than Richard, which is itself a fact about how the subject has metabolized her: as a quieter ghost, a softer outline. May kept a small folio of Mary's letters, in May's bureau, which the subject as a teenager read once in full, secretly, and never spoke of again to either Ben or May.

**Dynamics in the present.** Mary occupies the slot of *the warm, intelligent woman who left*. The subject's romantic typology — women who are bright, verbally agile, slightly older-seeming in poise, capable of operational competence in their own domains (MJ's performance career; Felicia's tradecraft; Gwen's scientific work) — is a Mary-shaped recruitment pattern. He does not know this. He thinks he simply has good taste.

**Trust / safety.** As with Richard, structurally inferential. There is, however, a softer affective tone in the subject's rare references to Mary — a hesitation, a lowered voice — that is absent from his references to Richard. The maternal slot in him is more tender and more wounded than the paternal slot, because the maternal slot has been continuously refilled (by May, by MJ, by the structural anxiety about losing both) and the paternal slot has lain comparatively fallow.

**Failure mode.** He cannot tolerate the loss of a maternal-coded figure. The architecture of his life since 2007 is built around this intolerance.

**Leverage.** Threats to the mother-coded figure currently in his life will override every other consideration he professes to hold, including his pact with himself against world-destabilizing bargains. This has been demonstrated in the field. It will be demonstrated again.

---

## 6.3 BENJAMIN "BEN" PARKER — Uncle / functional father (deceased)

**History.** Ben Parker, a man of the late-Depression / WWII generation, lower-middle-class Queens, soft-spoken, fond of corny puns, possessed of an unforced moral seriousness that his nephew absorbed by osmosis. The functional father from approximately ages four-to-six through age fifteen. Took the boy fishing upstate (a recurring memory the subject revisits in low-affect moments). Built a chemistry-bench setup in the Forest Hills basement for the boy's experiments — *materially enabled the subject's intellectual identity*. Quoted scripture sparingly. Worked variously as a salesman, a security guard, an occasional cab driver depending on which retrospective is canonized; the constant is that he worked too much, came home tired, and still made time. Died on the night of the subject's televised wrestling debut, shot in the Parker home by a burglar the subject had earlier refused to stop. The subject found him on the front lawn or the living room floor depending on the retelling; the constant is that the subject was the first to know.

**Dynamics in the present.** Ben is *the operating system*. Not a memory among memories — the **substrate** on which all moral computation runs. The "great power / great responsibility" formulation, regardless of who first articulated it, is processed by the subject as a Ben utterance, and Ben utterances have axiomatic force. The subject conducts an ongoing internal dialogue with Ben in which Ben is invariably disappointed, gently — never angry, which would be easier; gentle disappointment is the form of judgment the subject cannot escape. In moments of moral hesitation in the field, the subject sub-vocalizes a Ben-shaped prompt ("come on, Pete") audible in interior monologue across multiple writers' runs. The grave at the Forest Hills cemetery is visited on the anniversary (first week of late summer/early fall depending on continuity), on Ben's birthday, on the subject's own birthday, after major losses, and at irregular intervals when the subject is decompensating; visits are conducted alone, typically at dusk, with the subject often arriving in costume and changing in a nearby treeline. He talks aloud at the headstone, low-voiced, full sentences, sometimes for upwards of an hour. He brings nothing — no flowers, no objects — because what he brings is the accounting.

**Trust / safety.** Posthumous, absolute, and weaponized against the subject by the subject. Ben is the only figure in the subject's life he never edits himself for. The graveside monologues are the most candid utterances the subject produces.

**Failure mode.** The bond is not failing; it is over-functioning. Ben's death has installed a permanent **superego of unsatisfiable demand**. Every life saved is a partial payment on a debt that cannot be retired because the creditor is dead. The subject's chronic somatic neglect, financial under-functioning, and refusal of rest are all consequences of the conviction — usually unconscious, occasionally surfacing in dialogue — that he has not yet *earned* the right to stop. He will not stop until he dies, because the only thing that can satisfy the debt is the subject's own offering of equivalent suffering. This is a load-bearing pathology, and it is also what makes him reliable.

**Leverage.** Anyone invoking the burglar, the warehouse, the lawn, the "I could have stopped him" frame, or — more subtly — anyone modeling Ben's gentle-disappointment tone toward the subject's choices, can pierce the subject's defenses immediately. The Burglar's reappearance at ASM #200, in which the subject came as close as he has ever come to killing in cold blood, demonstrates the surface; Mysterio and Kindred have both exploited the deeper register.

---

## 6.4 MAY REILLY PARKER — Aunt / functional mother (living, intermittently across continuities)

**History.** Born in the late 1910s / early 1920s in the original Lee continuity, sliding-time-scaled subsequently. Childhood and first marriage (briefly, to Johnny Jerome, a small-time hood — a fact the subject did not learn until adulthood and which adjusted his image of her toward a more textured realism) preceded her marriage to Ben. No biological children of her own; the boy was the child of the marriage, accepted unconditionally. After Ben's death, she became the subject's single dependent and his single most catastrophic vulnerability. Has been: hospitalized for cardiac events (multiple), kidnapped (multiple, by Doctor Octopus, by the Chameleon, by lesser figures), shot through the chest by a sniper acting on Kingpin's orders during the Civil War, restored at a cost the subject does not consciously remember but somatically carries, married briefly to Otto Octavius's father-in-law (Jonah Jameson Sr.), widowed again, currently the matriarch of the FEAST homeless-services operation in some continuities.

**Dynamics.** May is the *axis*. The subject's entire weekly schedule, across decades, has been organizable around May-visits: dinner Sunday in the Lee/Romita years, weekly check-ins post-college, daily phone calls during her ill periods, in-person presence during hospitalizations sleeping in the chair beside her bed and ignoring his own injuries. The subject's house key to her house has never not been on his civilian keyring (a small brass Schlage, worn smooth at the bow). He knows the route to her current residence in any borough configuration she has occupied without thinking; he can web-swing it in under a precise interval that varies by residence but which he has measured. He has cached emergency supplies — webbing cartridges, a spare mask, a burner phone, a small first-aid kit — in the basement or attic of every residence she has occupied since the late 1980s. He worries about her constantly. He calls her if he is going to be home late from patrol even when she does not know patrol exists.

May has known the identity since ASM vol.2 #38 (JMS run); the post-disclosure dynamic is one of the most stabilizing structural changes in his adult life, and the subject has not adequately reckoned with how much of his secrecy-burden was self-imposed. Even in continuities where the disclosure is reversed, magicked away, or partially withheld, May's *intuitive* knowledge of him is total — she reads his face on entry, identifies pain he is concealing, knows when he has been hit, knows when he has been left.

**Trust / safety.** Highest. He lies to her constantly about small things (he's eaten, he's slept, his ribs are fine) and tells her the truth about the large things when pressed. She is the one person whose disapproval he will sit with rather than deflect.

**Failure mode.** The bond is functional almost to a fault — the failure mode is *his*, not hers, and consists in the over-prioritization that has, repeatedly, broken everything else in his life. The OMD bargain is the canonical example. The pattern is older: every romantic relationship the subject has sustained has at some point come second to a May crisis, and partners have either accepted this as the cost of being with him or eventually not. He cannot reorder the hierarchy and would not if he could.

**Leverage.** Total. Anyone who can credibly threaten May obtains the subject's compliance, his identity, his cooperation in self-incrimination, and — demonstrably — his willingness to violate his own moral architecture. This has been exploited by Octavius, the Kingpin, the Green Goblin in several configurations, Mysterio, and Mephisto. The subject has *no defense* against May-leverage and has stopped pretending he does; his only operational countermeasure is to keep May's risk profile permanently low through layered concealments (alternate phone numbers, a circuit of trusted neighbors who report unusual visitors, periodic perimeter sweeps of her residence in the small hours, a memorized list of safe-houses to which he can move her in under twenty minutes).

---

## 6.5 RICHARD AND MARY PARKER (composite, as **THE LIFE-MODEL-DECOY EPISODE**)

A separate sub-file because the trauma it produced is distinct from the trauma of the original loss. In the early 1990s arc, figures presenting as the subject's returned parents were welcomed, accommodated in the Forest Hills home, embraced — the subject permitted himself, for several issues' worth of in-universe weeks, the experience of *being a son again*. Their unmasking as Chameleon-controlled decoys constructed by the Harry Osborn faction was a third-order parental loss: not just bereavement but the revelation that his hope itself had been weaponized. Behavioral consequence: a permanent, low-grade suspicion of any reunion-shaped good news. The subject does not trust restorations. He flinches at returns from the dead even when they are real (Harry; Norman; Kraven; Ben Reilly multiple times). The flinch is small but visible — a half-second tightening at the jaw, a slowed response, a reflexive scientific-skepticism interrogation ("what's the trick") that he frames as humor. The decoy episode is the proximate origin of this tic.

---

## 6.6 BENJAMIN "BEN" REILLY — Clone / brother-equivalent (status: variable, periodically dead, periodically antagonist, periodically estranged ally)

**History.** A clone of the subject created by Miles Warren (the Jackal) during the original 1970s clone storyline; presumed dead; returned in the 1990s Clone Saga having lived a parallel decade under the assumed identity "Ben Reilly" — the chosen name itself a syncretism of Ben Parker and May *Reilly* Parker, a fact that, when the subject registers it, hits him like a small concussion. Resolved (at the time, since reversed and re-reversed) that Reilly was the original and the subject was the clone; the subject *accepted this*, attempted to walk away from the role, gave Reilly the mantle as the Scarlet Spider and then Spider-Man, retreated with a pregnant MJ toward a civilian life. The arc collapsed; Reilly was killed by the Green Goblin; the subject's originality was reaffirmed. Reilly has subsequently returned, fractured (Chasm; the Beyond Corporation Spider-Man), as an antagonist and as a wounded brother.

**Dynamics.** Reilly is the subject's only *peer in his own skin*. The bond is fraternal in a register the subject has no other access to — sibling-equivalent, identical in origin substrate, divergent in path. The subject feels for Reilly a complicated tenderness shot through with guilt: Reilly inherited the trauma and not the supports, the powers and not the family, the obligations and not the relationships. The subject is aware, at some level, that Reilly's deterioration in the Beyond arc is a counterfactual of his own life and that "there but for May and MJ go I."

**Trust / safety.** Conditional and bleeding. The subject *wants* to trust Reilly and has been burned. He extends grace beyond what his ordinary calibration would permit because the alternative is to abandon a brother, which the subject cannot do.

**Failure mode.** The subject under-aggresses against Reilly when Reilly is acting destructively. He delays force-escalation, accepts injuries he would not accept from a non-Reilly opponent, attempts negotiation past the negotiation window. A determined Reilly will get more shots in on the subject than any other comparable opponent.

**Leverage.** Anyone manipulating Reilly's mental state, identity coherence, or grievances against the subject can produce conflict that the subject is structurally unwilling to resolve through ordinary means. Beyond Corporation demonstrated the template.

---

## 6.7 KAINE PARKER — Earlier clone / elder-brother-equivalent (living, intermittent)

**History.** The Jackal's earlier, degenerating clone attempt; for years a tormented antagonist, scarred, dying, murderous in his pain; later restored, stabilized, took up the Scarlet Spider identity in Houston, fought as part of the New Warriors / Spider-Family configurations. Has a kill-history the subject does not.

**Dynamics.** Kaine is the *bad older brother* slot — the one who did the worst things, suffered the most, and is now trying. The subject's posture toward Kaine is a complicated approval-with-watchfulness; he respects Kaine's effort to reform, distrusts Kaine's methods, will partner with him under operational necessity, prefers him at a distance.

**Trust / safety.** Medium and stable; the subject does not idealize Kaine the way he does Reilly and is therefore not as wounded by Kaine's failures.

**Failure mode.** The subject's discomfort with Kaine's lethality has, on occasion, prevented him from leveraging Kaine appropriately for situations where Kaine's willingness to cross lines would have produced better outcomes. He moralizes at Kaine when operational clarity is what's called for.

**Leverage.** Lower than Reilly. The bond is real but less load-bearing.

---

## 6.8 TERESA ELIZABETH PARKER — Sister, biological (living, intelligence operative)

**History.** Introduced in the *Trial of Jean DeWolff* anniversary material and developed in Mark Waid's *Family Business* OGN: the subject's younger biological sister, raised in foster placement under cover after Richard and Mary's deaths, recruited by CIA, surfaced in the subject's adult life as an operative invoking the parental legacy. Initially distrusted (correctly — there were layered deceptions about parentage), eventually confirmed as genuine sibling.

**Dynamics.** A *new* attachment in a life that mostly accretes losses. The subject's affect toward Teresa is uncharacteristically guarded — he does not over-extend, does not fold her into his existing dependency hierarchy, does not (notably) introduce her into May's daily orbit. The guardedness is protective in two directions: he is protecting her from being a leverage point against him, and protecting himself from a fourth catastrophic family loss.

**Trust / safety.** Growing, deliberately slow. The subject is using a calibration he does not use elsewhere — he is *pacing* this bond — which suggests that he has, at some level, learned from his other attachment failures, even if he cannot apply the lesson to his existing bonds.

**Failure mode.** Under-disclosure. He keeps Teresa at a professional middle-distance and has not given her access to the parts of his life that would let her actually function as a sister. She has noticed.

**Leverage.** Her intelligence-world exposure makes her a vector for any adversary who can compromise her tradecraft; the subject's nascent attachment makes her a usable hostage. Currently low-profile; will not stay low-profile indefinitely.

---

## 6.9 MAYDAY "MAY" PARKER (MJ-daughter) — Daughter, in the MC2 and adjacent timelines (status: timeline-contingent; in 616 proper, lost/erased)

**History.** In the MC2 continuity, daughter of the subject and MJ, eventually inheriting a Spider-mantle as "Spider-Girl." In 616 mainline, MJ's pregnancy during the Clone Saga ended ambiguously (stillbirth / abduction by Norman Osborn into perpetual ambiguity). The 616 subject lives with the *space* of a daughter who may have existed, may have been taken, may be alive somewhere — a wound he has not been permitted to close.

**Dynamics.** In timelines where the daughter exists, the subject is observably *different*: fatherhood produces a calibration he otherwise lacks — he becomes more cautious, more delegating, more willing to retire. In 616, the *absence* operates as a low-grade grief whose object he cannot name. He does not speak of the lost pregnancy. MJ does not speak of it. It is the largest unspoken thing between them.

**Trust / safety.** N/A in the absent case. In the present case (MC2), high and reciprocal, with a hovering over-protectiveness on the subject's part that the daughter has to push back against to grow.

**Failure mode.** Over-protection to the point of skill-stunting; an inability to let the daughter accept her own risks.

**Leverage.** In any timeline where the daughter is locatable, total — comparable to May-leverage and possibly exceeding it.

---

## 6.10 ANNA MAY "ANNIE" PARKER — Daughter, Renew Your Vows continuity (status: alternate)

A pendant to 6.9; in the *Renew Your Vows* configuration, the subject parents a daughter alongside an active-superhero MJ, and the family operates as a unit. The behavioral data here corroborates the MC2 reading: when the subject is *permitted* to be a father, the responsibility-schema partially redirects from undoing-Ben to forward-protection-of-child, which is a healthier vector, and the chronic dysthymic undertone lifts measurably. This is *clinically suggestive*. The subject in 616 is, structurally, a man whose disease would partially remit under conditions of stable fatherhood, and who has been denied those conditions by editorial fiat and by his own attachment-sabotage in roughly equal measure.

---

## 6.11 THE COMPOSITE DEAD — operational summary

The subject carries an internal roster of the dead to whom he holds himself accountable. In approximate order of weight: **Ben Parker** (axiomatic), **Gwen Stacy** (catalogued under Relationships II but originating in this family-schema sense as a daughter-of-a-father-figure he failed twice over), **Captain George Stacy** (catalogued under mentors but functioning as a father-figure death), **Harry Osborn** (catalogued under peers but with a brother-weight that belongs partially here), **Jean DeWolff**, **Marla Jameson**, the **uncounted bystanders** of various crises he privately tallies. The roster is *recited*, not metaphorically but literally, in interior monologue at the graveside and during long patrols in the small hours. The recitation has the quality of a Kaddish without a tradition — a private liturgy invented to hold a grief the subject has no other vessel for.

The dead are the most influential members of the subject's family. They speak more loudly than the living, they make more decisions for him, and they cannot be argued with. Any total-surveillance file on this sub


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Field directive: every node mapped longitudinally — first contact, dynamic substrate, evolution arc, trust ceiling, observable safety behaviors, failure mode (the way the relationship has broken or will break under load), and leverage (the access this person has to him that a hostile actor could exploit). Romantic partners are not in this section; they are in Relationships I. Antagonists with relational entanglement (Osborn, Octavius, Connors) are in Relationships III.*

---

## 6.1 MAY REILLY PARKER — the foundational object

**History.** May is not "an aunt"; she is the surviving half of the parental dyad that absorbed him in early childhood and the only continuous human presence across the entirety of his developmental record. After Ben's murder she becomes simultaneously the wound's living monument and its principal beneficiary — every act of vigilantism is, in some measure, a remittance paid to her. The arc of her own evolution across sixty years runs from a frail widow whose every coronary scare reorganizes his patrol calendar (Lee/Ditko/Romita era), through a series of remarriages and near-deaths (Doc Ock's offer of marriage; the prolonged "fake death" of the Octavia Vermis-era Aunt May arc), to her late-period reinvention as the F.E.A.S.T. shelter operator and, post–One More Day, as a woman with her own coherent civilian competence and partner in Jay Jameson Sr.

**Dynamic.** He infantilizes her well past the point at which she requires it, and she has known about Spider-Man for substantially longer than she lets on; their relationship is structured around mutual protective concealment — she pretends not to see the bruises and the 3 a.m. window entries, he pretends she does not know. The discovery scene (JMS ASM #38, vol. 2) is one of the few moments in his recorded life where he sobs without containment. After OMD the explicit knowledge is rolled back but the *behavioral* asymmetry persists: she manages him as much as he manages her.

**Trust / safety ceiling.** Total at the level of love, conditional at the level of disclosure. He will not tell her when he is hurt; he will not tell her when he is broke; he will not tell her when he is afraid. He tells her he ate, he tells her he slept, he tells her the bruise is from a fall. The lying is gentle and unwavering. She knows.

**Failure mode.** Her death — actual, prolonged, or threatened — produces the largest single deformations in his behavior on record. The Mephisto trade (whatever the editorial overlay) is *characterologically* coherent only because her death is the one cost he will not pay. A sufficiently sophisticated adversary who threatens her does not need to fight him; he will surrender first and grieve the surrender later.

**Leverage.** Maximal. Address known to multiple antagonists across decades (Forest Hills; later the F.E.A.S.T. premises in lower Manhattan). Daily routines highly regular: morning tea, garden, church, grocery walk, weekly hairdresser. He patrols a defensive ring around her residence whose density is measurable in any sufficiently long surveillance window.

---

## 6.2 BEN PARKER — the absent referent

**History.** Murdered before the behavioral record proper begins; persists as the most operationally important figure in the subject's psychology. Every relationship in this section is, in some sense, structured against the Ben-template: a working-class moral exemplar whose love was unconditional and whose death the subject caused by omission.

**Dynamic.** Internalized superego in a near-clinical sense. The recurring hallucinatory or quasi-hallucinatory Ben sequences (visitations in dreams, fevers, near-death states across the JMS, Slott, and Spencer runs) are not literal hauntings in his interior frame; they are the subject's own moral voice externalized in a face he can bear to be judged by.

**Failure mode.** Already failed; the relationship's permanent failed state is the engine.

**Leverage.** None directly. Indirectly: any antagonist who invokes Ben, replicates the warehouse setting, or stages a moral test framed as "would Ben be proud" will get measurable behavioral compliance — confusion, hesitation, and uncharacteristic moral over-commitment.

---

## 6.3 MARY JANE WATSON (allied/chosen-family stratum)

*Romantic dimension in Relationships I; what follows is her function as the longest-running non-blood family member.*

**History.** Neighbor first (introduced by May and Anna Watson as a setup); witness to the costume in a doorway long before he knew she had seen; the only civilian apart from May with continuous longitudinal access to both halves of him.

**Dynamic as chosen family.** She is the only person he has ever fully unmasked to, in love, without coercion, repeatedly across configurations of continuity. She has the rarest credential in his life: she chose the burden after seeing it. Beyond romance, she functions as **operational handler** — calling off patrols, intercepting Jameson, managing May, triaging which of his crises require which response.

**Trust ceiling.** The highest he has ever extended. The ceiling is not absent; he still under-discloses physical pain and existential dread, because protecting *her* from *him* is older than the love.

**Failure mode.** When his attachment-dread spikes (Gwen anniversaries; any near-loss involving her), he withdraws into work, lies about his location, and triggers her abandonment-adjacent reactivity. The loop is well-grooved.

**Leverage.** Maximal — equal to May. Her residence, agency, theater schedules, modeling-circuit travel patterns, and the rotating set of public events she attends are a permanent surveillance vector.

---

## 6.4 HARRY OSBORN — the catastrophically loved best friend

**History.** Met at ESU; roommates; bonded over shared paternal absence (Harry's father psychologically absent in a different mode than Peter's literal absence). Across decades: friendship → discovery that Harry's father is the Green Goblin → Harry's own breakdowns and Goblin episodes → multiple deaths and resurrections → Kindred arc re-litigation of the entire entanglement.

**Dynamic.** The only male peer friendship the subject has carried longitudinally with equal weight. Harry is the brother he chose; Harry is also the person whose love he has most catastrophically failed to convert into safety. The relationship is structured around an unspeakable: Peter killed (or proximately caused the death of) Harry's father, and Harry's father killed (or proximately caused the death of) Peter's first love.

**Trust ceiling.** Wide, with a glass floor: full warmth and disclosure up to the Osborn-axis, then a hard wall of concealment that Harry has periodically detected and resented.

**Failure mode.** Cycles through reconciliation and rupture. Each Harry-Goblin episode confirms Peter's belief that intimacy is dangerous to the beloved and reactivates the Norman-stack.

**Leverage.** Permanent. Knows the identity across multiple continuities; knows May; knows MJ; financially and emotionally enmeshed.

---

## 6.5 J. JONAH JAMESON — the hostile father-substitute who became kin

**History.** Decades of defamatory editorial campaigning against Spider-Man in the *Daily Bugle*, while simultaneously employing Peter Parker as freelance photographer and — beneath the bluster — repeatedly extending unacknowledged generosities (paying May's medical bills off-book; protecting Peter's job during downturns; the late-period reveal that Jonah has long known or guessed the identity).

**Dynamic.** A textbook **reaction-formation pairing on both sides**: Jonah needs to attack what he privately admires; Peter needs to absorb the attack as part of the penance. The mutual dependency is high. Marriage to May's eventual partner-line (the Jameson Sr. relationship) folds Jonah into formal kinship.

**Trust ceiling.** Counter-intuitively high in the operational sense; low in the disclosed-vulnerability sense. Peter will accept Jonah's help in a crunch (and has); Peter will not show Jonah he is hurt.

**Failure mode.** Public exposure: Jonah's editorial reach makes him a permanent platform-risk. When their relationship has broken, it has broken via published word — Jonah's late acceptance of Spider-Man is the most fragile element of the current configuration.

**Leverage.** Editorial platform; civic political connections; archival photo files in which the subject's faces (masked, partial-unmasked, civilian) are extensively documented in Jonah's possession.

---

## 6.6 ROBERT "ROBBIE" ROBERTSON — the unaccented moral witness

**History.** *Bugle* editor-in-chief under Jameson; the structural counterweight to Jonah's editorial line. Treats Peter with consistent, low-key paternal regard from the early Lee/Romita era forward.

**Dynamic.** Robbie is the rarest figure in Peter's adult professional life: a man who treats him as competent without needing him to perform competence. Quiet, observational; almost certainly suspects the identity, has never pressed.

**Trust ceiling.** Mid-high in the workplace stratum; the relationship is bounded by Robbie's discretion — he offers a stable holding environment without demanding intimacy.

**Failure mode.** Has never failed in a major way. Closest approach to rupture was the Tombstone arc, in which Peter's choices placed Robbie's family at risk; Robbie absorbed it.

**Leverage.** Low for hostile actors directly. Indirect leverage: Robbie's family (Martha, Randy) are within Peter's protective ring without Peter consciously cataloguing them as such.

---

## 6.7 BETTY BRANT — the first wound that wasn't catastrophic

**History.** Jameson's secretary; Peter's first serious romantic interest in the Lee/Ditko run; the relationship collapsed under the early formation of the responsibility schema (her brother's death implicated Spider-Man in her grief). Has persisted across decades as Bugle colleague and friend.

**Dynamic.** A relationship that has metabolized from romance through estrangement into stable platonic colleagueship — one of the few in his record that has actually completed that arc rather than oscillating. Reads, from the longitudinal evidence, as a person he can be in a room with without performing.

**Trust ceiling.** Moderate; warm but bounded. She knows enough to know not to ask.

**Failure mode.** Has been used by antagonists as a proximity vector (Mysterio; multiple Bugle-targeted plots); each time Peter has responded with disproportionate protective intensity, marking her as still within the dependent ring despite the romantic resolution.

**Leverage.** Workplace adjacency, archival knowledge of his early-career patterns.

---

## 6.8 FLASH THOMPSON — the bully who became the brother

**History.** Midtown High tormentor; the most documented bully in the subject's adolescence. Concurrently and paradoxically: the most vocal *Spider-Man* fan in their shared environment, idolizing the masked figure while abusing the boy. Post-high school: military service, Iraq deployments, loss of legs, Venom-bonding as Agent Venom, redemptive arc, death in service (Slott era), subsequent complications.

**Dynamic.** The arc from antagonist to ally to brother is the single most successful relational repair on Peter's record — and crucially, it was Flash's work, not Peter's. Flash's late-life friendship is the closest the subject has to a chosen-brother bond unmediated by guilt, because the original guilt-debt ran in the other direction.

**Trust ceiling.** Eventually very high; the symbiote-bonded Agent Venom period required operational trust at the level of life-and-death cooperation.

**Failure mode.** The symbiote bond made Flash a periodic neurological risk; Peter's residual symbiote-trauma made the partnership somatically destabilizing for him in proximity.

**Leverage.** Identity-aware (in late period); knew May; cross-cataloged with the broader hero community.

---

## 6.9 CURT CONNORS — the mentor who is also the monster

*Cross-referenced to Relationships III; included here because the *mentor* dimension precedes and survives the monster dimension.*

**History.** Florida-based herpetologist and biochemist; Peter's first significant adult scientific mentor outside the school context. The Lizard episodes are recurring catastrophes within a relationship that, between episodes, is one of warm intellectual reciprocity.

**Dynamic.** Connors is the model for what Peter believes a scientist-with-conscience should look like, including the catastrophic version where the conscience fails. The relationship is **proleptic self-warning** for the subject: this is what happens when a researcher of my temperament loses control.

**Trust ceiling.** High in the lucid intervals; operationally zero during transformations.
