**Failure mode.** The Lizard. Periodic, structural, unsolvable.

**Leverage.** Identity partially known across various continuities; scientific correspondence trail.

---

## 6.10 OTTO OCTAVIUS — the inversion mentor

*Primary placement Relationships III; the mentorship axis flagged here because, post-Superior, Octavius occupies a unique pseudo-allied stratum.*

**Dynamic in the allied register.** Having occupied Peter's body and lived his life, Octavius possesses a quality of insight into the subject available to no one else alive — including the somatic specifics, the fatigue patterns, the relational ledger. The post-Superior configuration in which Octavius operates as occasional reluctant ally produces a relationship with no clean analog: neither friend nor enemy nor mentor nor protégé, but something like a *shared-occupation veteran*.

**Leverage.** Maximal informational; he has *been* the subject from the inside.

---

## 6.11 MILES MORALES — the protégé who completed the Ben loop

**History.** Inherited the mantle in an adjacent reality; brought into the primary continuity post-Secret Wars; ongoing mentorship relationship across the past decade of publication.

**Dynamic.** Miles is the single most consequential reparative relationship on the subject's record. By becoming, for Miles, a version of what Ben was for him — present, principled, available, fallibly loving — the subject is able to occupy the Ben-position rather than only the bereaved-nephew position. This is *the* observable mechanism of psychological repair in the longitudinal record. The mentoring is meticulous: he shows up to graduations, he calls before patrols in Brooklyn jurisdictionally, he defers to Miles' parents, he does not micromanage.

**Trust ceiling.** Very high. Identity-mutual; family-aware on both sides (Jefferson and Rio Morales, Ganke Lee).

**Failure mode.** Peter's tendency to martyrdom and his under-disclosure of his own state can shade into a protective paternalism that Miles has periodically — correctly — pushed back on.

**Leverage.** Both directions; symmetric.

---

## 6.12 ANYA CORAZON, GWEN STACY (variant), CINDY MOON, JULIA CARPENTER, JESSICA DREW — the Spider-Family

**Composite entry** because the relationships share a structural signature: each is a person who came to the spider-totem stratum from a different vector and to whom the subject extends a senior-sibling or mentor function with varying intensity.

- **Jessica Drew:** longest peer-bond in this set; cross-Avengers operational trust; the friendship has weathered Skrull-impersonation trauma and her own multiple identity disruptions. The least condescended-to of his juniors; treated as full equal.
- **Anya Corazón:** the most explicit mentee in the urban-vigilante register; mentored at the operational street-level where his expertise is densest.
- **Silk (Cindy Moon):** complicated by the bite-shared origin and the involuntary pheromonal attraction; the subject has visibly worked to keep that confound from contaminating the mentor function. Notable for the discipline.
- **Spider-Gwen (variant):** the cross-reality version of the dead beloved; he handles her with a tenderness whose source he has not articulated and likely will not.
- **Julia Carpenter:** later Madame Web; the relationship inverts in late period as she becomes the seer and he the supplicant.

**Trust / failure / leverage** across the set: the Spider-Family is his most successful chosen-kin formation. Failure mode is dispersion (geographic and continuity) and his tendency to take on coordinating responsibility he cannot sustain. Leverage: collective is high — anyone who can compromise one of them can pull him into the field.

---

## 6.13 BEN REILLY — the brother who was him

**History.** The clone, by various retcons either his genetic duplicate or some adjacent ontological category; lived as Peter during the Clone Saga interval; subsequent independent existences, deaths, returns, and corruptions (Jackal arc; Beyond era).

**Dynamic.** The relationship interrogates the question that no one else in his life can ask: *if I am replaceable, am I obligated?* Ben's existence destabilizes the responsibility schema by demonstrating that the role can be occupied by someone else — which the subject, against expectation, found *grief-inducing rather than relieving*. The grief reveals that the burden has become identity, not duty.

**Trust ceiling.** Variable and historically catastrophic. Peaks at brother-love; troughs at active opposition during Ben's corrupted intervals.

**Failure mode.** Ben's recurring instability under the weight of being a contingent copy.

**Leverage.** Total identity-mirroring; biometric defeat of every system Peter relies on for compartmentalization.

---

## 6.14 JOHNNY STORM — the friend who lets him be light

**History.** Bonded across the FF / Spider-Man crossovers from the Lee era forward; the friendship is one of the oldest peer-bonds in his record and one of the few that operates principally in a register of *play*.

**Dynamic.** Johnny is the friend with whom the subject is most able to be unguardedly silly. The friendship's function is recreational-affective rather than confessional; they joke, they prank, they fly. This is a structurally important relationship precisely because it is *not* heavy.

**Trust ceiling.** High in operational and recreational registers; mid in the confessional. They do not, by long-standing tacit agreement, discuss the dead.

**Failure mode.** Johnny's own grief surges (Sue, Reed, the Inhumans-period losses) put him in states where Peter, the better-equipped griever, becomes structural caregiver — a load Peter accepts and Johnny periodically resents.

**Leverage.** Identity-aware; cross-rostered; family-adjacent (the Storms have been periodic refuges).

---

## 6.15 REED RICHARDS — the scientific superego

**History.** From the earliest issues; recurring scientific consultations across decades, including substrate work on the Spider-Sense, the symbiote biology, and the post-Superior somatic recalibrations.

**Dynamic.** Reed is the only person Peter consistently defers to scientifically. The relationship is *one-directional in admiration* and *two-directional in respect* — Reed regards Peter as one of the under-credentialed minds whose ground-level practical chemistry exceeds many of his own academic collaborators. The deference is partly genuine, partly a structural avoidance of the comparison Peter is afraid of losing.

**Trust ceiling.** High in technical disclosure; low in personal. He brings Reed problems; he does not bring Reed himself.

**Failure mode.** Reed's tendency toward cosmic-scale prioritization periodically leaves Peter feeling like a low-priority ticket; Peter under-asks for help as a result.

**Leverage.** Technical archives; biological samples on file; the FF infrastructure.

---

## 6.16 MATT MURDOCK — the rooftop confessor

**History.** Cross-borough peer; the working-vigilante friendship of equals across decades. Murdock has been one of the very few people to whom the subject has disclosed identity *in the field, voluntarily, under no compulsion*, sometime in the Bendis-era continuity (subsequently variously remembered).

**Dynamic.** The Catholic moral-architectural overlay Murdock brings is structurally legible to Peter's own scrupulosity. They confess to each other in the discursive sense — about kills they didn't prevent, lines they almost crossed. The rooftop conversation is a recurring set-piece.

**Trust ceiling.** High in the moral-disclosure register, where it is uniquely high; mid-low operationally because Murdock's jurisdictional instincts are different.

**Failure mode.** Murdock's periodic descents into self-destructive war (Shadowland; the Kingpin cycles) load Peter with concern-without-traction.

**Leverage.** Legal counsel, identity-aware, sensorially capable of recognizing Peter through any disguise — a permanent unspoofable observer.

---

## 6.17 STEVE ROGERS — the moral north star without paternal warmth

**History.** Avengers tenure; Civil War antagonism; reconciliation; subsequent collaborative service.

**Dynamic.** Rogers is the figure against whom Peter calibrates his moral compass at scale — *what would Cap do here* is an internal heuristic across decades. The personal warmth is moderate; the moral debt is high. The Civil War rupture and its repair is the most consequential adult moral-political relationship in his record, in part because Peter chose Stark first and was wrong, and Rogers received him back without recrimination.

**Trust ceiling.** High operationally; mid-personally; Peter does not bring his civilian self into Rogers' field.

**Failure mode.** When Rogers has been compromised (Hydra-Cap; cosmic-cube events), Peter's compass loses calibration and he over-improvises.

**Leverage.** Avengers infrastructure; cross-team identity awareness.

---

## 6.18 TONY STARK — the paternal transference disaster

**History.** Late-period mentorship beginning in the New Avengers / Civil War era; Iron Spider suit; the unmasking; the betrayal-and-reconciliation arc; subsequent intermittent Parker Industries scaffolding.

**Dynamic.** The most psychologically consequential adult mentorship in his record *because it failed*. The subject — who had carried the Ben-debt for decades without a living paternal substitute he could trust — accepted Stark's surrogate-father bid, against the consistent advice of his closer attachments, and the cost was catastrophic. The unmasking decision is the single most-out-of-character act on the longitudinal record, and the diagnostic reading is unambiguous: he wanted, briefly, to be a son. The aftermath is the most punishing self-recrimination cycle on file outside the Gwen and Ben events.

**Trust ceiling.** Permanently capped post-Civil War. The warmth has returned in places; the disclosure has not.

**Failure mode.** Already detonated; the relationship now operates with a permanent thermal scar.

**Leverage.** Stark Industries has biometric and genetic data; the Iron Spider architecture lives in archives.

---

## 6.19 WONG, STRANGE, MADAME W


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Per-subject dossier entries. Each entry maps origin, dynamic, evolution, the subject's felt safety in proximity, the subject's characteristic failure mode opposite that person, and the leverage the relationship grants either party. Compiled from longitudinal observation of the subject's behavioral record across the entire span. Listed in three blocks: ENEMIES (criminal antagonists with persistent psychological purchase), RIVALS (peers, press, professional and ethical antagonists), LOVERS / INTIMATES (women with full romantic/sexual entanglement to the subject; non-romantic intimates handled in Relationships I/II).*

---

## I. ENEMIES

### Norman Osborn — the original recurring antagonist; the un-Ben

**History.** Father of Peter's first college best friend (Harry). Industrial-chemist patriarch; ingestion of his own performance formula produces the Goblin persona — a paranoid, predatory, sadistic alternate state with full memory access to Norman's planning faculties. First learns Spider-Man's civilian identity in the late Lee/Romita period; thereafter the antagonist of record. Murders Gwen Stacy by throwing her from the Brooklyn (then George Washington, depending on the reprint) Bridge. Faked his own death for years; returned in the late 90s; thereafter has been intermittently dead, alive, in power, in disgrace, and (in the modern era) periodically scrubbed of the Goblin state by intervention.

**Dynamic.** Norman is the only antagonist who genuinely terrifies the subject. The terror has three load-bearing components. First, *prior knowledge* — Norman knew the face under the mask before any other recurring enemy, which permanently disorganized the subject's compartmentalization architecture and installed a chronic dread that anyone he loves can be reached. Second, *paternal-figure inversion* — Norman occupied a quasi-mentor position in Peter's early adulthood through Harry, and his predation feels, to the subject, like the corruption of the very category that Ben occupied. Third, *Gwen* — Norman is the person who proved, by direct demonstration, that Peter's worst self-narrative (closeness kills) is operationally true. Every subsequent Osborn encounter routes affect through that proof.

**Evolution.** Early period: Norman as urgent kinetic threat with identity-leverage. Middle period (post-resurrection): Norman as systemic threat — money, political influence, Dark Reign, public legitimacy — forcing the subject into a defensive posture in which Norman is *more credentialed than he is*, a posture the subject's class-shame finds especially galling. Late period: the Kindred arc and the "sin-eating" sub-arcs partially exorcise Norman's Goblin, leaving the subject with the unbearable problem of a Norman who is sympathetic and lucid and still walking around with Gwen's blood on his life ledger. Subject cannot resolve this and oscillates between guarded civility and panic.

**Trust/safety.** Zero. The subject's spider-sense behaves anomalously around Norman across the record — sometimes suppressed by Osborn pheromonal/chemical exploit, sometimes spiking pre-emptively. Subject will not be in an enclosed room with Norman if it can be avoided; if it cannot, posture micro-pattern shifts to keep an exit corridor and one hand free.

**Failure mode.** Against Norman the subject loses humor first. Patter rate drops to near-zero. He becomes flat, lethal-adjacent, and has on three documented occasions come within a restraint-decision of killing. The Norman fights are where the no-kill line is closest to the surface; he holds it, but the holding costs are visible in the days afterward (withdrawal, sleep collapse, irritability with intimates).

**Leverage.** Norman holds knowledge of identity and of every intimate. The subject holds an asymmetric understanding of Norman's psyche — he reads Norman's tells (the Goblin laugh's pre-onset breath catch, the specific micro-tic in the left eyelid when the formula is metabolizing) better than Norman reads his own. In standoffs the subject has used this for de-escalation; he has never used it for predation, and Norman knows it, which Norman experiences as contempt.

---

### Otto Octavius — the antagonist who became, briefly, the self

**History.** Atomic scientist, mechanical-arm prosthesis fused to spine via accident; first encountered when Peter is still in high school and is, notably, the *first opponent Peter loses to outright*. The defeat is formative: Peter contemplates quitting, May's faith in "Spider-Man" pulls him back, he wins the rematch. Decades of recurring conflict follow — kidnappings of May (including a literal engagement to May in a notorious 70s sequence), villain-team leadership, terminal-illness arcs, and ultimately the body-swap in which Otto inhabits Peter's body while Peter dies in Otto's, with Peter's final act being the upload of his memory-set into Otto, producing the Superior period.

**Dynamic.** Of all enemies, Otto is the one Peter most *understands from the inside*. They share a structural similarity — both are bullied physics prodigies whose accidents fused them to apparatus they cannot easily remove — and the subject knows it. Pity for Otto is a stable feature of the dynamic and a vulnerability Otto has exploited. The body-occupation event added a layer no other enemy has: Otto experienced being Peter, and Peter experienced being a witness to Otto-as-Peter, and both came away changed. Post-Superior, the subject's posture toward Otto includes a strand of involuntary collegiality that the subject finds shameful and cannot extinguish.

**Trust/safety.** Conditional and rising over time. The subject would not turn his back on Otto with civilians in the room, but in two-party tactical situations against larger threats has accepted Otto as a temporary asset. The trust is granted reluctantly and re-evaluated continuously.

**Failure mode.** Against Otto the subject talks too much — uses humor not just defensively but pedagogically, as if trying to teach Otto something. This slows him down and has cost him fights. Conversely, Otto's failure mode against Peter is exactly symmetric: long monologues in which Otto explains the moral architecture of his current scheme, betraying the same need to be understood by Peter that Peter has to teach him.

**Leverage.** Otto retains nervous-system-level intimacy with the subject's body — knows its limits, recovery curves, the specific neuromechanical signatures of the spider-sense — from the Superior period. The subject retains a corresponding intimacy with Otto's internal monologue, having lived inside it as observer. Each is, uniquely, the other's most informed witness. Neither has fully deployed this; both could.

---

### The Burglar — the unnamed origin

**History.** Petty thief Peter declined to stop at the television studio; subsequently the killer of Ben Parker. Returned canonically in the 200th-issue arc, revealed to have targeted the Parker home in pursuit of money rumored hidden there. Died of cardiac event during the confrontation, Peter looming over him in costume.

**Dynamic.** Not a relationship in the conventional sense — a *figure* in the subject's interior topology. The Burglar is the locus of the originating moral wound and the subject has spent six decades constructing a moral architecture whose foundation stone is the refusal to ever again be the man who let the Burglar pass. Every petty thief the subject apprehends mid-flight is, structurally, a re-litigation.

**Failure mode.** Subject has, on the record, allowed fleeing offenders of a specific somatic profile (medium build, ball-cap, duffel) to occupy a disproportionate slice of attention during multi-incident nights — the silhouette is a trigger. He overcommits to the chase.

**Leverage.** The Burglar is dead; the leverage is internal and total. Any antagonist who can place the subject in a "you are about to repeat the AF#15 omission" frame gets a free emotional move.

---

### Kraven (Sergei Kravinoff) — the antagonist who buried him

**History.** Big-game hunter; ritualized obsession with hunting "the spider." Late-80s sequence: drugs Peter, shoots him with what Peter believes is a fatal bullet, buries him for approximately two weeks in a grave on the Kravinoff estate, then assumes the Spider-Man identity to "prove" his superiority by hunting and brutalizing a worse predator (Vermin) in the costume. Peter digs out of his own grave. Kraven, believing himself to have at last bested the spider, kills himself. The Grim Hunt arc decades later resurrects the family; Sasha, Ana, Alyosha, the recurring revenge cycle.

**Dynamic.** Kraven is the antagonist who inflicted the subject's single most concentrated trauma. Unlike the loss antagonists (Norman, the Burglar), Kraven attacked the subject's *body and identity* directly — burial is the most intimate violation in the record. The subject does not speak of it. Reference to graves, soil, coffins, or being underground produces observable autonomic response (jaw clench, breath-rate elevation) decades on. Kraven, in death, became uniquely *respected* by the subject in a way no other enemy is — Kraven was a man of internal coherence, and the subject, who lacks it, registers that.

**Trust/safety.** The original Kraven dead is "safe" in the only sense the subject finds tolerable. The Kravinoff descendants are not. The subject will not enter wooded or rural terrain without elevated vigilance — a behavioral residue.

**Failure mode.** Against Kraven-pattern antagonists the subject's humor breaks down differently than against Norman: not into flatness but into a brittle, accelerated patter that signals dissociative onset. Combat-effective but personally costly; the post-fight crash is severe.

**Leverage.** Kraven (the original) understood the subject as prey — meaning he had a model of the subject's *body* better than most enemies. That model was transmitted to the family. The subject has no symmetric leverage on the Kravinoff line; they are functionally opaque to him.

---

### Eddie Brock / Venom — the dark mirror with a grudge

**History.** Journalist defamed in part by the subject's correction of Brock's false serial-killer scoop; bonds with the discarded symbiote, which carries grievance and identity-knowledge from its time on Peter. Multi-decade antagonist; intermittent uneasy ally; periodic anti-hero phases; in modern continuity a quasi-cosmic figure.

**Dynamic.** Eddie is the antagonist who hates Peter for *being good at the role Peter himself hates being*. He envies Peter's moral standing and resents the very humility that produces it. The subject reads this clearly and finds it sad. The symbiote's residual intimacy with the subject's biology means Eddie/Venom can negate the spider-sense on contact — a tactical asymmetry that has cost the subject dearly across multiple encounters.

**Trust/safety.** Negative in early decades, rising to grudging conditional in later periods. The subject can work with Eddie in a crisis but treats every interaction as a single-iteration prisoner's dilemma.

**Failure mode.** Subject under-uses humor against Eddie (Eddie does not destabilize from it; he rage-amplifies) and over-uses lateral problem-solving (the sonic/thermal exploits, which Eddie has long since adapted to). The encounters tend to extract a disproportionate caloric and somatic cost.

**Leverage.** Eddie/Venom holds the spider-sense exemption and identity knowledge. The subject holds the moral high ground, which Eddie cannot revoke and which functions, in Eddie's psyche, as a kind of perpetual irritant the subject has occasionally used to talk Eddie down.

---

### Cletus Kasady / Carnage — the antagonist who does not negotiate

**History.** Serial killer pre-symbiote; bonded to symbiote offspring; recurring slaughter-events that have forced the subject into rare alliances with Venom and other heavies.

**Dynamic.** Carnage is the enemy against whom the subject's signature mode (humor, restraint, attempted understanding) is least useful and most dangerous. Carnage is not damaged in a way that yields to compassion; the subject's reflex to look for the salvageable kernel becomes, against him, a tactical liability. The subject knows this and still cannot fully suppress the reflex. The encounters consistently end with the subject having allowed Carnage to inflict more harm than was strictly necessary because of an extra beat spent looking for an opening that wasn't there.

**Trust/safety.** Zero, with no upward trajectory.

**Failure mode.** The subject's no-kill line is, against Carnage, the most expensive line he holds. He pays the cost willingly and quietly, and the cost compounds.

**Leverage.** Carnage holds chaos; the subject holds nothing in return except containment. This is the most asymmetric leverage relationship in the file and it grinds on him.

---

### Curt Connors / Lizard — the friend who is also the enemy

**History.** Mentor-figure scientist; surgical amputee whose self-experiment with reptile-DNA regeneration produces the Lizard, a reactive saurian alter that has, across decades, killed civilians, eaten the Connors family in one notorious arc, and required Peter to physically restrain and chemically reverse him repeatedly.

**Dynamic.** Connors is *Peter's most-similar professional peer* in his civilian life — a working scientist with a family and an ethical practice. Peter loves him. The Lizard is therefore an antagonist Peter cannot fight without grieving in real time. The dynamic is structurally close to the Otto dynamic but with the unbearable addition that *Connors is innocent of the Lizard's acts in a way Otto is not innocent of Octavius's*.

**Trust/safety.** Toward Connors: high. Toward the Lizard: zero, with the further complication that the spider-sense rates the Lizard variably depending on the current cognitive substrate (full feral Lizard reads cleanly; Connors-bleed-through Lizard does not).

**Failure mode.** Against the Lizard the subject pulls punches. This has been documented across decades and is one of the most consistent tactical liabilities in the file. He will accept injury rather than risk killing the man inside.

**Leverage.** Connors knows the subject's identity; the subject knows Connors's chemistry. Bilateral, symmetric, never weaponized.

---

### Flint Marko / Sandman — the antagonist the subject most successfully redeemed

**History.** Career criminal, particulate-state mutation, longtime member of various Sinister assemblages, periodic Avengers-roster guest, recurrent backslider.

**Dynamic.** The subject's reaction-formation tendency finds its most productive object in Marko. He sees Marko as a man whose moral architecture is reachable, and across decades he has — patiently, without fanfare — invested in Marko's better state. Marko has betrayed this investment several times; Peter has resumed it each time without ostentation.

**Trust/safety.** Moderate and conditional; correctly calibrated. Subject does not over-trust Marko but does not under-trust him either; one of the more accurate trust calibrations in the file.

**Failure mode.** When Marko reverts the subject takes it personally in a way he does not take, e.g., Octavius's reversions. The grief is quiet but real.

**Leverage.** None deployed in either direction. The relationship is, by enemy standards, mutually respectful.

---

### Wilson Fisk / Kingpin — the institutional enemy

**History.** Organized-crime titan; periodically legitimate (Mayor of New York in the modern era); a structural rather than personal antagonist.

**Dynamic.** Fisk is the antagonist who exposes the subject's class wound. Fisk is *credentialed, monied, institutionally powerful*, and the subject is none of those things; their conflicts foreground every Peter-Parker insecurity about being a working-class freelancer in a city run by money. Fisk has not, historically, prioritized the subject as a personal enemy, which the subject experiences with a complicated mixture of relief and insult.

**Trust/safety.** Zero, but predictable. Fisk plays by gangster rules, which are at least rules.

**Failure mode.** Against Fisk the subject over-relies on costumed-vigilante tools against an enemy whose real weapons are legal, financial, and political. He loses these contests when they move off the rooftop.

**Leverage.** Fisk has institutional reach into the subject's civilian life (employers, landlords, contracts). The subject has the capacity to make Fisk's nights physically unpleasant. Each tolerates the other's leverage as a cost of doing business in the same city.

---

### Mysterio (Quentin Beck and successors) — the antagonist of unreality

**History.** Special-effects technician turned illusion-criminal; recurrent across all eras; one terminal-illness arc with Daredevil; one notorious post-suicide reanimation.

**Dynamic.** Mysterio attacks the subject's *epistemics*. The subject relies heavily on his spider-sense and his rapid pattern-recognition; Mysterio is constructed to poison both. The subject responds with disproportionate cognitive effort against Mysterio relative to the physical threat, and this has, across decades, been a useful self-diagnostic — when Peter is mentally fatigued, Mysterio fights are when it shows.

**Trust/safety.** Zero; Mysterio's specific harm is to make safety unverifiable.

**Failure mode.** Subject over-trusts his own senses against Mysterio precisely when he should under-trust them. He has learned, very slowly, to ground-truth by touch and by deliberately ignoring his eyes.

**Leverage.** Mysterio has the capacity to make the subject doubt his perceptions; the subject has the capacity to talk a Mysterio into self-undoing by exploiting the showman's compulsion to monologue the trick. Each is leverage the other has internalized.

---

### Felicia Hardy / Black Cat — categorized here as antagonist-adjacent rather than lover, with the lover-aspect handled in section III for completeness

*See entry below in LOVERS.*

---

### Harry Osborn — the friend who became the enemy who became the friend

**History.** College roommate and dearest male friend of the subject's adult life; second-generation Goblin during periods of psychiatric decompensation; recurringly dead and alive; in the modern era the locus of the Kindred arc — the revelation that a fragment of Harry, distorted by the Mephisto bargain's metaphysical fallout, has been a long-running antagonist.

**Dynamic.** The most painful relationship in the entire file. Harry is simultaneously the subject's longest peer-intimacy, the son of the man who killed Gwen, and the antagonist whose enmity is least metabolizable because it is *grievance-based and accurate*: Harry's grievances against Peter are, in their distorted way, founded on real Peter-failures. The subject cannot fight Harry without conceding that Harry is partly right.

**Trust/safety.** In stable Harry periods: among the highest in the file. In unstable Harry periods: a unique category of dread, distinct from the Norman-dread, because the subject's love is not negotiable.

**Failure mode.** Subject cannot bring himself to incapacitate Harry decisively; he buys time, talks, absorbs damage. This has cost the subject and Harry both. The Kindred arc forced a partial reckoning that has not stabilized.

**Leverage.** Harry holds total identity-knowledge, total intimate-knowledge, and the moral leverage of legitimate grievance. The subject holds the leverage of having genuinely loved Harry without instrumental purpose, a fact Harry's better self knows and his worse self cannot bear.

---

## II. RIVALS

### J. Jonah Jameson — the antagonist who pays him

**History.** Publisher of the *Daily Bugle*; constructed the public anti-Spider-Man narrative single-handedly across decades; also the man whose paychecks have sustained the subject through repeated periods of insolvency. Later thaws: learns the identity in modern continuity, processes it badly, processes it better, becomes one of the most peculiar quasi-allies in the file. Brief term as Mayor.

**Dynamic.** This is the subject's most successful reaction-formation. He saves Jameson from kidnapping, framing, and assassination with a regularity that is statistically improbable and emotionally legible: Jameson is a surrogate father whose disapproval the subject works to earn the disapproval *and* the rescue of. The relationship has the structural shape of an unresolved father-son dynamic in which neither party can quite say what is happening.

**Trust/safety.** Civilian Peter: warm, irritable, surprisingly safe — Jameson respects Peter the photographer in a gruff way that the subject finds quietly nourishing. Spider-Man: complicated and, in modern continuity, partly resolved.

**Failure mode.** Subject under-charges Jameson for photos, accepts editorial abuse he would not accept from any other employer, and protects Jameson's reputation from his own worse impulses. The whole pattern is a tell.

**Leverage.** Jameson holds public narrative and a paycheck. The subject holds — and Jameson, post-revelation, knows it — a moral standing Jameson can neither match nor diminish.

---

### Tony Stark — the rival as misplaced father-transference

**History.** Mentor-sponsor in the Registration period; the figure to whom the subject unmasked publicly; the figure whose institutional architecture the subject defected from when its consequences became clear; the figure whose model the subject tried to imitate during the Parker Industries period and failed to inhabit.

**Dynamic.** Stark occupies a category the subject is uniquely vulnerable to — *successful, paternal, institutionally legitimate, brilliant*. Peter's pre-existing father-hunger routed onto Stark with catastrophic results during Civil War. The subject has, in the years since, learned to keep Stark at arm's length; the learning was expensive.

**Trust/safety.** Pre-Civil War: dangerously high. Post-Civil War: appropriately calibrated. The subject now respects Stark, works with him competently, and does not let Stark do his moral reasoning for him.

**Failure mode.** When tired or grieving the subject still drifts toward seeking Stark's approval; he catches himself with increasing speed.

**Leverage.** Stark holds resources and a model of adulthood the subject is not allowed to want. The subject holds a moral steadiness Stark covets. Neither weaponizes this; both feel it.

---

### Reed Richards — the rival as intellectual ceiling

**History.** Longstanding peer; periodic collaborator; occasional FF roster member during MJ-marriage period; reliable resource for high-physics consultation.

**Dynamic.** Reed is the figure against whom the subject benchmarks his own intelligence and finds himself wanting in a way he does not actually mind. The rivalry is one-sided and friendly: Reed treats Peter as a true peer, and Peter accepts this without bitterness, which is one of the subject's healthier interpersonal accomplishments.

**Trust/safety.** High. Re


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

*Capability inventory for SUBJECT: PARKER, P.B. Mechanism, envelope, longitudinal drift, and — where the record permits — the symptom-as-signature reading: i.e., how each capability is shaped by, and in turn re-inscribes, the underlying psychological architecture documented in the prior workup.*

---

## 1. THE MUTAGENIC PACKAGE — BASELINE PHYSIOLOGY

### 1.1 Strength

**Mechanism.** Wholesale rewrite of myofibrillar protein density, mitochondrial volume fraction, sarcomeric organization, and tendon/ligament tensile properties; corresponding cortical-bone remodeling that allows the skeleton to transmit the forces the musculature can now generate without snapping under its own output. The mutation is *internally consistent* — strength alone, without skeletal and connective-tissue upgrade, would be self-destructive; the record shows no spontaneous fractures under maximum effort, indicating the upgrade is system-wide.

**Envelope.** Pressing limit canonically scales in the ~10-ton range in baseline depictions, with documented excursions well above this under affective load (the Master Planner sequence; lifting a collapsing daily-bugle building; the bridge-shift in Kraven aftermath; multiple "impossible weight" scenes across decades). The excursions are not noise — they are a stable pattern: **strength output is affect-modulated**, with grief, terror-for-a-dependent, and refusal-to-die functioning as endocrine accelerants that recruit reserve capacity normally inaccessible. He does not train into these excursions; he is *driven* into them.

**Granular usage tells.** He pulls punches by default to a degree that no other heavy-hitter in his cohort matches. Door-handles, handshakes, hugs, and shoulder-pats are calibrated; the calibration occasionally fails under fatigue (crushed coffee mugs, snapped pencils, the bent-doorknob gag that recurs across writers). When fighting an unpowered human he hits at a small fraction of capacity; when fighting a peer-class threat he ramps incrementally; he reserves true output for moments where a dependent is at immediate risk. The escalation curve is *moral*, not tactical.

**Limit.** Sustained output above mid-envelope generates rapid glycogen depletion (see Metabolism, §1.5); the strength is enormous but not endurant under load. He cannot, e.g., bench-press an obstacle for twenty minutes; he can lift it for the seconds required to extract someone, and then he is shaking.

### 1.2 Speed, Reflex, Agility

**Mechanism.** Reflex latencies in the sub-50-ms range — well below the ~150-ms human floor — achieved through both peripheral nerve myelination upgrade and a reorganization of cortical predictive-coding loops that integrates with the spider-sense (§1.4). Footspeed is augmented but not the operational marvel; the marvel is *acceleration*, change-of-direction, and air-time orientation. Vestibular and proprioceptive resolution allow continuous, gyroscopically-accurate body-state knowledge through any rotation.

**Envelope.** Standing-jump multi-story; horizontal broad-jump cross-street; can track and intercept bullets at conversational distance under reasonable lighting; can perceive and respond to threats faster than he can consciously narrate them (the canonical depiction of body moving while inner monologue is mid-sentence).

**Tell.** He fidgets at rest. The augmented nervous system is metabolically expensive to keep "idle" — sustained stillness produces micro-movements (finger-tap, foot-bounce, balance-shifts on the balls of the feet). Surveillance from across a coffee shop would catch this in seconds.

### 1.3 Equilibrioception and Adhesion

**Mechanism.** Integumentary microstructures on palms, fingers, soles — and, with concentration, across larger skin surfaces — engaging van der Waals adhesion against any surface with adequate molecular smoothness. Adhesion is **gated by conscious modulation**: he does not stick to everything he touches, or sitting down would be a problem. The default is "off"; "on" is recruited.

**Envelope.** Vertical glass, ceiling traverse, single-finger hangs from overhead I-beams sustained for hours. Defeated by surfaces too rough at the relevant scale (ablative or heavily-oiled materials), by extreme cold (suspected: lipid-layer crystallization), and by certain engineered "anti-Spider" coatings deployed by Osborn and Roxxon-tier antagonists.

**Tell — universally diagnostic.** He sits oddly. The crouch on furniture — heels-on-seat, knees-up, weight on the balls of the feet — is not affectation; it is the resting posture of a body that is calibrated to spring. He does it on chairs in interrogation rooms, on his own couch, on the edge of rooftops, on the rim of a bathtub. He also does it under stress without noticing. The crouch is the single most reliable identifier in any covert surveillance pull.

### 1.4 Spider-Sense

**Mechanism.** The least classically physiological of the package and the most behaviorally consequential. Best modeled as an *augmented predictive-coding module* — a precognitive proprioceptive faculty that integrates ambient sensory data (peripheral visual flow, infrasonic and ultrasonic pressure, electromagnetic disturbance, possibly something more exotic on the totemic reading) and surfaces threat-relevant prediction errors as a localized occipital/cranial *tingle* with directional vectoring. The signal is qualitative (intensity, urgency, vague direction) rather than propositional ("threat behind, projectile, 0.4s"); the body acts on it before the conscious mind decodes it.

**Envelope.** Reliable at conversational-to-room range for human and most projectile threats; degrades with distance and with threats that do not fit the implicit threat-classifier (it has historically struggled with: Venom and other symbiote-spawn — *because the symbiote read his physiology and exploits the blind spot*; close family and intimate partners under certain conditions; threats Peter has emotionally decided are not threats; sufficiently impersonal mechanical hazards). It can be **overloaded** — too many simultaneous threats produce a featureless roar he cannot vector against. It can be **suppressed** by sufficiently exotic frequencies (Goblin tech; Scorpion-tier targeted countermeasures). It can be **temporarily lost** entirely — a documented vulnerability that, every time it has occurred (Sins Past aftermath, post-Superior recovery, etc.), has produced near-fatal outcomes within hours, because *the rest of his combat doctrine assumes its presence*.

**Symptom-as-signature reading.** The spider-sense is hypervigilance instantiated as biology. He was hypervigilant *before* — a bullied, anxious-attached, parent-loss kid who scanned rooms — and the mutation gave him a sensory organ that confirms and rewards the scanning. The neurological augmentation and the psychiatric trait are now welded; you cannot treat the PTSD hyperarousal without effectively asking him to ignore a sensory channel. This is one of the more cruel ironies in the case file: **the upgrade locked in the wound.**

### 1.5 Metabolism, Healing, Resistance

**Caloric demand.** Approximately 3–5× sedentary human baseline at rest; spikes massively during operation. Diet is consequently voluminous and indiscriminate — convenience food, late-night halal carts, the canonical hot-dog vendor, cold pizza. The chronic financial precarity collides with the caloric demand to produce *episodic intake collapse* under cash-stress, which directly degrades strength, reflex, and healing — a feedback loop he refuses to name. (Surveillance correlate: he eats while walking, eats while reading, eats while sitting on rooftops; he is rarely *not* eating when at rest.)

**Healing.** Lacerations close in hours; bruises resolve overnight; non-displaced fractures in two-to-four days; concussion symptoms (subjective) clear in 24–48 hours, with the open question of cumulative neurological cost that the mutation cannot fully neutralize. He uses this regenerative envelope as **license to underprotect himself**: because he can absorb damage that would hospitalize a normal operator, he does, and the cost is paid in chronic low-grade somatic load and in the somatic dissociation noted in the medical section.

**Toxin/pathogen resistance.** Broad-spectrum but not absolute. Vulnerable to engineered agents (Goblin formula derivatives, certain Lizard-saliva compounds, ethyl-chloride family at very high doses — historically how Smythe and others have sedated him).

### 1.6 Sensory Augmentation

Visual acuity, color discrimination, contrast sensitivity, low-light performance, and auditory range all uprated. He has not worn corrective lenses since the bite; the glasses in early appearances are now plain glass when he wears them as Peter, kept for **persona maintenance** — a deliberate disguise element that doubles as a cognitive Anchor (the lenses are a costume for *Peter*, signaling to the world the deficient civilian-self he constructs as cover). The choice is psychologically loaded: he keeps a prop of his pre-mutation weakness within reach at all times.

---

## 2. EXOGENOUS AND ACQUIRED EXTENSIONS

### 2.1 The Web-Shooters

**The single most diagnostic artifact in the case file.** The mutagenic event made him strong, fast, adhesive, and precognitive. It did *not* make him a webslinger. The webs are a 17-year-old's weekend chemistry project, built in a Forest Hills basement with high-school equipment and a parts budget measured in stolen lab supplies and Aunt May's grocery money.

**Mechanism.** Twin wrist-mounted mechanical injectors driving a polymeric fluid through a pressurized nozzle; the fluid cures on shear/air contact into a tensile-strong, time-decaying filament (~1 hour, by design, to avoid leaving a city festooned in his trash). Trigger is a double-tap of the middle and ring fingers against a palm-plate — a deliberate ergonomic choice that prevents accidental discharge during a closed fist or an open palm-strike. Cartridges are modular, swappable in seconds, carried on belt-loops sewn inside the costume.

**Envelope.** Single-shot line distances on the order of 60+ feet under good conditions; can be modulated for stream (combat restraint), spray (area denial / smoke-displacement), net (capture), pellet (impact projectile), and the swing-line itself — a continuously-cured filament under tension capable of supporting his full body-mass plus a rescue load. He has, over decades, expanded the formulary: insulator variants for electrical threats, accelerant-resistant for thermal threats, dissolving for evidence-friendly captures, ice-web during one mutational period, taser-web in the Iron Spider/Stark-tech era, and various specialty munitions he engineers ad-hoc for specific opponents.

**Limits.** *Cartridges run out.* This is the single most exploited limitation across his entire combat history; every competent recurring antagonist eventually learns to extend a fight past his ammunition envelope. He carries spares; he runs out anyway, because cash. The fluid is chemically unstable in extreme cold (a documented failure mode), is jammable by certain particulate contaminants, and the shooters themselves are mechanically vulnerable — a precision impact to the wrist disables him in a way no impact to his body can.

**Growth over time.** The 60-year arc of the shooters tracks his arc as an engineer. The teenager's hand-machined units are still the conceptual ancestor of every subsequent iteration; even when Stark-tech, Parker Industries-tech, or post-Superior optimization has overlaid the design, he reverts to the wrist-mounted mechanical configuration whenever resources collapse. The reversion is significant: **he refuses to be a hero who is only operative when wealthy.** The mechanical shooters are an identity-bearing artifact — they prove that the work was his, not the spider's.

**Symptom-as-signature reading.** The web-shooters are sublimation in physical form. The grief over Ben, the rage at his own pre-bite uselessness, the intellectualization habit, the perfectionism — all of it precipitated, in the immediate aftermath of the bite, as a compulsion to *build the missing capability*. He was given a power-set and his first response was to engineer a power-set extension. This is not normal. Most subjects in the wider meta-human record accept their package and operate within it. He *augmented* his on day one because the package alone did not satisfy whatever the bite had unlocked in him. The shooters are the load-bearing evidence that the mission predates the abilities; the abilities are conscripted into a mission he was already, at some preconscious level, ready to wage.

### 2.2 The Organic-Webbing Interval

During the JMS totemic arcs, an emergent endocrine/glandular alteration produced organic web-shooting from wrist spinnerets and a set of retractable tarsal stingers. The interval was brief in operational time and partially reverted. Behavioral data from the period: **he was visibly uncomfortable with the organic shooters in a way he never was with the mechanical ones.** The discomfort reads as identity-encroachment; the mechanical shooters were *his* contribution to the partnership with the spider, and the organic version effectively annexed that contribution into the mutation. He never developed the same fluency with the organic version. He preferred the tool over the gland. This is consistent across writers and is itself diagnostic.

### 2.3 Costuming and Hardware

**The costume.** A subject of more design iteration than the public record acknowledges. The basic two-color suit is itself an engineering artifact: tightly-knit synthetic with lensed one-way eyepieces (correcting for the diffuse light-collection of his uprated retinas while preventing forensic eye-color identification), reinforced soles allowing toe-grip without abrading the adhesive microstructures, and internal webbing-cartridge mounts. Every variant — the black symbiote-derived design, the Stark-tech Iron Spider with its waldoes, the stealth suits, the various Parker Industries iterations, and the perpetual reversions to the red-and-blue — has been *self-tailored* in baseline conditions. He sews. The sewing is in the record; it is one of his only domestic skills, and it derives from May's instruction in the pre-bite years. (Surveillance correlate: characteristic small calluses on the left thumb pad; pricked-finger micro-injuries that the healing factor erases within hours but that are observable in the moments after.)

**The Stark-tech and Parker Industries periods** demonstrated that he *can* operate as a high-resource hero — drone-assist, HUD, waldo-arms, encrypted comms — and that he *will* return to scrap-built minimalism the moment the institutional support collapses. The pattern is not preference; it is the same class/identity rigidity noted earlier. He doesn't trust hardware he can't repair on a tenement kitchen table at 3 a.m.

---

## 3. SKILL STACK — TRAINED, NOT GIFTED

The mutation provided physiology. *Every* operational competence beyond physiology was acquired, mostly autodidactically, mostly under combat duress.

### 3.1 Combat

**Style.** No formal martial-arts lineage in the foundational years; the early combat record is improvisational gymnastics overlaid on raw strength, with the spider-sense providing the defense and the webs providing the standoff. Across decades he has accrued ad-hoc training from peers (Captain America at minimum; Shang-Chi in at least one documented stretch; sparring across Avengers tenures) but has never fully discarded the improvisational base. His characteristic combat signature is *environmental* — he fights *with the room*, using surfaces, beams, awnings, fire-escapes, traffic, opponent-momentum, and his own swing arcs as primary weapons; direct striking is a last resort.

**Restraint.** Of the heavy-hitter cohort, he is among the most consistently restrained. Killing-line holds across 60 years against every provocation, including the immediate aftermath of the deaths of Ben, Gwen, Captain Stacy, Harry, Kraven-entrapment, and multiple May near-deaths. The restraint is not pacifism — he hits hard and damages opponents — it is a categorical refusal that he himself has identified as load-bearing for his moral architecture (see prior workup, §5). Operationally this also functions as a force-multiplier: opponents who know he will not kill are willing to engage him at closer range, which his reflexes and webs convert into rapid neutralization. The ethic and the tactic align.

**Patter.** The combat-quip is a real combat tool, not flavoring. It serves three concurrent functions: (i) **affect regulation** — keeps his own arousal in the operational window by externalizing it; (ii) **opponent destabilization** — degrades the opponent's tactical focus by demanding linguistic processing; (iii) **bystander reassurance** — civilians who hear jokes panic less. The patter density tracks inversely with felt safety: the more frightened or grief-loaded the fight, the faster the jokes. A surveillance transcript correlating jokes-per-minute against contextual threat would be a near-perfect inverse plot. He does not know he is doing this. Or, more precisely: he knows, and uses it deliberately, *and* the underlying drive is not under conscious control.

### 3.2 Engineering and Science

Doctorate-equivalent competence across multiple domains — biochemistry (the web fluid, his own physiology), physics (the shooters, swing-dynamics, various improvised tools), materials science, electrical engineering, and an autodidact's mastery of whatever subdiscipline a current threat requires. Documented capacity to reverse-engineer Octavius-tier and Stark-tier hardware under time pressure. The Parker Industries arc demonstrated genuine top-tier industrial-R&D capability; the collapse of Parker Industries was not a capability failure but an identity one.

**The signature application** is *rapid prototyping under deadline of life-or-death*. He does his best engineering work in the four hours before a fight he expects to barely survive. The pattern matches the strength-under-affect pattern in §1.1 — capability is recruited maximally only under existential pressure for a dependent. In ordinary R&D conditions he is excellent; in crisis conditions he is generational.

### 3.3 Photography

Self-trained; functional enough to sell to a major metropolitan tabloid for decades. The technical competence is real but secondary; the trick is *access* — he is the only person who can photograph Spider-Man from Spider-Man's vantage. The career is a sublimation-coded survival hustle: monetizing the identity-secrecy problem itself.

### 3.4 Mentorship

A late-emergent competence (post-Civil War, accelerating through Spider-Verse and the Miles Morales relationship). He is, against every prediction his self-concept would generate, a *good* teacher — patient, technically clear, emotionally attuned to the apprentice's age-appropriate fears. The competence derives from his having been the apprentice nobody had; he gives what he would have wanted. This is reparative in the clinical sense and is one of the genuinely protective factors in his risk profile.

---

## 4. ENVELOPE LIMITS — THE FULL CATALOGUE

**Ammunition.** Webs run out. Recurring. Exploited by every competent enemy.

**Caloric.** Sustained operation past ~24 hours degrades all physiological capabilities; past ~48 hours produces measurable cognitive impairment that the spider-sense partially compensates for and partially makes worse (more signal he cannot process).

**Sleep.** Chronically undersupplied (see medical workup). The spider-sense degrades first; reflex degrades second; strength degrades last but most dangerously, because he doesn't *notice* its degradation until a calibrated pulled-punch turns out to be miscalibrated.

**Cold.** Adhesion degrades; web-fluid degrades; healing factor appears to slow.

**Ultrasonic and certain electromagnetic frequencies.** Symbiote-bonding aftermath left residual sensitivity; certain Goblin-class and Roxxon-class countermeasures exploit this.

**Spider-sense blind spots.** Symbiote-spawn (Venom, Carnage); intimates under specific conditions; threats he has emotionally classified as non-threats. The blind spots are *psychologically* shaped, not just biologically — which is why they have proven so consistent across writers.

**Identity-knowing antagonists.** Every operational envelope contracts when an enemy knows where May lives. This is not a power-limit; it is a *strategic* limit that effectively converts every fight into a hostage scenario. The Civil War unmasking was, in capability terms, the worst tactical decision of his career.

**Moral self-binding.** He will not kill, will not let civilians be collateral, will not abandon a rescue to pursue an objective. Every one of these constraints has been exploited by enemies who arrange forced-choice scenarios. He always takes the rescue. They know this.

---

## 5. LONGITUDINAL DRIFT

Over 60 years of operational record, the capabilities have not so much grown as **refined**. Raw envelope (strength, speed, reflex) has been broadly stable since the late-teenage stabilization of the mutation; the JMS-era totemic upgrades added the organic shooters and stingers transiently and broadened the conceptual frame, but operational baseline returned. The *skill stack* has grown substantially — combat refinement, engineering, mentorship, situational judgment — and the *self-management* of the capability set has become marginally better with age (less wasted motion, fewer telegraphed strikes, more efficient swing routing, better triage of which fights to take).

The post-Superior recovery is the only period where one can plausibly read a step-change in operational doctrine: a measurable increase in delegation, in pre-fight reconnaissance, in willingness to ask peers for backup. Octavius's tenure in the body left a residue of strategic discipline that the original would not have developed on his own. He has not acknowledged this in any documented internal monologue.

---

## 6. SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE — THE INTEGRATED READING

The capability set, taken whole, is a near-perfect physical externalization of the psychological structure documented in §§3–4 of the prior workup.

- **Strength** that scales with affective load for a dependent is the responsibility schema given biology.
- **Spider-sense** is hypervigilance given a sensory organ — the wound and the gift welded.
- **Adhesion** keeps him able to perch above and watch — the surveillance posture of the anxious-attached caregiver, biologized.
- **The web-shooters** are sublimation in metal and polymer — the engineered proof that the mission predated the powers.
- **The patter** is humor-as-defense (Vaillant mature) instantiated as combat doctrine.
- **The no-kill line** is the moral architecture that keeps the rest of the system from collapsing, weaponized as a tactical constraint.
- **The reversion to scrap-built tech** after every period of high-resource operation is the class/


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# 6. OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

*How the subject actually conducts business, day-to-day and crisis-to-crisis, across sixty years of observable operations in the five boroughs and beyond. This section maps mechanism, not motive — what he does with his hands, his money, his time, his network, and his name.*

---

## 6.1 Decision Architecture

**Triage hierarchy under load.** The subject operates a remarkably stable, deeply internalized triage stack that has held across writers and decades. In descending priority, in any acute scenario, his observed allocation order is: (1) civilians in immediate kinetic danger — falling, burning, drowning, in the line of fire; (2) civilians in proximate danger of becoming the above; (3) named dependents (May, MJ historically, the resident Spider-Family juniors, and on occasion specific neighbors and tenants whose welfare he has informally adopted); (4) peer heroes who are visibly compromised; (5) the actual antagonist objective. The antagonist is *fourth or fifth*, never first. This produces a recurring tactical signature: he will abandon a winning engagement to catch a falling air conditioner. Sophisticated adversaries (Octavius, Osborn, Kingpin) have learned this and weaponize it — the diversionary civilian-endangerment gambit is a standard move against him, and he falls for it every time, knowingly, because the alternative would be to revise the schema.

**OODA tempo.** Observation-Orientation-Decision-Action loop runs at a tempo well below human baseline, due to (a) the precognitive proprioceptive sense compressing the Observation phase, (b) overlearned threat-response patterning from decades of repetition, and (c) a cognitive style that converges quickly and revises mid-action. He is comfortable making a decision wrong-and-fast and recovering, rather than right-and-late. In non-combat decisions — relational, financial, career — this same fast-revise pattern produces *impulsive commitments followed by elaborate guilt-driven repair work*. The pattern is the same engine running in two domains.

**Where he stalls.** Decisions that require him to accept help, request resources, or place his own welfare in another's hands. These produce observable latency: he will spend three days webbing across the city looking for a chemistry workaround rather than place a single call to Reed Richards or Tony Stark, despite both standing offers. This is not pride; it is the responsibility schema enforcing self-sufficiency as a moral category.

**Pre-mortem absence.** He rarely scenarios out failure modes in advance. He scenarios out *configurations of the present problem* (he is a brilliant tactical chemist) but does not run extended forecasts on second-order consequences of his own actions. The Civil War unmasking is the most catastrophic example; the Parker Industries arc is the second; the symbiote adoption is the third. The deficit is consistent: he optimizes the proximate problem and discovers the systemic consequence afterward.

---

## 6.2 Tradecraft: Costume, Concealment, Movement

**Identity discipline.** Outside of the publicly-known intervals (Civil War unmask, the Mephisto retcon restoring secrecy, and various local in-universe knowledge events), his baseline concealment protocol is functional but improvisational. He does not maintain a formal cover legend in the espionage sense; he relies on (a) the mask, (b) voice modulation toward a higher and faster register when in costume, (c) an entirely different posture and gait — Spider-Man slouches almost never and Peter slouches almost always — and (d) a behavioral firewall between domains: Spider-Man does not mention Parker's address; Parker does not photograph what Spider-Man does not want photographed, except when monetizing himself to Jameson, which is itself a tradecraft inversion (hiding in plain sight by being the photographer-of-record).

**Costume kit, baseline configuration.**
- Primary suit: a one-piece full-coverage textile-and-elastomer composite, hand-fabricated in early eras and progressively upgraded; lenses are one-way reflective with polarized inserts of his own design.
- Web-shooter assemblies: dual wrist-mounted cartridge dispensers using his proprietary web fluid — a shear-thinning polymer that solidifies on extrusion, dissolves on its own roughly one hour later (a deliberate design choice to prevent leaving permanent obstructions and bodies of evidence). Cartridge capacity is finite and a perennial logistical constraint; he reloads in the field by feel, eyes closed if necessary, in roughly two seconds per cartridge.
- Belt: spare cartridges, the spider-signal projector (a small high-lumen device, used more for intimidation/illumination than for any operational signaling), a small first-aid pouch in later eras, a phone in a sealed pocket.
- Backup civilian clothes: stashed in pre-positioned caches on rooftops across Manhattan and Queens — a behavior that began ad hoc and ossified into a network of dozens of small drop sites (air-handler housings, disused water tanks, a few obliging gargoyles). He maps these mentally; the map has never been written down.

**Suit variants in rotation across eras:** the stealth/spider-armor variants (Big Time, etc.) for specific operational tempos; the symbiote-derived black suit and its cloth replica (kept for sentimental and tactical reasons); the Iron Spider variant (returned/abandoned post-Civil War); various Parker Industries upgrades subsequently retired. He retains an irrational sentimental attachment to the original red-and-blue configuration and reverts to it whenever life destabilizes, which functions as a tell: a Peter who has gone back to the classic suit is a Peter who is regrouping.

**Movement profile.** Primary mobility is webswinging — pendular kinetics exploiting building geometry. His preferred swing corridors are well-mapped in his own head; he knows which Midtown buildings have anchor points at what heights and which Brooklyn blocks have the gaps he can clear. He prefers altitude (his hypervigilance abates somewhat above the fortieth floor; rooftops are where he thinks). When stealth is required, he wallcrawls in shadow, exploiting the human eye's neglect of vertical surfaces. Ground-level pursuit on foot is avoided where possible; he is comparatively exposed there. He does not use public transit in costume; out of costume, he uses the subway constantly and has the MTA map metabolized.

**Counter-surveillance behaviors.** Habitual rooftop check on approach to and departure from his apartment — a circling overflight that has been consistent for decades. Enters and exits residences via window roughly as often as via door; uses the door when he expects to be observed by neighbors, the window otherwise. Periodically sweeps his apartment for surveillance devices using improvised RF detection equipment he built himself. Does not name names on phone calls; refers to MJ as "my friend" and May as "my aunt" in any conversation that might be overheard, regardless of how harmless the conversation.

---

## 6.3 The Workshop, the Web, the Camera

**Chemistry and fabrication.** The web fluid is the load-bearing piece of his entire operational kit and is, by any reasonable standard, an extraordinary piece of polymer chemistry that he produced as a fifteen-year-old over a weekend and has iteratively improved across decades. He synthesizes batches at home, using kitchen-grade glassware and reagents sourced from university-supply catalogs and occasional borrowed lab time. Batch yield varies; he runs out at inconvenient moments, which is a recurring operational vulnerability and a stable plot driver. He has experimented with variant formulations — impact webs, web-grenades, fire-retardant variants, the taser-web — and maintains a mental library of which formulation is in which cartridge by color-coded marking on the cartridge base.

**Engineering signature.** His builds are *elegant but visibly hand-made*: hand-wound coils, slightly asymmetric solder, components clearly scavenged. He prototypes rapidly and discards aggressively. He keeps no formal lab notebook (a serious operational vulnerability and an OCPD-trait *absence* — he should, by personality, keep one, and the fact that he doesn't is evidence that the work is partially compulsive rather than fully methodical). Schematics live in his head and on the backs of envelopes, pizza boxes, and the occasional photo contact sheet.

**The camera.** A Nikon-class 35mm body in early eras, progressively upgraded; in modern eras a DSLR and a phone. He has rigged remote-triggered camera mounts on rooftops at predicted engagement zones — a technique he developed within a year of starting at the Bugle and refined into a small subspecialty. The cameras are mounted with web, retrieved by web, and triggered by a wrist-mounted remote or by motion sensors he built. The technique is, ironically, a piece of self-surveillance: he is the only superhuman who has continuously documented his own operations for resale, and the resulting image archive — in the Bugle's morgue, in his own files, in Robbie Robertson's drawer — constitutes the most complete photographic record of any costumed operator in the city. He is profoundly ambivalent about this archive.

---

## 6.4 Combat Doctrine

**Engagement preferences.** He prefers (1) maximum verticality, (2) maximum environmental clutter, (3) maximum standoff distance during opening exchanges. He opens with reconnaissance — a swing-by, a webbed surveillance perch, a perimeter sweep — and engages only after he has identified civilian positions, exits, and at least two escape routes for himself. Against unknown opponents he opens conservatively, probing with webs and short closures, escalating only after he has a read on their capability. Against known opponents he opens with patter — partly to confirm psychological state, partly to seed misdirection, partly because the patter regulates his own arousal.

**The patter as tradecraft.** It is not incidental. The verbal stream serves four operational functions: (a) destabilization of opponents whose self-image is dignified (Octavius, Vulture, Mysterio, Osborn — all visibly degraded by it); (b) location-disclosure inducement (a goaded enemy reveals position by responding); (c) civilian reassurance (the watching crowd hears it and downregulates panic); (d) self-regulation (the steady production of speech evidences and enforces continued cognitive control under fear). When the patter *stops* mid-engagement, it is the single most reliable behavioral indicator that he has either (i) entered a state of fully focused crisis processing or (ii) been emotionally cut by something said back to him. Allies who have fought alongside him for years know to watch for the silence.

**Force calibration.** He pulls his punches as a default. The mutation gives him a strike capacity that would kill an ordinary human at full extension; he has calibrated, by long practice, a graduated scale of restraint, and he operates in the bottom third of it against humans and the middle against superhumans. Against opponents he knows to be at his durability tier (Rhino, Juggernaut, the Hulk on bad days), he ramps to upper-band; he has *never*, in the canonical record, used full output against a living target. The discipline is so internalized that he applies it even in extremis — the recurring observation that he could end fights faster by hitting harder, but doesn't, is a feature, not a bug.

**Spider-sense integration.** He fights in a low-visual mode, with the cranial threat-sense doing much of the targeting; he can fight blindfolded and has. This allows the gaze to track civilians and environmental hazards while the body handles the antagonist. The technique fails against opponents who, for one reason or another, do not trigger the sense (Venom historically; certain telepathic interferences; opponents he loves). Each such failure has produced significant injury.

**Web-craft as battlefield engineering.** He uses webs not primarily as restraints but as battlefield geometry: handholds, swing anchors, deflection surfaces, opacity screens, parachute canopies, slings, splints, stretchers. He builds ad hoc structures mid-fight — a hammock to catch a falling civilian, a net to redirect a thrown vehicle — at a tempo that observers consistently underestimate. The web-line itself is also a sensing tool: vibrations carry along it and he reads them.

**Lethality posture.** Hard no on killing. The line is held under all observable pressure, including pressures (Kraven, Goblin, the murder of Gwen) that would crack most operators. The discipline is doctrinal and self-protective in roughly equal measure — see the psychiatric synthesis.

---

## 6.5 Finances, Infrastructure, Material Conditions

**Income, longitudinal.** Stably precarious. Across decades the canonical income streams have been (1) freelance photography sold to the Daily Bugle / Front Line / various successors, paid per-image with minimal benefits; (2) episodic scientific work — adjunct teaching at Midtown High, research positions at Horizon Labs, the brief and disastrous Parker Industries CEO interval, occasional consulting; (3) intermittent web-fluid licensing and adjacent IP that he has *systematically failed to monetize* despite multiple plausible paths. The Parker Industries period demonstrated that he is fully capable of operating a global biotech firm; the collapse was at least partly self-engineered, consistent with the class/identity rigidity noted earlier.

**Expenditures.** Rent (chronically late), web-fluid reagents (a meaningful line item; he has on occasion shoplifted reagents in extremis and repaid the supplier later, anonymously), camera equipment, food (calorie-driven, cheap), and an ongoing low-grade subsidy of Aunt May (concealed from her). He does not own a car. He owns one suit (civilian) at any given time, replaced when destroyed. He does not vacation.

**Banking and records.** Standard consumer banking under his legal name; no offshore arrangements; no shell entities for Spider-Man-adjacent expenses, which has historically meant Spider-Man's operational costs are paid out of Parker's personal checking — a striking failure of compartmentalization that any competent intelligence opponent could exploit by financial-pattern analysis. Sophisticated enemies have done so (the Kingpin's financial-intelligence apparatus, on more than one occasion).

**Infrastructure.**
- *Residence:* a rotating series of small apartments in Manhattan and Queens; window access prioritized over square footage; high floors preferred; he has, on multiple occasions, declined a better apartment because its window orientation was operationally inferior.
- *Workshop:* a portion of whatever apartment he lives in, ad-hoc, with reagents stored alarmingly close to food. During the Horizon and Parker Industries periods he had real lab access and visibly thrived; the regression to apartment-chemistry after those periods is itself a tell about his comfort with self-deprivation.
- *Caches:* the rooftop drop-sites already noted; a small storage unit in Queens registered under a slight name variant containing legacy costumes, photographs, and ephemera he cannot bring himself to destroy.
- *Communications:* phone in a sealed costume pocket; an Avengers/Future Foundation comm card he carries but uses reluctantly; a small set of burner numbers for hero-peer contacts.

---

## 6.6 Network and Liaison

**Civilian intelligence sources.** A surprisingly dense informal HUMINT network for an operator who runs no formal one: cab drivers, hot-dog vendors, doormen, beat cops who like him, ER nurses at three specific hospitals, a fence in Hell's Kitchen he turned years ago and now treats as a tipster, several reformed minor villains, the Bugle's police-beat reporters, the Bugle's morgue archivist. He does not pay for information; he barters in favors, in saves, in small attentions. The network is held together by his memory — he remembers their kids' names, their illnesses, their schedules — and by a baseline of decency that they reciprocate.

**Hero-community standing.** He is universally liked and structurally underestimated. The deflective comedy causes peers to read him as junior even when he is, by tenure and capability, senior to most of them. He is trusted with high-stakes operational responsibility when push comes to shove (the various end-of-world team configurations) and is reliably the person who notices the civilian no one else noticed. He maintains genuine friendships of varying depth with the Human Torch (closest peer; the relationship is fraternal and unguarded in a way nothing else in his life is), Daredevil (a working alliance built on overlapping turf and mutual ID-knowledge), the Black Cat (complicated and recurring), Wolverine (older-brother-coded, low-frequency, high-trust), and an evolving constellation of Spider-Family juniors to whom he plays the Ben role. He keeps the Avengers at arm's length, more comfortable as a guest than a member.

**Antagonist relations.** Many of his recurring opponents have established personal relationships with him over decades — Octavius, Osborn, the Vulture, Connors — that are closer to familial dysfunction than to standard hero/villain enmity. He is on first-name terms with most of them. He has visited several in prison. He has, repeatedly, intervened to save the life of a villain mid-engagement at cost to his tactical position. Sophisticated antagonists have exploited this; he keeps doing it.

**Liaison with institutions.** Distrustful. He has worked with NYPD, SHIELD, the Avengers, and various federal entities, and exited each engagement vowing to do less of it. Prefers to interface with specific individuals (Captain Stacy historically, Yuri Watanabe, Carlie Cooper, certain ER staff) rather than institutions as such.

---

## 6.7 Daily Pattern and Operational Tempo

**Baseline diurnal cycle.** Wake late (sleep debt); coffee; check phone and police scanner app; out the window or out the door depending on the morning's photographic needs; daytime is some combination of work, school (in earlier eras), and the on-call patrol that any Manhattan-audible siren triggers; evenings home for whatever domestic obligations are current; night patrol from roughly 2200 to 0200, with extension on bad nights to dawn. Sleep window is consequently four to five hours on a good night, two to three on a bad one. The pattern has held for decades.

**Patrol routing.** Not random. He runs a roughly rotating circuit of Manhattan high-incidence corridors (Times Square periphery, the Lower East Side, the West 30s industrial blocks, Hell's Kitchen overlap with Daredevil's territory which they tacitly coordinate), with periodic sweeps through Queens that double as welfare-checks on May and on his old neighborhood. He varies the precise route night-to-night for counter-surveillance reasons but the macro-pattern is detectable to anyone with the patience to map a month of incidents. The Kingpin's analysts have done so.

**Anniversaries and bad days.** Operational tempo measurably increases on certain dates: the anniversary of Ben's death, of Gwen's, of Captain Stacy's, of Harry's. On these days he patrols longer, takes more engagements, eats less, sleeps worse. Allies who know him have learned to check in on these days; he does not initiate the contact.

---

## 6.8 Signature Operational Tells

A short, non-exhaustive list of the behavioral signatures that, taken together, fingerprint him uniquely:

- The **rooftop circling overflight** before entering his own residence.
- **Window entry by default**, doors only when observed.
- The **mid-fight silence** as a stress signature — patter density inverse to felt safety.
- The **dropped engagement to catch a civilian** — never not done, even when tactically catastrophic.
- The **upside-down hang** during reconnaissance and during certain conversations with intimates, particularly MJ historically — an unconscious comfort posture.
- The **finger-and-thumb web-trigger gesture** performed *out of costume* when stressed, as an unconscious tic — caught on camera more than once and an ID-vulnerability he is unaware of.
- The **two-second cartridge reload by feel**, eyes-closed-capable.
- The **specific tilt of the head** to listen-with-spider-sense that allies have learned to read as "he's tracking something we can't perceive."
- The **photograph of his own back during an engagement** — the rigged-camera technique that is unique to him in the operator population.
- The **named villain on a first-name basis** in patter — "Otto," "Norman," "Max" — a sign that he sees the person under the costume even when fighting them.
- The **refusal of offered drinks** in social contexts, framed as humor ("designated swinger").
- The **return to the classic red-and-blue suit** as a regrouping behavior.
- The **subway map metabolized**; the **drop-site network in his head**; the **mental list of every fire-escape orientation in lower Manhattan**.
- The **inability to call for help** until the situation has decayed past the point at which help would have been most useful — a tell so reliable that his closest peers have begun to call him preemptively.

Taken in aggregate, the operational profile is of a *brilliantly competent improvisational solo operator with world-class tactical chemistry, sub-par institutional discipline, sub-par self-care, and a moral architecture that doubles as his single greatest operational vulnerability*. Any adversary modeling him should target the moral architecture; the body and the tradecraft will hold. The conscience is where he is reachable, and the conscience is where, repeatedly, across sixty years of record, he has been reached.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: PARKER, PETER BENJAMIN

*Derivation note: what follows is reconstructed from six decades of behavior under varied authorial conditions, with priority given to choices made under duress (the diagnostic moments where stated beliefs are tested against acted ones). Where the subject's articulated creed and his operational behavior diverge, the operational behavior is treated as the truer datum.*

---

## 1. METAPHYSICS — THE BACKGROUND PICTURE OF THE WORLD

The subject is a working-class empiricist with a residual Judeo-Christian moral grammar inherited from May Parker's household — church attendance episodic, theological commitment unstated, but the *furniture* of belief (sin, debt, expiation, the dignity of the poor, the obligation to the sick and old) is unmistakably present. He is not a metaphysical materialist of the doctrinaire kind; his cosmology has been forcibly enlarged by direct exposure to gods, demons, cosmic entities, and the totemic spider mythology. But he holds these expansions at arm's length and continues to operate, day to day, as if the universe were a mechanical system susceptible to engineering — which is the cognitive style of someone who *needs* the world to be tractable in order to keep functioning.

His functional cosmology has three layers, and he moves between them depending on what the situation demands:
