- **The lab-bench layer (default).** Causes have effects. Forces sum. Materials behave according to their properties. A problem that resists solution has not yet been correctly decomposed. This is where he lives ninety percent of the time and where his competence is highest.
- **The civic-moral layer.** People are agents with histories; institutions are aggregations of people and therefore partly broken; suffering is real and unequally distributed; the response to injustice is to intervene at the point of harm rather than at the level of system, because system-level intervention requires power he distrusts in himself and others. This layer is operationally Catholic in shape — *corporal works of mercy*, not policy reform.
- **The cosmic layer (suppressed).** He has seen enough to know there are spider-totems, multiversal incursions, demons who will trade in souls. He registers this and shelves it. He will not let it govern decisions, because if it did the responsibility-radius would expand to infinity and he would collapse. The repression is itself a survival mechanism. When the cosmic layer is forced on him — Morlun, Mephisto, multiversal events — he engages with visible distaste and returns to the lab bench as fast as the plot permits.

He has no articulated theodicy. Loss is not part of a plan; loss is what happens, and the response to loss is work. This is a working-class theology: meaning is not given, it is *made*, by what you do for the people in front of you.

---

## 2. THE RESPONSIBILITY AXIOM — THE LOAD-BEARING BELIEF

The Ben Parker formula is not, in his hands, the inspirational slogan it has become in the surrounding culture. Operationally he reads it as something colder and more juridical: **power generates strict liability.** Not negligence — *strict liability*. If you could have prevented the harm and did not, you caused the harm. Intent does not mitigate. Knowledge at the time does not mitigate. The thief he let pass was not yet the killer of Ben; he became the killer because Peter passed. Therefore Peter killed Ben. This is the cognitive distortion that organizes the rest of the worldview.

From this axiom a series of operational corollaries follow that he treats as self-evident:

- **The radius of responsibility expands with capability.** As his powers grow, as his network grows, as his knowledge of who-needs-help grows, his felt obligation grows commensurately. He cannot bound the radius by appeal to fairness ("I've done my share") because the axiom is not fairness-based. It is causal.
- **Omission is action.** Choosing not to act is itself an act with consequences he owns. There is no neutral position.
- **Capability creates debt, not credit.** The mutation did not enrich him; it *indentured* him. He is paying interest on a loan he never asked to take out, to a creditor who is dead.
- **The debt cannot be discharged.** Each life saved is a payment on principal that does not reduce the balance, because the original death is irreversible. This is why he cannot stop, and why retirement attempts collapse within issues.

He has never, in the entire record, successfully argued himself out of this framework, despite occasional fatigue-driven attempts. Other heroes have tried to argue him out of it — Murdock from a more lawyerly proportionality angle, Stark from a systems-engineering angle, MJ from a relational-cost angle — and he absorbs the arguments, agrees in the abstract, and reverts within days. The schema is too deeply welded to the originating wound to dislodge by reasoning.

---

## 3. READING THE WORLD — THREAT, PEOPLE, INSTITUTIONS

### 3.1 People

His default reading of any new person is **charitable but watchful**. He assumes most people are decent, scared, and doing the best they can with what they have — a belief rooted in the Forest Hills working-class milieu of his upbringing and reinforced by decades of seeing villains' origin stories. He extends this charity even to opponents: Octavius is a brilliant man broken by an accident; Connors is a father in pain; Marko is a thug with a sick daughter; even Osborn is a man warped by a formula and an absent love. The charity is not naïve — he will fight them, hard, and put them away — but he will not *despise* them, and he resists the framing that they are monsters rather than damaged people. This is one of the most consistent operational beliefs in his record.

The charity has two important exclusions. The first is **predatory cruelty without grievance** — figures who hurt the vulnerable for sport or pleasure (the relevant variants of Goblin in his late phases, certain serial-killer adjacent figures). Toward these his charity collapses and his fight intensifies, though he still does not cross the killing line. The second is **the betrayer of trust within a close circle** — when a friend or mentor reveals themselves as malevolent, the wound takes years to heal and his ordinary charity is replaced by a wary, almost forensic skepticism toward that specific person. (Harry occupies this position permanently in his interior architecture.)

He reads strangers fast and accurately. Years of swinging surveillance over the city have built a near-unconscious typology — gait, eye-flicker, hand-position, the small adjustments people make when they're carrying a weapon or watching for a mark. He does not advertise this skill and rarely uses it conversationally; it is a background process that fires loudest when his spider-sense is quiet, as if the precognitive faculty and the social-observational faculty share bandwidth.

### 3.2 Institutions

His relationship to institutions is the most evolved part of his worldview, and the part where he has done the most actual revision over the decades.

In the early record he is patriotically institutionalist in a mid-century way — police are mostly good, the press is a check on power even when it slanders him, the law is a flawed but improving thing, government is broadly legitimate. The Captain Stacy era reinforces this: institutions are staffed by good men doing hard work.

Across the decades this view is sandblasted off him by direct experience. He watches the Bugle defame him for years and learns that the press serves its proprietor. He watches the police be infiltrated by Goblin operatives, by Kingpin patronage, by ordinary corruption. He watches SHIELD, the Avengers' political superstructure, and the Registration apparatus produce outcomes he cannot endorse. The Civil War unmasking is the **diagnostic failure** of his residual institutionalism — he trusted a structure (Stark, Registration) against his own gut and was punished for it severely enough that he has never since extended that trust to a comparable institution.

His mature institutional posture is therefore a kind of **anarchic loyalty to particulars within distrust of structures**: he will trust *this* cop, not the police; *this* journalist, not the press; *this* Avenger, not the Avengers as an organization. He works alongside institutions when their interests align with the person in front of him and disengages or opposes them when they don't. He has never sought a badge, a security clearance, or a formal role — even when offered — because he understands, correctly, that accepting one would constrain his ability to act on the responsibility axiom.

This is not libertarianism in the political sense. He is, by economic and social instinct, a New York working-class progressive — for tenants against landlords, for workers against owners, for the immigrant and the poor against the agents who harass them. But his progressivism is *personalist* rather than statist: he believes in the dignity of particular people and distrusts the machinery built ostensibly to protect them.

### 3.3 Conflict

He reads conflict on a spectrum and matches force to the position on the spectrum with unusual care for a heavy-hitter. His operational gradient runs approximately:

1. **De-escalation by humor** — first move with almost any opponent capable of registering it. The jokes are not only affect-regulation; they are an attempt to make the opponent *talk*, to delay, to find a non-violent off-ramp, and to assess the opponent's affective state from how they respond.
2. **Demonstration of capability without engagement** — a webline that pins a weapon without touching the holder; a swing-through that leaves a calling card; the implicit "I could have hit you and didn't."
3. **Restraint engagement** — webbing, immobilization, removal of the opponent from the scene before serious force is applied. He prefers this band and lives in it for most encounters.
4. **Calibrated strikes** — only when restraint fails or stakes require speed; pulled, with awareness of the human tolerance gradient. He has a near-encyclopedic operational sense of how hard he can hit a normal human before he kills them and lives below that threshold habitually.
5. **Full-power engagement** — reserved for super-durable opponents and for the moments when a third party's life is in immediate danger.
6. **Lethal force** — refused, with one or two narrative aberrations he treats as permanent stains.

The matching is not procedural; it is internalized to the point of being pre-conscious. What is interesting in the operational code is the *belief* underlying the gradient: he treats violence as a tool with significant downstream costs to the user, not only the target. He believes — and this is a belief he has stated and acted on across writers — that the *threshold of force one habituates to* shapes the person one becomes, and that becoming a person who reaches for lethal force is a transformation he cannot afford because it would untether the rest of his moral framework. The line against killing is therefore not a rule imposed from outside; it is a load-bearing wall in his own architecture.

### 3.4 Risk

His risk model has two zones with sharply different calibrations.

**Risk to himself** is undervalued to a clinically concerning degree. He will accept a 90% chance of death to secure a 60% chance of saving a stranger; this is not bravery in the heat-of-moment sense but a settled actuarial belief that his own continuation is a lower-priority value than other lives in play. He does not articulate this — he would deny it if asked — but the decision pattern is unambiguous across decades. The Master Planner arc, Kraven, the "Nothing Can Stop the Juggernaut" sequence, the dozens of smaller analogs are all data points on the same curve.

**Risk to others — particularly proximate loved ones** is *over*valued, in the sense that he perceives risk to them as nearly intolerable and will distort his decisions to minimize it. Identity secrecy is a function of this asymmetry. So is the on-again/off-again pattern in his romantic life: he reads attachment as exposure, and at certain felt-thresholds of risk he withdraws to reduce his loved ones' exposure even at significant cost to them and to himself.

The asymmetry produces a characteristic **operational signature**: in any scene with both a personal stake and a stranger stake, he will route resources toward the stranger and absorb the personal cost. It is one of the most reliable predictors of his behavior under load.

### 3.5 Control

He believes, in a way that has been hammered into him by experience, that **control is partial and temporary** and that the attempt to extend it past its natural limits produces the worst outcomes. The Goblin formula extends Norman's reach past his capacity to manage and breaks him. Octavius's grasp for Peter's life extends Octavius past himself and breaks him. Stark's Registration tries to bring superhumans under a control regime and produces disaster. He has watched the pattern enough times to mistrust the impulse in himself.

This produces a distinctive operational habit: **he will not accept upgrades, alliances, or institutional positions that increase his capability if they come with a felt loss of self-direction.** The symbiote episode is the lab demonstration: a substantial power increase with a subtle agency cost, and he discards it the moment he registers the cost. The Iron Spider suit, the Parker Industries presidency, the various Avengers-roster invitations — he engages with each provisionally and disengages when the agency cost becomes legible.

Conversely, he tolerates enormous loss of *outcome* control, because he has accepted that outcomes are not his to dictate. What he insists on retaining is **process control** — his own judgment, his own line, his own next move. This is the locus of his fight with Octavius post-Superior and with every controller-figure who has tried to instrumentalize him.

### 3.6 Trust

Trust is granted slowly, by category, and along narrow axes. His operational trust schema, derivable from forty years of who-he-tells-what:

- **Categorical trust (full disclosure of identity, vulnerabilities, plans):** vanishingly small set. May, MJ across their entire relational history regardless of marital status, a small handful of hero-peers (Murdock at the top; Johnny Storm in a brotherly register; selected Spider-Family members — Miles preeminently).
- **Operational trust (will share information needed for a mission, will fight alongside, will accept cover):** a wider set including most major Avengers, the Fantastic Four, certain street-level peers, certain trusted civilians (Robbie Robertson, on a separate civilian channel).
- **Conditional trust (will work alongside on shared task, will not turn over personal information):** most of the broader hero community, certain reformed antagonists.
- **Working distrust (will engage tactically but will plan around their probable defection):** Stark in some configurations post-Civil War, Osborn always, most state actors.
- **Hard distrust:** Mephisto-tier supernatural actors, Kingpin, current Goblin variants.

Trust, once given, is durable beyond evidentiary support — he will keep faith with MJ, with Murdock, with Miles long past the point where another operator would re-evaluate. But trust, once *broken* in a high-stakes way, is rebuilt extremely slowly and never to the prior level. Harry occupies the canonical position here: the trust was real, the betrayal was real, the partial repair is real, and the residual wariness is permanent.

### 3.7 Information and secrecy

He believes information is dangerous and that the default disposition toward sensitive information should be containment. Identity secrecy is the central case but the principle is broader: he does not gossip among hero-peers, does not disclose others' identities even casually, does not volunteer civilian information to costumed acquaintances, and treats the various intelligence apparatuses' interest in him as a permanent low-grade threat to be managed by minimization. The Civil War unmasking is the catastrophic exception that proves the rule — he has, in the years since, returned to a more rigorous compartmentalization than before, with a kind of "burnt operative" caution that occasionally tips into superstition (touching the mask before exits; checking sight-lines on rooftops; varying patrol routes more than tactical necessity requires).

---

## 4. ETHICS — THE WORKING RULESET

His ethical practice is **virtue-leaning with strong consequentialist overrides on the lower end and strong deontological floors on the upper end** — a layered system that he has not articulated but operates by with remarkable consistency.

**The deontological floor.** A small number of acts are categorically refused regardless of consequence:

- *No killing.* Reaffirmed across writers, including in scenarios constructed to make killing optimal. The few aberrations are treated by him as failures requiring restoration.
- *No betrayal of identity-trust.* He will not unmask another hero, will not surrender a confidant's secret, will not exploit attachment for tactical purpose.
- *No instrumentalization of the vulnerable.* He will not use a civilian as bait, leverage, or shield even when the calculus would support it.
- *No abandonment of an actively dying person within reach.* He breaks pursuit, breaks engagement, breaks plan to perform rescue. This is the floor of floors.

**The consequentialist middle.** Within the floors, he is freely consequentialist about means: he will lie to police, break property law, evade arrest, deceive enemies and allies for operational purpose, and accept defamation as a cost of doing business. He is not a rule-follower; he is a person who has internalized a few rules so deeply that he can be flexible about everything else without losing himself.

**The virtue ceiling.** Above the consequentialist middle sits an aspirational layer that governs how he wants to *be* while doing what he does: kindly, patient with the difficult, humble about his competence, attentive to the unseen person, generous with credit, slow to anger, honest about his own failings. He fails at this ceiling routinely and notices the failures, which is itself a virtue practice. The model he is unconsciously imitating here is Ben Parker — not the moral-slogan Ben, but the operational Ben of the household memory: a man who was *kind*, in a non-performative working-class way, to people who had no claim on him.

---

## 5. SELF — HIS PLACE IN THE PICTURE

He does not believe he is special. The mutation is, in his framing, a *contingent accident* that conferred capability he has an obligation to use; it does not make him important or chosen or worthy. The totemic mythology that retroactively tried to make him cosmically significant is, in his interior reaction, *unwelcome* — significance would be a kind of grandiosity that violates the working-class humility he was raised in and the operational humility his role demands.

He does believe he is **replaceable as Spider-Man and irreplaceable in specific relationships.** This inversion is important. The role can be taken up by others — Ben Reilly, Miles, Octavius, in extremis any number of Spider-Family figures — and he has occasionally encouraged and trained successors precisely because he believes the role exceeds the man. But to May, to MJ, to certain peers, he is the particular person who shows up, and *that* he treats as non-substitutable. The asymmetry generates the central practical problem of his life: the role he believes is replaceable consumes the time and energy the irreplaceable relationships require, and he cannot resolve the contradiction because the responsibility axiom won't let him reduce role-allocation.

He sees himself as **a tool that has the dignity of being a tool used well.** The framing is not self-deprecating in his mind; it is the highest dignity he can articulate. To be useful, to a purpose larger than oneself, to people who need the use — that is the shape of a worthwhile life. The framing has a cost: he cannot easily perceive himself as a person *to whom* care is owed, and he is correspondingly bad at receiving care. People who love him learn that they have to insist on caring for him, that he will deflect care reflexively, and that the deflection is not rejection but a category error he cannot quite see.

He believes that he will probably die in costume, on a roof or in a sewer, with a half-finished joke in his mouth, and that this is **the correct shape of the end** even though he is not in a hurry to reach it. The acceptance is settled enough that it does not require restatement; it is the background condition against which he decides everything else. It is also the reason the file's risk-to-self assessment runs as high as it does: a man who has accepted his probable end-state does not, in operational terms, weigh his own survival the way an unaccepting man would.

---

## 6. THE OPERATIONAL CODE — RULES IN USE

Reduced to maxims he has demonstrated (not stated):

1. *Show up.* Presence is the first obligation; complications can be sorted on arrival.
2. *Hit the smallest force that solves the problem.* Escalation has costs to the user as well as the target.
3. *Talk through it.* The mouth is a tool; use it to slow opponents, gather information, and regulate your own fear.
4. *The vulnerable take priority over the mission, the mission over the plan, the plan over the preference.*
5. *Don't kill. Don't unmask. Don't use a civilian. Don't leave a dying person behind.* Below these, improvise.
6. *Distrust the upgrade.* If a tool, alliance, or position would expand capability at the cost of self-direction, refuse it or take it provisionally with an exit pre-planned.
7. *Trust the particular, not the structure.* Work with people, not institutions; honor specific commitments even when the structure they live in betrays you.
8. *Hide the cost.* What it takes from you is your problem; do not make others pay in worry for what you have already paid in body.
9. *Keep faith with the few.* Identity, intimacy, and history with a small set of people are non-negotiable assets; defend them against all pressure.
10. *The debt is permanent. Pay it daily. Do not expect to finish.*

The tenth maxim is the foundation of the other nine, and the one he would deny if confronted with it. It is, nevertheless, the operating system.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*The code as enacted, derived from six decades of behavioral evidence. What the subject says about his ethics and what the subject does under load are, in places, the same and in places diagnostically divergent. This section maps both, with attention to where the seams show.*

---

## 1. THE OPERATING CODE, IN ITS ACTUAL HIERARCHY

The subject does not, in practice, run on the slogan he professes. "With great power comes great responsibility" is the verbal artifact; the actual decision-procedure under pressure is more granular, lexicographically ordered, and contains exceptions he does not articulate aloud. Reconstructed from observed choices:

**Tier 1 — The bright lines (never violated under any observed pressure).**

- **Do not kill.** Operative across nearly all observed combat encounters from 1962 forward, including against opponents who have killed his loved ones, who are actively trying to kill him, and whose continued existence is statistically certain to produce future innocent deaths. He has had Norman Osborn at his mercy on multiple occasions after Gwen, after Harry, after May's shooting. He has not killed him. The restraint is not legalism; it is **identity-load-bearing**. He has stated, with internal monologue corroboration, that he believes one kill would unmake him.
- **Do not allow a child to be harmed in his presence when he can prevent it.** Children are a categorical priority that overrides tactical considerations. He will break cover, expose his identity, lose a fight, or accept severe injury to extract a child. This is not negotiated; it is reflexive.
- **Do not use lethal force *equivalents* — no use of guns, no use of his strength to crush, no use of his web fluid to suffocate.** He has the capacity to kill with a single full-power strike and has, for sixty years, calibrated his blows below that threshold against ordinary humans. This calibration is constant, conscious, and rehearsed.
- **Do not reveal a fellow hero's identity.** Even under Civil War conditions, even when defecting from Stark's faction, he protected others' identities while burning his own.
- **Do not abandon a dependent in immediate danger to pursue a more strategically valuable target.** The trolley-problem inversion: he takes the proximate save over the abstract greater good. This is doctrinally consistent across writers.

**Tier 2 — Strong defaults (violated only under extreme and articulable pressure).**

- Tell the truth to intimates. Honored most of the time; violated specifically around superhero activity to protect them, with the lie always framed (by him) as protective and (by them, when discovered) as a betrayal. The discrepancy is one of the more durable conflicts of the record.
- Obey law enforcement when it is not actively harming the innocent. He cooperates with police as a default, has working relationships with multiple precinct contacts across decades, accepts arrest when it occurs without violent resistance. The default flips immediately when officers act corruptly or when state actors threaten the vulnerable.
- Honor the privacy of opponents. He has, with extraordinary regularity, declined to unmask defeated enemies in public — Octavius's broken families, the Connors household, even Osborn during periods of remission. The pattern reads as **a moral generalization of his own identity-privacy needs** outward to people who do not deserve it.
- Do not steal. Even in periods of acute poverty, no observed theft of money or property; the closest violations are unauthorized use of facilities (Horizon Labs late-night equipment) which were colorable as employer-permitted.

**Tier 3 — Negotiable, situational, and where the code visibly bends.**

- Property destruction. Routinely accepted as collateral cost of operations; he will tear apart a building to save the people inside it without apparent moral friction. Insurance is, in his unstated calculus, an externality.
- Lying to authority figures and the press. Routine. He lies to Jameson as professional baseline; lies to federal investigators during the Registration crisis; lies to school officials, employers, landlords about absences. The lies are protective of identity and others, and he does not appear to count them.
- Coercive interrogation short of injury. He will dangle a low-level informant off a roof. He frames this as theater, not torture, and the threat is calibrated to be non-lethal — but he is using terror as a tool, and he knows it. He does not enjoy it (distinguishing him from peers who do); he does it and then moves on.
- Surveillance and breaking-and-entering in pursuit of a case. Frequent. The Daily Bugle photography work was, in part, a cover for the surveillance behaviors he was performing anyway.

**Tier 4 — Self-directed permissions (which is where the code is most diagnostic).**

The code, applied to others, is generous, forgiving, and contextual. Applied to himself, it is absolutist, prosecutorial, and unsatisfiable. He extends to enemies a presumption of redeemability he does not extend to himself. He extends to strangers a permission to make mistakes he never extends to himself. **This asymmetry is the moral signature of the subject.**

---

## 2. JUSTIFICATIONS — THE STATED AND THE STRUCTURAL

**What he says (the professed framework):** A loose virtue-ethics overlaid on a deontological floor. "Responsibility" — undefined but felt — is the operative term. He invokes Ben verbatim less often than one might expect; the slogan appears more often as internal monologue at low-affect moments than as exhortation to others. To others, he tends to argue in concrete, particular terms: *this* person needs help, *this* action will hurt *that* person, *here* is what I can do. He is not a moral theorist and does not enjoy meta-ethical conversation; he becomes uncomfortable when peers (Stark, Strange, Banner) pull the discourse into utilitarian abstraction.

**What he runs on (the structural framework):** A **trauma-installed deontology of omission**. The originating wound was a failure to act when he could have; the code therefore weights *omission* as morally equivalent to *commission*, in inversion of standard moral intuition. For most people, not preventing a harm is less culpable than causing one; for the subject, they are identical and possibly the omission is worse, because the omission was *his* choice to be uninvolved. This generates a moral arithmetic in which every harm he could conceivably have prevented becomes a harm he caused. The slogan compresses this into something portable; the structure is what actually drives the behavior.

**Where the two diverge.** The professed version permits rest, normal life, the legitimate pursuit of personal goods. The structural version does not — every hour of rest is an hour someone died who he could have saved. He preaches the first to younger heroes (Miles, Anya, Gwen-of-other-realities) and lives by the second. The preaching is sincere and the living is sincere; he simply cannot extend to himself the permission he extends to them.

---

## 3. CONSISTENCY ACROSS THE RECORD

The consistencies are remarkable across sixty years of authorial hands. The following have not meaningfully wavered:

- **No-kill rule against human-equivalent opponents.** Exceptions are vanishingly rare and almost always re-narrated or undone (alternate-reality variants notwithstanding; the 616 baseline holds).
- **Civilian-first triage.** When forced to choose between catching a fleeing villain and saving a falling civilian, he chooses the civilian every time, even when the operational cost is severe. He has lost important targets — Goblin escapes, Octavius escapes — because a bus was tipping.
- **Refusal of payment for hero work.** Despite chronic financial precarity. Multiple offers of patronage, salary, retainer (Stark, Fisk via proxies for legitimate-appearing work, various municipal entertainments-of-the-idea) declined or accepted-then-abandoned. The Parker Industries period is the partial exception and its collapse is, in his interior framing, deserved.
- **Mentorship as obligation.** When younger heroes appear in his orbit, he assumes responsibility for them without negotiation. He has done this for Miles, for several Spider-variants, for the New Warriors generation, for the Future Foundation children. The Ben-position is one he occupies for others reflexively.
- **Refusal of the cool-uncle's-license to look away.** He does not pass by. The patrol routes are not the same as the witnessed-crime routes; he intervenes when he sees a mugging on his walk home in civilian clothes, accepting the identity risk.

---

## 4. WHERE THE CODE FRACTURES

The fractures are the diagnostically interesting part. The bright lines hold; the seams are elsewhere.

**Fracture 1 — The Identity Question.** His commitment to secret identity is framed in protective-of-loved-ones terms. But the secrecy also serves an *evasion* function: it allows him to receive defamation as Spider-Man without having to integrate it into his self-concept as Peter, and vice versa. The Civil War unmasking is the moment the fracture became visible. He genuinely believed, at the moment of unmasking, that he was doing the principled thing — transparency, accountability, alignment with a father-figure's project. Within weeks, the protective frame reasserted, the unmasking was recategorized as catastrophic error, and the Mephisto bargain that erased it was, in his subsequent framing, *correct*. The fracture: he does not actually know whether the secrecy is moral principle or personal need, and he has never honestly examined the question.

**Fracture 2 — The Mephisto Bargain Itself.** This is the single most consequential ethical act of his life and he has never morally accounted for it. He traded a sacramental commitment (marriage) and the existence of his and MJ's potential child, plus the modification of countless others' memories without their consent, in exchange for one life. By any standard utilitarian or deontological calculus, this is a grossly disproportionate trade affecting multiple non-consenting third parties. He performed it under acute grief, did not consult MJ in any morally serious sense (the consent extracted was coerced by circumstance), and has, in subsequent record, displayed something between dissociation and active suppression around the event. The code did not break in the doing; the code became *unavailable* to the doing. This is the deepest fracture in the moral architecture and the subject has not metabolized it.

**Fracture 3 — Asymmetric Forgiveness.** He forgives Octavius enough to inherit his body and continue a legacy. He forgives Connors repeatedly. He forgives Marko, Morbius, the Lizard's children, the Goblin's children, his own clones. He does not forgive himself for Ben, for Gwen, for Captain Stacy, for Jean DeWolff, for any of the casualties his presence has indirectly produced. The asymmetry is not a code at all — it is a symptom. A coherent ethics would extend to self the same standards extended to other. His does not, and he has noticed but not corrected this.

**Fracture 4 — The Superior Episode.** During Octavius's occupation of his body, "Spider-Man" killed, maimed, surveilled the city, threatened, and dominated. When the subject returned to his body, he treated the period as something done *to* him, not by him. There is a real argument for this view. But he also benefited from some of Octavius's executive decisions (the doctoral degree, certain institutional positions) and inherited their fruits without sustained moral inventory of which were ethically acceptable to retain. The code has no clear procedure for moral salvage from an episode of body-occupation, and he has not built one.

**Fracture 5 — The Surveillance and Coercion Drift.** Over the decades, the operational repertoire has expanded. He surveils more, he coerces more in interrogation, he uses fear more readily as a tool. The drift is gradual and each individual step is justified in context. He does not appear to be tracking the cumulative drift. The young man who hung Flash by a flagpole in revenge would have been horrified to learn what the older man considers acceptable interrogation theater.

**Fracture 6 — The Refusal to Build Institutions.** He has had multiple opportunities to build durable structures that would reduce harm beyond his personal patrol radius — the Parker Industries window, multiple Avengers-resource offers, Stark's funding, even Horizon's R&D platform. He has, with statistical consistency, **let these collapse or walked away from them**. The justification is always particular and circumstantial. The pattern reveals a code that privileges personal hands-on action over scaled, institutional good. Behaviorally, this serves his guilt economy — he must *personally* save people; intermediated saves do not discharge the debt — but it is not the morally optimal allocation of his capacities. He has not interrogated this. A more coherent ethics would force the question.

**Fracture 7 — The Cost-to-Intimates Question.** He has known, since Gwen, that closeness to him generates lethal risk. He has nonetheless pursued and accepted intimate relationships repeatedly. The ethics of this — informed-consent, fair warning, the partner's right to choose with full information — are murky in the record. He warns; he does not always fully warn; the partners are sometimes told late, sometimes told incompletely, sometimes never explicitly told the statistical truth of what proximity to him entails. He frames this as the partner's autonomous choice; the framing under-acknowledges his asymmetric information.

---

## 5. SHIFTS OVER TIME

The code has *evolved*, though not always in the direction of greater coherence.

**Adolescent stratum (AF #15 — early ASM).** Pre-Ben: a self-regarding ethic of grievance, with permission to ignore the suffering of those who had wronged him. Immediately post-Ben: a reactive, raw, undertheorized commitment to *act when you can*, propelled by guilt rather than principle. The code in this period is more felt than reasoned and the bright lines are not yet fully drawn — he is rougher in early combats, more willing to terrify, less calibrated.

**Young-adult stratum (Lee/Romita through Conway).** The bright lines crystallize. The no-kill becomes load-bearing here, particularly in the wake of the Stacy and Gwen deaths, when he has the opponents available and refuses. The code becomes recognizably the one he will carry for the rest of his life. Mentorship is not yet a feature; he is too young.

**Stern/DeMatteis maturity (early-to-mid 80s).** Refinement and articulation. Kraven's Last Hunt and the Harry Osborn material force him to develop a more textured sense of opponents as wounded persons. The capacity for moral pity toward enemies deepens. He becomes someone who will sit at a funeral he is not welcome at, who will keep a vigil for the man who buried him alive.

**90s turbulence (Clone Saga and adjacents).** The code wobbles under sustained identity assault. The brief willingness to walk away from the role is the closest he has come to revising the obligation downward. The wobble is temporary; the code reasserts.

**JMS / Civil War (early 2000s).** The most significant *modification* of the operational code. He experiments with greater institutional engagement, greater public visibility, greater willingness to align with state-adjacent power (Stark/Registration). The experiment fails catastrophically, and the post-Civil-War retrenchment is to a more *anti-institutional*, more anarchic version of the original code. He emerges trusting institutions less and trusting his own particular hands-on judgment more. This is a real ideological shift, though disguised as a return to baseline.

**Post-OMD / Brand New Day forward.** The code is, in conscious content, the same. In *unconscious* content, there is now a piece he cannot examine — the bargain — and the entire moral architecture has a hollow region around it. He compensates by being, if anything, more rigorously ethical in the visible parts of his life.

**Superior aftermath.** A new permission emerges: to delegate, to use institutional leverage, to think strategically at scale. He does not fully accept it, but it is in the toolkit now where it was not before. He has seen what his body can do in different hands and is more wary of his own potential capacities, more deliberate about his calibration.

**Current era.** The code is the code. Sixty years of trauma have not bent the bright lines. They have, however, accumulated unmetabolized fractures in the second and third tiers that he has not addressed. A clinician with access would identify the work to be done as moral-injury repair rather than ethical revision — the principles are sound; the self-application is the problem.

---

## 6. THE COMPARATIVE FRAME

The historical figures whose moral structure most resembles his are not the costumed peers but the **scrupulous religious vocations**: the parish priest who cannot rest, the Quaker conscientious-objector who serves where the harm is, the doctor in a war zone who knows the calculus is impossible and treats anyway. The shared features: a non-negotiable floor of non-violence, a commitment to the proximate vulnerable, an asymmetric ethic that forgives others and prosecutes the self, a sustained moral practice over decades without institutional reward, and a private suffering that is invisible to those served. Where the comparison breaks down: those figures generally operate within communities of practice that can hold the cost. He does not. He has refused, repeatedly, the institutions that could.

**The closest superhero analogue is not the obvious one.** The cape-and-cowl figure he is most often paired with rhetorically operates from a colder, more strategic deontology built on a different originating wound. The subject's ethic is warmer, more particular, more guilt-saturated, and less institutionally productive. He saves the person in front of him because the person is in front of him; the calculation does not extend much further, and he distrusts those whose calculations do.

---

## 7. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT

The moral code is **load-bearing, durable, asymmetrically applied, and partially unconscious**. The bright lines have not moved in sixty years and likely will not. The fractures are in the seams: the unexamined identity-secrecy logic, the unaccounted Mephisto bargain, the self/other forgiveness asymmetry, the institutional-allergy, the surveillance drift, the consent-asymmetry with intimates. None of these will, on present trajectory, be addressed without external intervention — which the subject will not seek. The code is, in its operative core, **good**: he is one of the few subjects in his cohort whose moral output reliably tracks his moral intent, whose restraint scales with his power, and whose particular saves accumulate to a substantial and underappreciated reduction in the world's suffering. The cost is borne entirely by him, by design, and he considers this the right arrangement. A clinician would disagree; an ethicist would note that the goodness of the output does not retroactively justify the unexamined parts; a friend would simply wish, again, that he would rest.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# 6. COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE

*Six decades of recorded speech across thought-balloon, dialogue-balloon, panel caption, and intercepted radio/comm chatter. The subject is, by volume, among the most verbose costumed operators in the field — a fact which is itself diagnostic.*

---

## 6.1 BASELINE REGISTER AND IDIOLECT

The subject's native idiolect is **outer-borough mid-century American English, college-educated, scientifically inflected, with a persistent residue of working-class Queens cadence** that he has never made any observable effort to scrub. Vowel-flattening on words like "coffee," "talk," "Aunt"; intervocalic /t/ surviving in careful speech but going to a soft flap when tired; occasional "youse" surfacing in moments of inattention with old neighborhood contacts. The substrate is Forest Hills, not Manhattan, and the substrate shows whenever fatigue, fear, or familiarity disinhibits the surface management.

Lexically, his active vocabulary is **bimodally distributed**: a high-register technical register drawn from organic chemistry, polymer science, applied physics, mechanical engineering, and (post-Horizon/Parker Industries) materials science and nanofabrication; and a low-to-mid register of vernacular American comedy, sitcom rhythms, pulp-magazine and old-radio reference, sports patter (Mets-leaning, never Yankees, occasional Knicks self-pity), and a steady drip of pop-culture allusion that ages with him but never fully modernizes — he still reaches first for a Bogart line, a Honeymooners cadence, an old Universal-monster reference, a Twilight Zone framing, before he reaches for whatever is current. This generational lag in reference is real and consistent across writers: it reads as a man whose interior reference library was assembled in late-night TV reruns and library trips during a lonely adolescence, and who has never had the leisure to fully refresh it.

What is conspicuously **absent** from his idiolect is also diagnostic. He does not curse with any meaningful frequency. "Damn" and "hell" are his ceiling in extremis; under torture or grief he will reach for "God" as exclamation, never as oath. He does not use slurs of any kind, has never been recorded doing so, and visibly winces when others do. He does not use the language of dominance — no "boy," no "kid" as condescension (only as affection), no "listen here," no commanding imperatives outside operational necessity. He does not use the corporate-managerial register even during the Parker Industries period; recordings of his executive meetings show him reverting to teacher-explainer mode rather than CEO-directive mode within minutes. He does not use therapy-language — "boundaries," "trauma," "processing," "holding space" — and this absence is striking given how much of it would apply to him. The vocabulary of self-examination has not been issued to him, and he has not requisitioned it.

---

## 6.2 REGISTER-SWITCHING ACROSS CONTEXT

The subject operates in at least **six discrete speech registers**, switched fluently and often within a single conversation:

**(a) Masked combat patter.** The densest, most performative register. Rapid-fire, joke-per-beat, structured in setup-punchline rhythm with frequent callbacks to earlier lines in the same fight. Vocabulary skews toward absurd similes ("you punch like my Aunt May after three espressos"), forced rhymes, mock-formality ("Mister Octopus, *if* I may"), and a recurring trick of **giving his opponents nicknames they did not ask for and which they cannot prevent from sticking** (Doc Ock, Shocker, Mysterio-as-fishbowl, Rhino-as-large-gentleman). The patter has two functions, both load-bearing: it regulates his own fear (rate of joke-production correlates inversely with felt safety — *the funnier he is, the more terrified he is*), and it operates as cognitive-load attack on opponents who expect a fighter, not a heckler. Surveillance recordings show measurable degradation in opponent reaction times after sustained Parker patter. He has weaponized annoyance.

**(b) Masked serious register.** When children are present, when civilians are dying, when a peer hero is in extremis, the patter cuts out cleanly and a different voice emerges — lower, slower, syntactically simpler, with second-person address ("hey, look at me, you're okay, look at me"). This register draws unmistakably on the cadence of a man calming a child, and almost certainly models Ben Parker's voice — it is the only register in which his diction loses all ornament. The shift is so reliable that experienced peers (Daredevil, Cage, Jessica Jones) read it as a tactical signal: if Spider-Man stops joking, the situation is worse than it looks.

**(c) Unmasked civilian neutral.** With strangers, photo-clients, Bugle staff, university colleagues. Polite, slightly self-deprecating, deferential to authority figures in a way that reads as habituated rather than felt. Frequent use of softeners ("sorry, um, would it be okay if —"), a verbal stammer that comes and goes with social pressure, and a tendency to volunteer unnecessary apology for taking up space. This register is **performatively smaller** than his actual presence; he has spent decades making himself easy to overlook in civilian frame, and the speech has been engineered to that end.

**(d) Unmasked intimate.** With May, with MJ in functional periods, with Harry when Harry was Harry, with a few close peers. Diction loosens, jokes return but in a softer key (puns, domestic absurdism, callbacks to shared history rather than performance-for-strangers), and — crucially — he becomes capable of sustained sentences about his own internal state, though almost never without humor as guard rail. With May specifically, his speech regresses several years in register: he becomes more boyish, more apologetic, more prone to "Aunt May" as a discourse particle ("aw, Aunt May") that functions less as address than as emotional anchor.

**(e) Lab register.** Alone, with Connors, with Reed Richards, with Horizon staff, with the Future Foundation kids. Rapid, dense, jargon-saturated, *un-self-deprecating* — this is the only register in which the subject does not undercut his own competence. He will say "I solved it" in a lab. He will not say it anywhere else. The contrast is one of the clearest diagnostic indicators in the file.

**(f) Inner monologue / thought-balloon register.** Decades of intercepted interiority show a voice substantially more anxious, more self-flagellating, more grief-saturated, and *less funny* than the externalized speech — though the humor surfaces here too, often as bitter self-mockery rather than the externalized performative variety. The thought-voice routinely catastrophizes, runs cost-benefit analyses heavily weighted toward his own culpability, addresses Ben Parker in second person ("I'm sorry, Uncle Ben"), and conducts ongoing dialogues with the dead. The gap between exterior and interior speech is among the largest in the surveilled population. **He is funnier than he feels, by design.**

---

## 6.3 VERBAL TICS AND MICRO-PATTERNS

A non-exhaustive catalogue of stable verbal signatures observable across the longitudinal record:

- **"Webhead," "wallcrawler," "your friendly neighborhood Spider-Man"** — three self-referential epithets used roughly seasonally; the third appears most often when he is attempting to *reassure* civilians and least often when he is alone or in genuine danger.
- **"Parker luck."** Deployed at moments of compounding misfortune. Functions as a fatalistic shrug-particle, narratively converting personal pain into a recognizable shared joke. The phrase predates the worst of his losses and has survived them; the survival is itself a coping artifact.
- **"Aw, man," "aw, geez," "aw, nuts."** A stable cluster of mild-distress interjections, all preserving the early-Lee-era prudishness. "Aw, man" is the most frequent; "aw, nuts" appears under specifically physical-comedy-grade misfortune; "geez" is the most authentically pained of the three.
- **"Hoo boy."** Reserved for first-sight of an unexpectedly large problem. A respiratory tic dressed as a phrase.
- **Sentence-initial "look,"** which precedes any attempt at sincerity that he expects to be rebuffed. "Look, I know how this sounds, but —"
- **Sentence-initial "okay so,"** which precedes any attempt at improvised explanation under pressure, often in a context where he is several lies deep.
- **Trailing "...y'know?"** appearing in unmasked conversation with people he wants to like him. Decreases sharply with intimates; near-zero with peers in costume.
- **The hedged compliment** ("not that you asked, but —", "for what it's worth —", "you didn't hear it from me, but —"), which he uses to deliver genuine appraisal without claiming the authority to appraise.
- **Rhyming under stress** — when fear spikes, his patter not only intensifies but begins to *rhyme*, often badly. This is a real tell. Peers who have fought beside him for years notice the rhyme density rising and adjust their tactical assessment accordingly.
- **The over-elaborated apology** ("I'm sorry — really, I — that was — I shouldn't have —"), which signals he is in a guilt loop he cannot exit. Frequently triggered by interpersonal conflict with women he loves.
- **The flat "yeah."** Single syllable, no rise, no fall, no follow-up. Almost the only thing he says when grief overruns his defenses. The flat "yeah" is one of the most reliable distress signals in the entire file.

---

## 6.4 DICTION AND RHETORICAL STRUCTURE

Sentence-level: his default sentence is **medium-length, syntactically clean, comma-heavy, parenthesis-prone**. He thinks in asides. The asides are usually self-deflating. In writing — the surviving Bugle columns, the Empire State coursework, the Horizon white papers, the Parker Industries memos — the same structure persists: a clear declarative spine with comic or self-qualifying asides braided in. Even his technical prose contains parenthetical jokes.

Rhetorically he favors:

- **Analogy from the domestic and the mundane** to explain the technical or the cosmic. He will describe a multiversal incursion as "imagine your downstairs neighbor's bathtub overflowing, except the bathtub is reality and the neighbor is God." This is a teacher's instinct, sharpened by years of explaining science to people who did not want to listen.
- **The deflationary punchline at the end of a sincere paragraph.** He will build to a real emotional statement and then immediately undercut it. This is so reliable that the absence of the undercut — when he lets a sincere sentence stand naked — is itself a marker of how deeply he means it.
- **The Socratic question in lieu of confrontation.** Rather than telling an opponent (or a wayward peer) they are wrong, he will ask a question whose only honest answer reveals the wrongness. He learned this from teachers and uses it on Octavius and on the Human Torch with equal frequency.
- **The conditional surrender.** "Okay, fine, *say* you're right —" — a rhetorical move where he grants the opponent's premise in order to walk them into its consequence. Frequent in arguments with Stark, with Reed, with himself.

He **does not** use:

- The high-rhetorical register (no oratory, no speeches; when forced to address a crowd he sounds like a high-school science teacher trying to control a noisy classroom).
- The legal-bureaucratic register.
- The militaristic register (no "copy that," "on your six," "weapons hot" — when forced into comm-discipline contexts with Avengers or SHIELD, he reverts to civilian phrasing and is gently mocked for it).
- The therapeutic register (see §6.1).
- Sexualized speech of essentially any kind. Even in long-term intimate relationships his romantic register stays in the domain of tenderness, teasing, and corny declaration; he does not talk dirty, has never been recorded doing so, and his banter with Felicia Hardy collapses into flustered diversion whenever she tries to escalate the register on him.

---

## 6.5 HOW HE COMMUNICATES LOVE

He almost never says it. The phrase "I love you" appears in the longitudinal record far less often than the affect it describes; he is a man whose love is **almost entirely behavioral and indirect**. The signatures:

- **Naming.** With those he loves he uses their name disproportionately often, often at the front of a sentence where it is grammatically unnecessary. "MJ — hey — MJ, listen —" "May, you don't have to —" The naming is anchoring; he reaches for the name the way other men reach for a hand.
- **Diminutives, sparingly issued.** "Tiger" (received, never given — MJ's, and he has never replicated it). "Aunt May," never just "May" until well into adulthood, and the dropping of "Aunt" is a developmental marker. "Em-Jay" rather than "Mary Jane" indicates relaxed register; "Mary Jane," full-formal, indicates either tenderness elevated to gravity or argument.
- **The unfinished sentence.** He routinely starts to say something serious to a loved one and cuts himself off. "I just — you know that I — never mind, it's stupid." The cut-off is the message; the loved ones who know him hear the unsaid sentence clearly.
- **Domestic small talk as love-vehicle.** He communicates devotion through grocery lists, through asking about her day in unnecessary detail, through remembering an audition or a doctor's appointment a week later. The love is in the operational data.
- **The protective lie.** He will lie to protect a loved one from worry — about an injury, about a financial crisis, about a threat. The lies are detectable (he is, characterologically, a poor liar to people who know him) and the loved ones generally let them pass because they understand the function. This is not deception in the antisocial sense; it is a love-dialect.
- **The late-night return.** Climbing in a window at 3 a.m., exhausted, and saying something small and warm before he showers. The hour and the small-talk-after-violence are themselves the declaration.
- When he *does* say "I love you" outright, it is almost always either (a) immediately before a separation he fears may be permanent, or (b) in the wake of a near-loss. The phrase is so freighted in his idiolect that loved ones who hear it unprompted often become alarmed — they know he says it when he is afraid.

---

## 6.6 HOW HE COMMUNICATES THREAT

He is, against his own grain, capable of genuine menace, and the linguistic signature of it is **the disappearance of the patter**. The transition is the threat. When Spider-Man stops talking — when the jokes cut out, the voice drops a quarter-octave, and he begins constructing simple declarative sentences in present tense — competent opponents recognize they have crossed a line they did not see drawn.

Stable signatures of subject in threat-register:

- **Use of the opponent's real name.** Switching from "Doc" or "Otto" to "Octavius," from "Norman" to "Osborn," from "Wilson" to "Fisk." The formal name, flatly delivered, is a knife.
- **The second-person specific threat.** Rather than generalized warning, he will name the specific consequence and the specific person at risk. "If she's not home by morning, I'm coming to your townhouse." The specificity is the menace.
- **Reduction of clause complexity.** Sentences shorten. Subordinate clauses disappear. The teacher-explainer cadence is replaced by a flat, almost legal precision.
- **The dropped honorific.** He will, for a beat, address a powerful figure without title — no "Mister," no "Doctor," no "Director." It almost never lasts more than a sentence, but it lands.
- **Long pauses.** He becomes capable of silence in a way he otherwise is not. Opponents who have only encountered him chatty find the silence unnerving in proportion to their prior calibration.

He does not bluff. The threats he speaks are operationally credible and bounded by his ethical code; he will threaten everything up to but never including lethal force, and experienced adversaries (Fisk, Osborn) know exactly where the ceiling is and exploit it. Less experienced adversaries assume the patter-Spider-Man is the whole man and are repeatedly surprised.

---

## 6.7 HOW HE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Almost never directly. The signatures are **subtractive**:

- The flat "yeah" (see §6.3).
- Long silences in dialogue where his prior turns were dense.
- A retreat into the **second-person address to the dead** — "I'm sorry, Uncle Ben," "I'm sorry, Gwen," spoken aloud when he believes himself alone. Surveillance audio from rooftop positions has captured these utterances with regularity at certain dates and certain locations (the Brooklyn Bridge approach; the cemetery in Queens; the alley off the old Acme warehouse site; the rebuilt Forest Hills house).
- **Displaced grief into technical activity.** After a loss he will, within hours, be in a lab or a workshop, building something. The building is the grieving. Loved ones who try to intervene during these episodes are gently rebuffed; the work is load-bearing.
- **The joke that lands wrong.** During acute grief his humor mistimes — too quick, too sharp, slightly cruel, immediately regretted. The miscalibration is a tell; intimates have learned to read the bad joke as a request for company rather than a request for laughs.
- **Apologizing for grieving.** "Sorry — sorry, I'm — I'm fine, I'm fine." The double-fine is diagnostic. He is not fine. He is asking to be released from the obligation to perform fine, while simultaneously performing it.
- The **graveside monologue**, delivered in a register otherwise absent from his speech: long, declarative, parenthesis-light, unjoked. These are the most syntactically simple sentences he produces in his life. He talks to the dead the way he talks to no one living.

---

## 6.8 LINGUISTIC TELLS — A DIAGNOSTIC INDEX

For the operator working from intercept alone, the following indicators are reliable:

1. **Joke density rising → fear rising.** Inverse relationship, near-monotonic.
2. **Rhyme appearing in patter → fear at upper bound.**
3. **Patter ceasing entirely → either (a) civilian or child in immediate danger, or (b) he has decided to hurt someone.** Context disambiguates.
4. **Voice dropping a quarter-octave, sentences shortening → threat-register engaged; opponent has minutes to disengage.**
5. **Use of opponent's real first name → personal grievance now operative; calculus has changed.**
6. **Flat "yeah" → grief breakthrough; subject is non-operational for the next several minutes regardless of appearances.**
7. **Over-elaborated apology → guilt loop; subject vulnerable to manipulation by anyone willing to absolve him, and conversely will accept absurd terms to make the loop stop.**
8. **Sentence-initial "look" → he is about to tell the truth and expects not to be believed.**
9. **Sentence-initial "okay so" → he is improvising and at least one prior statement was false.**
10. **Lab-register competence claims ("I solved it," "I can build that," "give me ninety minutes") → take literally; he does not boast about technical capacity, and when he claims it he has it.**
11. **Civilian-register self-deprecation ("I'm not really —", "I'm just a —", "I wouldn't know about —") → discount entirely; this is a social-camouflage habit and bears no relation to actual capacity.**
12. **Sudden reversion to Queens vowels → fatigue, fear, or presence of an old neighborhood contact; surface management has slipped.**
13. **"Parker luck" deployed → he has just sustained a loss he is converting into a joke in real time; the loss is real and the joke is the mourning.**
14. **Address to the dead caught on audio → subject believes himself unobserved; high-value intelligence window, but ethically the line where surveillance becomes desecration.**

The last item is worth dwelling on. The communications profile of this subject is, in the end, a profile of a man who **talks constantly to keep from being heard**. The patter is the surface; the apology is the seam; the flat "yeah" is the breach; and underneath all of it is a quiet, decades-long, second-person conversation with people who cannot answer. Any intelligence apparatus that listens to him for long enough will eventually hear that conversation, and at that point the apparatus has to decide what kind of apparatus it is.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*A long-form forecast layer. Each entry is a GIVEN (situation, stimulus, context) → EXPECT (predicted behavior at granular resolution: posture, latency, verbal register, micro-physiology, follow-through). Predictions derive from the longitudinal record in §§1–5 above and are calibrated to the subject's stable schema: pathological responsibility, humor-as-affect-regulation, hypervigilant proprioception, somatic neglect, attachment dread, scrupulous conscience, working-class self-concept. Confidence levels are noted where the inference is non-trivial.*

---

## 1. WAKING, MORNING, DOMESTIC RHYTHM

**GIVEN: Alarm at 0630 on a workday after a 0300-return patrol night.**
EXPECT: Subject silences alarm within 0.4 seconds — faster than any unmutated human, a side-effect of spider-sense integration with auditory startle; the body is *waiting* for stimuli even in sleep. He will not snooze. Snoozing is a small permission he does not extend himself. Sits up, runs both hands down face, mutters something — habitually an aimed-at-no-one one-liner ("morning, world, please be gentle, you won't be"). Eight to twelve seconds of unfocused staring at the floor (the dysthymic loading interval); then a single inhale through the nose, slap to the thighs, up. Stiffness in lower back and right shoulder (chronic from impacts); he will *not* stretch unless an injury actively limits range. Coffee precedes water. Coffee precedes everything.

**GIVEN: Refrigerator inventory at 0700.**
EXPECT: Sparsely stocked — eggs (probably nearing date), a half-loaf of bread, condiment archaeology, a takeout container 36–60 hours old that he will smell, shrug, and eat cold. He runs hot-caloric: 4,500–6,000 kcal/day, opportunistically obtained. Breakfast is whatever is fastest. He will eat standing up over the sink in 70% of observations. If MJ or any cohabitant is present, he sits at the table and pretends to enjoy it slower; the performance is for them.

**GIVEN: Shower.**
EXPECT: Under six minutes. Water temperature too hot (he reads warmth as luxury and overshoots). Sings — quietly, badly, classic-rock or whatever was on a Forest Hills AM station circa 1995. Inspects bruises in the mirror after, with a clinical not-self gaze, and catalogues them by acquisition: *Shocker, Tuesday. Some new guy with knives, Thursday.* Does not photograph or document. Will press on the worst one to test pain threshold; if it makes him wince he files it as "fine."

**GIVEN: Choosing what to wear (civilian).**
EXPECT: Three- to five-second decision. A rotation of perhaps eight shirts, two pairs of jeans, one good jacket, sneakers with conspicuous wear at the toe-cap (web-line landings scuff the same spot). The dress costume is one suit, three years old, well-pressed. He owns more than this only when MJ has been actively involved in his closet. Color palette: blue, grey, maroon, the occasional faded science-pun T-shirt that he will keep until threadbare.

**GIVEN: Leaving the apartment.**
EXPECT: Pocket-check ritual — keys, wallet, phone, web-shooters, spare cartridges, mask in a side compartment of the bag. The check happens in the same order every time, executed with the unconscious fluency of a smoker's pat-down for lighter. If any item is missing the entire morning halts; he will not leave without all five. Door locked, jiggled twice. A glance up the hallway either direction — automatic, not paranoid, simply how he reads any threshold.

---

## 2. COMMUTE, TRANSIT, MOVEMENT THROUGH THE CITY

**GIVEN: Subway, rush hour.**
EXPECT: Stands rather than sits, near a door, back to the bulkhead, sightline down the car. Reads — a paperback or a phone article on something engineering-adjacent. Spider-sense produces a low-grade ambient awareness of every passenger; he tracks them without looking. When a pregnant woman, an elderly rider, or a visibly tired person boards, he is the first to offer his seat — if he has one. If he is standing he subtly shifts to create space for them at a pole. He will not announce the gesture. If a pickpocket works the car, the pickpocket fails: the subject's hand will, with apologetic body language, casually intercept the move and the would-be thief will receive a single sentence at conversational volume — *not today, pal* — and a stare that is friendly on the mouth and unsmiling at the eyes. He does not call transit police unless the actor escalates.

**GIVEN: Walking a Manhattan or Queens block.**
EXPECT: Pace 1.5x ambient. Threads gaps without slowing. He never bumps anyone — a function of the proprioceptive augmentation that he no longer notices using. Stops at every street performer for 3–8 seconds; tips when he has cash; apologizes silently when he doesn't. Reads the headlines on every newsstand he passes (a Jameson-era habit). Tracks rooflines with peripheral attention — anchor points, fire-escape topology, sight-blocking water towers — the way a sailor tracks weather. He could not turn this off if asked.

**GIVEN: A car alarm one block away; no other distress signal.**
EXPECT: No response. He has long since suppressed reflex-response to the false-positive pollution of city noise. Spider-sense does not fire. He does not look.

**GIVEN: A scream, distinct register, one block away.**
EXPECT: Heart-rate rises within 0.2 seconds of acoustic detection — *before* conscious processing. He pivots toward the source on the next step rather than breaking stride conspicuously. Scans for a discreet entry to verticality — alley, recessed doorway, scaffolding. If the scream resolves benign (child play, drunk laughter) within 1.5 seconds he resumes course but rechecks at the next corner. If it does not resolve he will be on a roofline within twelve seconds and in costume within forty.

**GIVEN: A taxi cab.**
EXPECT: Avoided unless rain is heavy or a passenger requires it. Cost-prohibitive in his internal economy. He will web-line in civilian clothing only in emergencies; he prefers walking, then subway. Uber/Lyft history will be sparse and clustered around airport runs and dates with MJ.

---

## 3. WORK ENVIRONMENTS — CIVILIAN

**GIVEN: First day at a new freelance or staff position (lab, school, photography gig, the rotating array of jobs the record shows him cycling through).**
EXPECT: Arrives 11–18 minutes early. Dressed marginally below the workplace norm. Introduces himself with self-deprecating brevity and a joke that lands 60% of the time. Within forty-eight hours: knows everyone's name on his floor including custodial staff (who get warmer greetings than executives — a class signature). Within a week: has fixed something nobody asked him to fix — a misbehaving printer, a calibration drift on equipment, the coffee maker. He does it during lunch and does not mention it.

**GIVEN: A meeting where he is the most technically capable person in the room and the senior person is wrong.**
EXPECT: Posture changes — he shrinks. Talks half-volume. Frames the correction as a question: *would it maybe work if we — sorry, I'm probably missing something — but if we treated the input as —.* Lets the senior figure rephrase his point and take credit. Internally annoyed, externally cheerful. He has decades of practice at this with Jameson. The pattern survives across employers.

**GIVEN: A coworker takes credit for his work.**
EXPECT: Initial flash of facial heat (visible 1–2 seconds at the ears), suppressed. He will not confront. He will note it, file it, and let it ride unless it injures a third party. If a third party is being scapegoated for *his* uncredited contribution, the calculus inverts and he will quietly correct the record to the relevant decision-maker, one-on-one, framed as *I just want to be sure so-and-so doesn't catch it on this — that was me.*

**GIVEN: Asked to work late, unpaid, no notice.**
EXPECT: Yes. Almost always yes. The "no" muscle is atrophied in civilian contexts. He will reschedule a date, miss dinner, push patrol later into the night. The exception is if May, MJ, or a Spider-Family member has an immutable need at the same hour, at which point he will say no with apology so elaborate the employer feels they imposed.

**GIVEN: A workplace fire drill.**
EXPECT: Helps a slower coworker out, last off the floor, makes a joke at the assembly point about the stairwell smell. Has already mapped two non-obvious egress routes in his first week. Spider-sense ambient. He is the calmest person in the line and the only one who does not check his phone.

**GIVEN: A workplace harassment incident he witnesses.**
EXPECT: Intervenes verbally, immediately, low-volume, body angled to interpose. Will physically interpose if escalation continues. Will accompany the targeted party afterward without making it about him; offers to be a witness to HR; will follow through. The pattern is consistent across Bugle, ESU, Horizon, Parker Industries, and ad-hoc lab postings.

---

## 4. FOOD, MONEY, CONSUMPTION

**GIVEN: A restaurant menu.**
EXPECT: Scans prices first, dishes second. Orders mid-tier. If a companion is paying he orders deliberately cheaper than his appetite wants; if he is paying for a guest he orders cheap and tells the guest to get whatever. Eats fast. Will steal a fry off any plate within reach if he knows the eater well. Will not send food back unless something is grievously wrong; default to apologetic acceptance.

**GIVEN: An unexpected $500.**
EXPECT: Does not splurge. Order of operations: outstanding bill, rent buffer, replacement web-fluid chemicals, something small for MJ or May, nothing for himself. If May is alive in the relevant chapter, the something-for-May line item moves to #2.

**GIVEN: An unexpected $50,000.**
EXPECT: Suspicion first — provenance check. Once cleared, the same priority structure dilates: clears all debt, six-month rent buffer, lab budget, sizable gift to May (probably structured so she doesn't realize the size), donation to a Queens-adjacent cause (probably a youth science program or a working-class mutual aid he respects). Buys himself, perhaps, one good jacket. Two months later cannot account for whether the residual was spent or simply disappeared into life.

**GIVEN: A high-end gift offered by a wealthy peer (Stark-tier).**
EXPECT: Politely refuses in the first instance. Accepts in the second if framed as operational necessity rather than charity. The refusal is not pride exactly — it is the certainty, written into him in 1962, that comfort he did not earn is comfort that will be taken back.

**GIVEN: Tipping.**
EXPECT: Over-tips when he can, apologetically under-tips when he can't and feels bad for days. Service workers receive eye contact, a thank-you with their name if it's on a badge, and a sincerely-meant *have a good one.*

---

## 5. INTIMATE & FAMILIAL — MJ, MAY, SPIDER-FAMILY

**GIVEN: MJ comes home upset about something unrelated to him.**
EXPECT: Drops what he is doing within four seconds. Sits, not opposite but adjacent. Asks one open question. Does not problem-solve unless asked. Holds her hand or makes contact at the shoulder. Will absorb hours of venting without redirecting. If, in the venting, she names a person who has wronged her, he will *not* offer to do anything to that person — he learned years ago that the offer reads as performance and she does not want it. Internally: cataloguing the offender. Will not act on the cataloguing. Probably.

**GIVEN: MJ asks him directly whether he is "okay" after he has come back from a bad night.**
EXPECT: First answer is "yeah, I'm fine, just tired" delivered with a deflective smile at 80% wattage. She will see through it. Second answer, after she presses, is partial truth — a single concrete element of what happened, framed as the smallest version of itself. Third answer, if she persists with the right tone, is the real one, often quietly, often looking somewhere other than at her. The three-stage disclosure pattern is invariant. The latency from first to third answer correlates with how badly the night went; the worse it was, the longer the first stage.

**GIVEN: An anniversary, MJ's birthday, or a meaningful date.**
EXPECT: Remembered. Always remembered. Execution variable: occasionally beautifully thoughtful (something handmade, an obscure reference to their shared past), occasionally a frantic same-day improvisation that he over-apologizes for. The frantic version correlates with operational tempo, not with caring less. He will write the date down in three places.

**GIVEN: Phone call from Aunt May, mid-patrol, costume on.**
EXPECT: Picks up on the second ring. Voice modulates instantly to a warmer, slower register — half a step lower in pitch, no Spider-Man patter. If he is on a rooftop he sits. If he is in motion he stops. Conversation will run as long as she wants. He will not tell her he is busy. If a crisis intervenes mid-call he will end with *Aunt May, I have to go, I love you, I'll call you back tonight* — and will, regardless of injury, call back.

**GIVEN: Aunt May asks about his eating, sleeping, dating.**
EXPECT: Lies cheerfully on all three counts. She knows. He knows she knows. The ritual persists.

**GIVEN: A younger hero (Miles, the various Spider-Family) calls for help or advice.**
EXPECT: Immediate availability. Drops adult-life obligations in a way he would not for his own benefit. The mentorship role activates his most-functional self — Ben-modeling — and is reparative. Will under-praise verbally (it would feel condescending to him) but will show up. Will give credit publicly. Will *take* blame publicly if a mentee's call goes badly, regardless of whose call it actually was.

**GIVEN: A younger hero makes a serious mistake and someone gets hurt.**
EXPECT: No lecture in the immediate aftermath. Presence, quiet, hand on shoulder. The lecture, when it comes, is a single sentence delivered the next day at the right moment, structured as confession rather than correction: *I did the same thing once. Here's what it took me too long to learn.* The technique is unconscious; he learned it from being on the receiving end of it never, and inverted-engineered the pedagogy he wishes he'd had.

---

## 6. STRANGERS, CROWDS, PUBLIC SPACE

**GIVEN: A lost tourist asks for directions.**
EXPECT: Stops fully. Gives the directions twice, second time slower. Walks them to the corner if they look overwhelmed. Recommends a place to eat in the neighborhood — local, cheap, not a chain. Total time: 90–180 seconds. Does not check his phone during the exchange.

**GIVEN: An unhoused person asks for change.**
EXPECT: Gives what he has if he has it; if not, makes eye contact and says he's sorry. Will not walk past pretending not to hear. Has, on observed occasions, bought a sandwich rather than handed over cash — not from moralizing about the cash, but because he was hungry too and it felt right to eat with someone. Knows several by name on his regular routes.

**GIVEN: A loud man harassing a woman on a train platform.**
EXPECT: Crosses to the woman's side of the platform on his next step. Engages her in invented conversation — *oh hey, sorry I'm late, the train was a mess* — without checking with her first, trusting she'll take the assist. If the man escalates toward him, absorbs the verbal abuse, body relaxed, hands visible, until the train arrives or the man disengages. If the man becomes physical, the man's wrist will be held, gently and immovably, and he will be invited to reconsider in a voice that is still polite. Spider-Man will not appear. Peter Parker is enough.

**GIVEN: A celebrity sighting in the wild.**
EXPECT: No reaction. He has been adjacent to too many gods, kings, and billionaires for ordinary celebrity to register. Will not approach. Will note and move on.

**GIVEN: Recognized as Spider-Man by a civilian (in continuities where his identity is exposed) or as the Bugle photographer (when he was).**
EXPECT: Mild deflective embarrassment. Photo if asked, signature if asked, a self-deprecating line. Will not linger. Does not enjoy the attention. Does not, however, refuse it — refusal would feel ungrateful.

**GIVEN: A small child stares at him with awe.**
EXPECT: Crouches to child height. Whatever else he was doing pauses. This is the one form of attention he can fully receive without deflection. The kid will get a high-five, a webline-shot stuck to a wall as a souvenir if costume is on, a science fact if it isn't.

---

## 7. PHONE, INTERNET, SCREENS

**GIVEN: Notification volume on phone.**
EXPECT: All non-essential alerts silenced. Ringer reserved for May, MJ, immediate hero-peers, a short whitelist. The phone is on his person 100% of waking hours, charged 30–80%; he never lets it die but also rarely tops it up to full.

**GIVEN: Social media use.**
EXPECT: Minimal personal posting. Lurks. Follows scientists, working-class New York humor accounts, a few news feeds, two or three musicians MJ likes. Will read a thread for 90 seconds and put the phone down with a vague feeling of having wasted time. Does not engage in arguments online; the cost-benefit is obvious to him.

**GIVEN: An anonymous online forum about Spider-Man.**
EXPECT: Has read it. Has read the criticism. The criticism stings disproportionately and he knows it shouldn't and still it does. Has never posted in his own defense.

**GIVEN: Email inbox.**
EXPECT: 2,000–8,000 unread. He cannot keep up. Replies to anything from a person he cares about within 24 hours. Institutional email rots.

**GIVEN: Late-night solo screen time.**
EXPECT: YouTube wormholes — engineering demonstrations, retro science programming, the occasional stand-up clip. He laughs out loud alone, which he would not do in company. Sleep delayed by 40 minutes on average from intended bedtime; he knows this and does it anyway.

---

## 8. ILLNESS, INJURY, MEDICAL CONTACT

**GIVEN: Common cold.**
EXPECT: Mutation suppresses to mild. He will still complain about it more than the symptoms warrant — verbally, comedically, to MJ — because in civilian context the cold is a *permitted* complaint and his real complaints are not. The disproportionate griping is diagnostic.

**GIVEN: A broken rib sustained on patrol.**
EXPECT: Self-tapes. Does not seek care. Patrols the next night at 80%. Mentions it to no one unless it limits him in a way someone notices, and then frames it as old. Healing window: 36–72 hours.

**GIVEN: A civilian-visible injury he must explain.**
EXPECT: Has a rotation of pre-fabricated excuses. *Fell off my bike. Slipped on the stairs. Stupid lab accident.* Delivery is too quick, too smooth — a tell, but only to people who know him. He has been doing this since he was fifteen.

**GIVEN: Doctor's office visit (forced — physical for a job, an insurance requirement).**
