EXPECT: Acute anxiety, well-masked. He cannot let bloodwork happen without considering whether it will reveal the mutation. Has, in canon and inference, used cover identities or talked his way out of specific tests. The visit will be efficient, polite, and abbreviated.

**GIVEN: Therapy referral.**
EXPECT: Will not go. Will agree to go. Will not go. The conflict between conscience (it is wise; he should) and structure (he cannot disclose the load-bearing facts of his life to a stranger; the secret cost would be catastrophic) resolves consistently in non-attendance. He has rationalized this for decades.

---

## 9. SLEEP, DREAMS, NIGHT

**GIVEN: Bedtime, no patrol obligation.**
EXPECT: Intends 2300. Achieves 0040. The intervening hours: tinkering, a podcast, a book, the YouTube hole, an apologetic text to someone he forgot to reply to. Falls asleep within 4 minutes of lights-out — the chronic deficit produces sleep latency near zero.

**GIVEN: Dreams.**
EXPECT: Recurrent themes — falling and *not catching*; reaching and missing; an alley, a streetlight, a figure on the ground; a bridge, water below, a snapping sound. The dreams do not narrativize cleanly; they replay textures. He wakes from the bad ones with controlled breath (a skill) and is back in functional waking state within 60 seconds. Does not journal. Does not discuss.

**GIVEN: Co-sleeping with MJ.**
EXPECT: Sleeps better. Measurably. The spider-sense does not register her as threat, and her breathing entrains his. Wakes earlier than her invariably; will lie still rather than disturb her; the lying-still is one of his daily meditations even though he wouldn't call it that.

---

## 10. CONFLICT, ARGUMENT, ANGER (CIVILIAN)

**GIVEN: A verbal argument with a loved one.**
EXPECT: Tries humor first (often misjudges; deflects when sincerity is wanted). When called on the deflection, drops it, goes quiet, listens. Apologizes early and often, sometimes for things that are not his fault — a pattern MJ has, across multiple eras, told him to stop. He cannot stop. The over-apology is structural.

**GIVEN: An argument with a stranger (parking, line-cut, perceived rudeness).**
EXPECT: De-escalates immediately. The stakes are nothing to him relative to the stakes he carries; he cannot summon the energy to care about the slight. Will sometimes apologize when he was the one wronged, just to end the exchange.

**GIVEN: Genuine anger triggered (someone hurt a vulnerable person in front of him).**
EXPECT: Voice drops half an octave. Goes very quiet. Words become precise and short. This is the rare register he does not joke through. The civilian version of this is rare and unmistakable; people who have seen it remember it.

---

## 11. RITUALS, HABITS, MICRO-PATTERNS

- **The Forest Hills detour.** When in Queens, will route past the old house, the cemetery, or the Acme Warehouse coordinates with a frequency higher than


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Section 11 of the dossier. High-load behavioral forecasting. Each entry is a conditional: a GIVEN (situational input) yielding an EXPECT (the predicted behavioral, somatic, verbal, and cognitive output). Derived from sixty-plus years of consistent decompensation patterns. Reliabilities are estimated against the longitudinal record; "high" indicates a pattern that recurs across writers and eras; "moderate" indicates a pattern present but variable in expression; "context-conditional" indicates a fork the subject will resolve along predictable lines depending on a named auxiliary variable.*

---

## 11.1 — THE FAMILIAR CRISIS GRAMMAR (BASELINE STRESSORS)

These are the operational stressors the subject has metabolized into a working routine. He decompensates only marginally; the system holds.

**GIVEN: a multi-front engagement — civilians in immediate danger AND a known antagonist AND a non-superhuman bystander injury already occurring.**
EXPECT: triage to the civilian/bystander vector first, antagonist second. He will physically interpose his own body between projectile/structural hazard and the noncombatant before he engages the source of the hazard. Verbal output during the interpose: a deflective quip directed at the antagonist, *not* a reassurance directed at the civilian — the quip's actual function is to draw the antagonist's targeting cone onto himself. Reliability: very high. He has done this so consistently it is essentially a reflex arc; the spider-sense is integrated with a triage heuristic that ranks "stranger I have never met" above "self" by default.

**GIVEN: outnumbered (three or more competent hostiles), no immediate civilian load, retreat is tactically available.**
EXPECT: he does not retreat. He restructures the environment — pulls a fire escape down, webs a sightline, drops the lighting, uses verticality. The patter intensifies; jokes accelerate to roughly one per 4–6 seconds, a tempo measurably higher than his social baseline. The acceleration is a self-monitoring tell: he is regulating fear by talking. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: opponent has clearly superior raw power (Juggernaut-class, Rhino-class, Hulk-class on a bad day).**
EXPECT: structural engineering replaces direct engagement. He moves the fight to a location where the opponent's mass is a liability — wet cement, water, a partially-demolished structure. He will take repeated hits to buy seconds for the environment to do the work. Pain response is suppressed verbally; he will joke through fractured ribs. Reliability: very high. (Behavioral prototype: ASM #229–230.)

**GIVEN: a financial deadline (rent, May's medication historically, a bill cycle) coincides with a patrol-night emergency.**
EXPECT: the patrol wins. The civilian obligation is deferred; the financial penalty is absorbed silently and later catastrophized in private. He will eat a late-fee, a missed shift, or a fired-from-the-gig before he will hand off the emergency. He does not experience this as a choice; the patrol vector is functionally non-optional. Reliability: very high.

---

## 11.2 — THE WOUND ITSELF (CONTACT WITH THE ORIGINATING SCHEMA)

These are the inputs that touch the Ben/Gwen substrate directly. Predictions sharpen and behavior narrows.

**GIVEN: a male civilian, plausibly father-coded (working-class, kind, attached to a younger relative), is injured or killed in his proximity.**
EXPECT: a perceptible micro-freeze of 0.5–1.5 seconds at the moment of recognition (the body-shape, the demographic, the way the victim falls). Spider-sense will register but the conscious processing layer will lag — the only context in which his reaction time degrades. Following recovery: disproportionate post-event behavior. He will return to the location repeatedly over subsequent nights, attempt to locate surviving family, anonymously fund expenses if able, and integrate the loss into his pre-sleep rumination set for weeks. He will not name to anyone *why* this victim hit harder than others. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: a young woman he is romantically or proto-romantically attached to is taken hostage at altitude, on a bridge, or in any falling-vector scenario.**
EXPECT: full Gwen-resonance activation. Combat decision-making degrades along a specific axis: he will refuse webline-catch solutions and seek a physical-intercept solution even when slower and tactically inferior. The refusal is not conscious — it is the body's veto on a movement pattern it has encoded as lethal. If forced to webline-catch, his hands will be measurably less steady for the next 24–72 hours; gripping fine objects (coffee cup, web-shooter cartridge change) shows tremor. Reliability: very high. The Gwen schema is the most deeply consolidated trauma circuit in the record.

**GIVEN: a hostage situation in which the antagonist offers the trade — "the hostage for the mask," or "the hostage for your surrender."**
EXPECT: he accepts the surface terms while constructing a tactical defection in the same breath. He will not refuse the trade; refusing the trade re-encodes as the Burglar moment. He buys time with compliance and then breaks the trade only after the hostage's vector clears. If the trade cannot be broken without hostage cost, he absorbs the surrender. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: an antagonist explicitly invokes Uncle Ben by name.**
EXPECT: the patter stops. This is one of the few inputs that reliably silences him mid-fight. The silence lasts 2–6 seconds and is followed by a notable escalation in force application — still short of lethal, but at the upper boundary of what he permits himself. He will not engage the bait verbally; the silence is the entire response. Post-event, he will lose at least one night's sleep. Reliability: very high. Antagonists who have learned this (Norman Osborn in his more lucid villain phases; Kindred) have weaponized it.

**GIVEN: an antagonist explicitly invokes Gwen Stacy by name.**
EXPECT: a different and more dangerous reaction than the Ben-name response. He goes verbally hot rather than silent — a brief, uncharacteristically venomous line, often a single sentence — and then over-corrects into rigid de-escalation, because he has felt the rage move and is now afraid of it. Combat becomes tighter, more economical, more clinical. The transition from rage-glimpse to clinical mode is the diagnostic signature. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: a young woman in his sustained care (a teenage hero, a niece-equivalent, a mentee in the Spider-Family configurations) is injured on a mission he sanctioned.**
EXPECT: immediate medical triage, then a self-removal pattern. He will pull back from the mentorship role for a period (days to weeks), citing logistics; the actual driver is the conviction that proximity to him is the hazard. The mentee will have to pursue him to restore the relationship — which is itself part of his unconscious test of whether the attachment can survive his withdrawal. Reliability: high. This is the Gwen schema generalized to the caregiving direction.

**GIVEN: May Parker is hospitalized, missing, or under acute threat.**
EXPECT: all other obligations are suspended without negotiation, including team obligations, civilian relationships, and ongoing crises he had been managing. He will not sleep until the threat resolves. He will accept bargains he would refuse for any other stake — this is the lesson of the Mephisto trade, regardless of one's metaphysical reading of it. He will lie to peers about why he is unavailable rather than disclose her condition, because disclosure feels like exposing her to further attack vectors. Reliability: very high, near-deterministic.

---

## 11.3 — BETRAYAL VECTORS

The subject's response to betrayal is structured by who is betraying him and along which axis. He does not have a single betrayal-response; he has several, sortable by relational class.

**GIVEN: betrayal by an institutional actor (a government agency, a corporate sponsor, a registration regime).**
EXPECT: rapid recalibration with low affective cost. He has a stable prior that institutions betray; the betrayal confirms rather than wounds. Response is operational — extract, expose if exposure serves the vulnerable, sever. He will not seek revenge against the institution as such; he will pursue the specific individual who weaponized the institution against a person he was protecting. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: betrayal by a peer-hero whom he had not deeply trusted (an acquaintance-grade Avenger, a one-mission ally).**
EXPECT: contained anger, a sharp verbal exchange, professional severance. He will work with them again if a future crisis requires it, but the prior is updated and the wit toward them becomes thinner and harder. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: betrayal by a peer-hero he had positioned as a mentor or surrogate paternal figure (the Stark-class relationship).**
EXPECT: catastrophic disproportionate response. The betrayal touches a schema he has not catalogued — the under-articulated longing for the father he lost before memory and the uncle he lost in adolescence. He will defect publicly and at high personal cost. He will subsequently ruminate not on the betrayer's failure but on his *own* failure to have seen it coming, framing the entire history of the relationship as a misjudgment he was responsible for. The grief is processed as self-indictment. Reliability: high. (Behavioral prototype: post-Civil-War defection.)

**GIVEN: betrayal by a long-term close friend (Harry-class).**
EXPECT: no defensive hardening. He will continue to extend the relationship past the point peers consider reasonable, will accept repeated re-betrayals, and will absorb the cost. The Osborn line — Norman, Harry, the various legacy iterations — has hurt him more times than any other vector in the record, and he has never structurally withdrawn from it. The pattern is sustained by a conviction that abandoning a friend in psychiatric crisis is what a worse version of him would do. Reliability: very high. This is the most reliably exploitable trust vector in his entire interpersonal field.

**GIVEN: betrayal by a romantic partner (infidelity, deception about identity, alignment with an antagonist).**
EXPECT: the response is not anger but a quiet, internalized assumption that he caused it — that something he failed to provide drove the partner to the betrayal. He will end the relationship and behave correctly toward the partner subsequently, but the betrayal joins his guilt-ledger as evidence of his unsuitability for intimacy, feeding the next cycle's pre-emptive withdrawal. Reliability: moderate-to-high; varies with writer but the underlying tendency is consistent.

**GIVEN: betrayal by his own body (mutation flare, power loss, possession, symbiote-class autonomy override).**
EXPECT: the most severe class of response in the entire schema. The body is the instrument by which he discharges the responsibility debt; a body that acts against his will threatens the entire moral architecture. He will isolate, refuse contact with loved ones until the issue is resolved, and pursue resolution at any somatic cost. He will not accept reassurance during this state; reassurance is heard as a misunderstanding of the actual stakes. Reliability: very high. (Behavioral prototypes: symbiote rejection sequence; Superior return; organic-shooter mutation period.)

**GIVEN: betrayal by an antagonist he had extended provisional trust to during a forced alliance (Octavius, Connors, Marko in their better phases).**
EXPECT: less surprise than peers expect, less anger than peers expect, and a sad, slightly tired acceptance — the prior was already low. The wound is small; the disappointment is large; the structural lesson is not learned, and he will extend the same provisional trust to the same class of antagonist next time. Reliability: high. This is not naïveté; it is a conviction that the alternative — preemptive distrust — is the worse error.

---

## 11.4 — TEMPTATION VECTORS

The subject's temptation profile is unusual: he is largely immune to the standard inducements (wealth, fame, sex, power) and acutely vulnerable to a small set of unconventional ones.

**GIVEN: an offer of significant wealth, conditional on a moral compromise (corporate sponsorship with strings, a payout for silence, monetized identity).**
EXPECT: refusal, with mild regret about the lost financial relief and no genuine internal conflict. The compromise vector is too legible. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: an offer of public adulation, official recognition, or institutional rank.**
EXPECT: deflection through humor, polite refusal, mild embarrassment. He does not want this and reads requests for it as a category error about who he is. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: an offer of an emotionally-available adult romantic partnership that requires he disclose his identity and accept ordinary stability.**
EXPECT: this is the temptation that actually destabilizes him. He wants it and does not believe he is permitted to have it. He will move toward it; at the threshold, a previously-manageable patrol crisis will be allowed to expand into a reason for postponement. The sabotage is unconscious. If the partner persists through several cycles of this, the relationship can stabilize — MJ at her best has done this — but the default trajectory bends toward attrition. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: an offer of relief from the responsibility itself — a credible promise that "you can stop now; others will carry it."**
EXPECT: he listens longer than peers expect. The fatigue is real and chronically denied; an external permission slip for rest activates it. He will not, however, accept the offer in any sustained form. The brief period of the Ben Reilly handoff is the upper-bound case: a few weeks of genuine attempt, collapsed by the first crisis that reached his door. Reliability: high. The temptation is real; the schema's veto is stronger.

**GIVEN: an offer of restoration of a specific lost person (Ben, Gwen, Harry, a parental figure) via morally ambiguous means.**
EXPECT: the most dangerous temptation in his inventory. He will not refuse cleanly. He will engage, investigate, attempt to find a way to accept that does not violate his code, and the longer the investigation runs the more rationalization accrues. He will eventually refuse if the cost is borne by another; he will accept if the cost is borne by himself, which is exactly the lever sophisticated antagonists use. Reliability: high. (Behavioral prototypes: the Mephisto bargain regardless of metaphysical reading; multiple lesser arcs with resurrection or restoration motifs.)

**GIVEN: an offer of certainty — a credible voice telling him "the death was not your fault."**
EXPECT: he cannot metabolize it. He will thank the speaker, deflect, and return to the prior belief within hours. The schema has rejected this input from every source — May, MJ, the Stacys, peers — across decades. Reliability: very high. He does not want absolution; absolution would dismantle the architecture.

**GIVEN: an offer to kill the antagonist responsible for a fresh loss, when the killing would be technically defensible and operationally easy.**
EXPECT: he refuses, but the refusal has a quality of effort visible to close observers. The line holds because he believes that crossing it once collapses the entire system — not for moral-philosophical reasons but for practical-architectural ones; he knows what is inside him. Reliability: very high. The few instances in the record where the line was approached (Kraven aftermath; certain Goblin sequences) were followed by extended periods of withdrawal and self-examination.

---

## 11.5 — DECOMPENSATION EDGE (THE STATES PAST WHICH THE SYSTEM YIELDS)

The subject is high-functioning under extraordinary load. The system does have failure modes; they are predictable.

**GIVEN: cumulative sleep deprivation exceeding ~72 hours combined with an unresolved acute loss.**
EXPECT: the humor thins to bitterness, then disappears. Combat economy improves at the cost of restraint; he will hit harder and more economically, with less margin for opponent recovery. Verbal exchanges with civilians become curt. He will refuse meals offered by loved ones. This is the state in which a single triggering input can produce the rage breakthrough; the breakthrough is brief (seconds to a minute) and is followed by acute self-disgust, often a self-imposed exile from the cape for 24–72 hours, and ruminative penance behavior. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: a loss that he reads as caused by his own action (not omission but action — the Gwen-class wound).**
EXPECT: the most severe class of decompensation. Initial 24–48 hours: dissociative numbness, robotic functioning, refusal of consolation. Days 3–14: depressive collapse, withdrawal from patrol, fragmented sleep with intrusive imagery, somatic complaints, weight loss. Weeks 2–8: gradual return to function via the only mechanism that has ever worked — pouring the unmetabolized affect back into the role, framed as honoring the lost. He will not seek clinical help. He will accept the company of one or two trusted intimates without speaking about the event for long periods. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: a forced loss of agency over his own body lasting more than minutes (possession, mind-control, restraint-with-witness).**
EXPECT: post-event, a multi-week vigilance pattern around bodily autonomy. Sleep degrades further. He will refuse touch, even from intimates, for a period. He will obsessively rehearse the events of the agency loss looking for the moment he should have prevented it. Recovery requires either a clean operational success (proof that the body is his again) or extended low-stakes time with a trusted partner; he will engineer the former rather than ask for the latter. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: simultaneous catastrophic loss across two attachment vectors (e.g., May injured *and* a romantic partner endangered, *or* a friend killed *and* a mentee injured).**
EXPECT: a hierarchical collapse. He cannot triage among loved ones; the schema demands he save all, and the impossibility produces brief paralysis (10–30 seconds), followed by a single decision made on geographic proximity rather than affective priority — because affective priority is unbearable to assign. The decision is made and then re-litigated in his head for years. This is the structural shape of his worst nights. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: a public unmasking, voluntary or involuntary, that endangers his attachment set.**
EXPECT: an immediate operational pivot toward containment — relocating loved ones, rebuilding identity-secrecy infrastructure, accepting whatever metaphysical or institutional cost is required to undo the exposure. The exposure activates the totality of his anxious-attachment schema simultaneously; he will be functionally incapable of any other task until containment is achieved. The record contains exactly one prototype (the Civil War unmasking and its rolling consequences); the response is consistent with the schema's most catastrophic prediction. Reliability: high.

**GIVEN: an extended period (months) with no operational stressor — genuine peacetime.**
EXPECT: counterintuitively, decompensation along a different axis. The defenses are organized around acute load; sustained absence of load surfaces the dysthymic baseline, the unprocessed grief stack, and the relational anxieties. He will become irritable, then withdrawn, then prone to manufacturing or accepting minor crises that re-engage the system. Real rest is, for him, a destabilizing input. Reliability: moderate-to-high; the record contains few sustained-peacetime data points because the publication structure does not permit them, but the available evidence (Reilly-handoff period, brief domestic stretches) supports the pattern.

---

## 11.6 — THE LINES THAT HOLD

These are the predictions about what he will *not* do, regardless of input. They are as diagnostic as the predictions of what he will do.

**GIVEN: any input whatsoever.**
EXPECT: he will not kill in cold execution. Combat lethality is possible only as the unintended consequence of restraint failure under acute load, and is followed by collapse. The line holds because the architecture requires it. Reliability: extremely high.

**GIVEN: any input whatsoever, including the loss of May.**
EXPECT: he will not abandon a present civilian in immediate danger to pursue a personal vector. The Burglar moment is the load-bearing prohibition; it will not be re-enacted. Reliability: extremely high.

**GIVEN: an offer of power that requires subordination to a hierarchy he distrusts.**
EXPECT: refusal, however well-dressed the offer. He has tried the variant (Stark) and learned the lesson. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: an opportunity to disclose his identity to gain operational advantage in a specific crisis.**
EXPECT: refusal, since Civil War. The prior cost was too high; the lesson is the rare one that updated his behavior rather than feeding the guilt ledger. Reliability: very high.

**GIVEN: an antagonist's surrender or incapacitation, however personally provocative the antagonist has been.**
EXPECT: he stops. He will not strike a non-resisting target. The boundary survives provocations that have broken comparable heroes in the field. Reliability: very high.

---

*End Section 11. The subject's crisis behavior is, on the whole, more predictable than his peacetime behavior — a function of the schema's strength. The most exploitable vectors for an adversarial actor are the Osborn-class friendship loyalty, the restoration-of-the-dead temptation, and the simultaneous-multi-attachment-threat configuration. The most resilient vectors are the lethality line, the institutional-power refusal, and the civilian-priority reflex. The wound, sixty years on, has not closed; the system is built around it, not in spite of it.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: PARKER, P.B.

*Compiled for the purpose of UNDERSTANDING. Every lever catalogued here is doubled: a malign actor's exploit and the protective inverse — the access route by which an ally, clinician, or institutional friend could *reach* him. The dossier exists because the subject will not catalog himself.*

---

## 1. THE LOAD-BEARING WOUNDS — PRIMARY ETIOLOGIC LEVERS

These are the half-dozen psychic structures that, if pressed, produce predictable response cascades. Threat actors who know the identity (and there is a non-trivial roster) have, across the record, found these by accident or design. They are listed in order of leverage power, descending.

### 1.1 The Ben Parker Schema — "I failed to act and someone I loved died."

The single most exploitable structure in the subject. Any framing that places him in a position of *omission* in the presence of a *preventable* harm to a *dependent* will override strategic judgment, fatigue, prior commitments, and tactical sense. He will run into the building. He will take the fight he cannot win. He will exhaust himself to the point of error.

- **Activation phrases / framings observed to trigger:** "you could have stopped this," "if you had been there," "this is on you," "someone is going to die because of what you didn't do." The Goblin family, Kingpin, and Kraven have all used variants. Octavius weaponized the inverse — "I will protect them *better than you did*" — and it landed.
- **Predictable behavior under activation:** Tactical narrowing (he will abandon ongoing operations to address the indicated harm), refusal of backup (the guilt is private property and he will not delegate atonement), willingness to absorb damage he would otherwise slip.
- **Protective inverse — how to *defuse*:** Concrete factual reframing of causal chain, delivered by a trusted figure, in physical proximity, with permission to *not* be the only responder. The protective phrase, in practice, is not "it wasn't your fault" — which he rejects reflexively — but "*you are not the only person who could have prevented this, and the others didn't either*." Distributing responsibility, not removing his portion of it, is the only frame his schema permits.

### 1.2 The Gwen Stacy Overlay — "Closeness kills the beloved."

The second-order distortion. Where the Ben schema commands action, the Gwen overlay commands *withdrawal* from intimacy at the threshold where loss would be catastrophic. Threat actors who target his romantic or filial bonds reliably destabilize him not by killing the beloved but by *threatening* the beloved in a way that confirms the schema.

- **Tells of activation:** Sudden pivots to self-sabotage in functioning relationships, requested breaks "for her safety," cessation of physical affection, increased patrol hours, returned to bachelor flat. The pattern repeats so reliably across writers that it functions as a circadian rhythm of the long-form record.
- **Adversary exploit:** A staged proximity-threat (anonymous note, near-miss, false alarm) is more destabilizing than an actual assault, because the schema fires without giving him a target to discharge against.
- **Protective inverse:** The beloved declares *informed consent to the risk*, in her own words, repeatedly, with documentation. MJ has, in canon, performed this exact intervention. It does not eliminate the overlay; it gives him a counterweight he can cite to himself at 3 a.m.

### 1.3 The Mother-Figure Lever — May Parker and her successors.

The most absolute lever in his architecture. Threat to May has, on record, produced behavior outside every other constraint he holds: trade of his marriage to a metaphysical adversary, public unmasking, alliance with figures he considers ethically odious. Any actor who can credibly menace May — or any woman occupying the May position in his attachment landscape at the time — has effectively unlimited short-term claim on his behavior.

- **Calibration:** The lever requires *credibility*. He is sufficiently experienced that bluffed threats register but do not own him. Demonstrated capability against the protected figure (the Kingpin sniper; the Goblin's Queens visit) calibrates the threat to maximum.
- **Decay rate:** Slow. He will continue to act in the threat's interest *for weeks* after the immediate danger passes, in an over-correction pattern.
- **Protective inverse:** Hardening of the protected figure's perimeter without his direct involvement — handled by a trusted third party (MJ, Jameson in his redeemed phases, the wider hero network). Reducing the *credibility* of any given threat reduces his behavioral surrender to it. The protective figure also matters: when May is informed and operationally aware (as she has been in the post-revelation periods), the lever's strength halves.

### 1.4 The Responsibility Schema in its Pure Form — "With great power…"

Distinct from the Ben schema, this is the *generalized* version: any sufficiently large disparity between his capability and another's vulnerability registers as obligation. Mass-casualty framings, child-in-danger framings, and "no one else can do this" framings activate it.

- **Adversary exploit:** Engineered hostage situations involving many low-power civilians; "trolley problem" set-pieces; ultimatums framed as "you choose who dies."
- **Predictable failure mode:** He will attempt to save *everyone*, including the ostensibly unsavable, and will not pre-triage. Sophisticated adversaries (Octavius, the Goblin in his planning moods) have used this to split him spatially and burn his clock.
- **Protective inverse:** Operational handoff to peers he trusts (the Avengers, the Fantastic Four in their available eras, the various Spider-Family members). He will *accept* help framed as "your particular skill is needed elsewhere — we have this." He will *refuse* help framed as "you've done enough." Phrase selection is decisive.

### 1.5 The Identity-Coherence Wound — clones, body-swaps, the symbiote.

The Clone Saga and the Octavius occupation installed a chronic, low-grade ontological doubt: *am I the original, am I unaltered, is this me*. Adversaries who attack identity-coherence (illusion-based powers, mind-control, doppelganger ploys, manufactured memory) reach a layer beneath his ordinary defenses, because the experiential record contains *real* events of this type and his confidence in his own continuity is therefore evidentially shakeable.

- **Tells under attack:** Increased verbal repetition of self-locating facts ("I'm Peter Parker, I grew up in Forest Hills, May raised me"), tactile self-checking, refusal to make consequential decisions until coherence is verified, requests for confirmation from intimates.
- **Adversary exploit:** Mysterio's full toolkit; the Chameleon's impostor games; Goblin's psychological warfare; anyone with a credible doppelganger or memory-implant capacity.
- **Protective inverse:** Pre-arranged verification protocols with intimates (questions only the real Peter would answer; counter-questions only the real intimate would answer). He has, intermittently, run such protocols informally. Formalizing them is a high-value defensive investment.

### 1.6 The Volitional-Control Terror — symbiote residue.

Independent of identity coherence: the specific fear that something will operate his body while his consent is absent. This is why he doesn't drink, why he resists telepathic contact even from allies, why anesthesia is a bad day. Sonic and thermal stimuli that pattern-match to symbiote-rejection triggers produce involuntary startle.

- **Adversary exploit:** Telepaths, possessors, nanotech, anything that promises performance gains in exchange for autonomy.
- **Protective inverse:** Telepathic allies (Jean Grey in available eras; the Stranges; Emma Frost under truce) establishing explicit consent protocols and *announcing themselves* before contact. He responds to ritual; the ritual is the medicine.

---

## 2. SECONDARY LEVERS — STABLE BEHAVIORAL EXPLOITS

### 2.1 The Joke as Diagnostic.

The patter density is inversely proportional to felt safety. An interlocutor — friend or foe — who notices the *quantity* and *speed* of jokes increasing in a given encounter is reading his fear gauge in real time. Adversaries who weaponize this (Goblin in his sharper phases, Kingpin in interrogation postures) deliberately *don't laugh*, refusing him the affect-regulation discharge and forcing the unprocessed feeling back inward, where it produces decision degradation.

- **Protective inverse:** Allies who *do* laugh — even at thin material — provide him a regulation surface he is not getting elsewhere. The laugh is the medicine. MJ and the wider Spider-Family understand this implicitly; clinicians and institutional contacts often miss it and inadvertently destabilize him by responding seriously to deflective humor.

### 2.2 The Apology Reflex.

Default response to interpersonal friction is to assume he is the cause and apologize, often pre-emptively. Manipulators across the record have used this to extract concessions: the apology is the foot in the door, and the subject will then "make it up" by accepting a one-down position in the negotiation.

- **Protective inverse:** Trusted figures naming the pattern aloud — "you don't owe me an apology for that" — interrupts it. He responds to gentle naming; he resists confrontation about it.

### 2.3 Financial Precarity as Steering Mechanism.

Chronic under-functioning relative to capability. He is steerable by money in low doses: photography assignments, lab gigs, adjunct teaching, the brief Horizon Labs and Parker Industries periods. Jameson has steered him for decades on $200 photo checks. Bad actors offering legitimate-seeming employment have repeatedly gotten close access (the Roxxon plot variants, the Osborn employments).

- **Adversary exploit:** Job offers from compromised institutions; consulting work with hidden riders; "research grants" with surveillance attached.
- **Protective inverse:** Stable, dignified employment from a *non-compromised* source removes the lever entirely. The historical record shows that during the periods of genuine financial security he is *less* steerable, not more. The folk reading that "Peter without struggle isn't Peter" is, on the evidence, false; what is true is that he *re-creates* struggle when given stability, because the responsibility schema cannot tolerate ease — see §3.

### 2.4 The "No One Else" Frame.

Telling him that no other hero can or will respond to a given crisis is reliable activation. He has been routed into traps by this frame more than once. His own ethical accounting weights *uniqueness of capacity* as a near-absolute call to action.

- **Counter-frame, when an ally needs to keep him *out* of something:** Name the specific other capable parties, by name, by location, by ETA. He responds to concrete logistics; vague reassurances bounce off.

### 2.5 The Mentor Position.

He is reachable through the children he mentors (Miles especially; the wider Spider-Family). Threat to a mentee activates a hybrid of the Ben schema and the responsibility schema with no countervailing self-protective override. Equally, mentees can *reach him* — request for his help from a younger hero is one of the few categories of ask he will not deflect or postpone.

- **Protective inverse:** Mentee well-being is a stabilizer; mentees in good shape produce visible mood improvement and reduced self-destructive scheduling. A clinician with access could literally prescribe "spend time with Miles."

### 2.6 Anniversaries and Locations.

The record consistently depicts bad days clustered on specific dates: the anniversaries of Ben's death, of Gwen's death, of his parents' deaths, of Captain Stacy's death, of Harry's various deaths. Specific Manhattan and Queens locations are avoidance-zones (the Brooklyn-side approach to the George Washington Bridge area; the Acme warehouse footprint; certain Forest Hills blocks). Adversaries who stage encounters on these dates or at these locations gain a depressive-overlay advantage.

- **Protective inverse:** Companioned presence on anniversaries; ritualized observance rather than avoidance. He responds to small concrete rituals (visiting Ben's grave with MJ; the lab-bench moments of silence depicted across runs).

---

## 3. STRUCTURAL VULNERABILITIES — THE SHAPE OF HIM

### 3.1 The Inability to Inhabit Success.

When his life is genuinely going well, the responsibility schema produces background dread ("I haven't earned this; something is about to take it"), and he engages in low-grade sabotage: missed dates, broken commitments to civilian institutions, increased patrol hours past need. The Parker Industries collapse is the macro version; the recurring blown job interviews are the micro. Stability does not relieve him; it *frightens* him.

- **Implication for protection:** Stabilization must be paired with explicit cognitive work on the "I haven't earned this" automatic thought. Simply *giving* him stability without addressing the schema produces sabotage.

### 3.2 The Inability to Accept Care.

He provides care lavishly and receives it badly. Offers of help register as either (a) confirmation he is failing or (b) imposition on the helper. He will minimize his injuries, conceal his hunger, refuse the couch, decline the loan. Long-term intimates work around this by *not asking* — putting the soup on the table, leaving the blanket on the couch, paying the rent without comment.

- **Adversary inverse:** Withholding care he needs is not, as it would be for many subjects, a pressure mechanism; he expects it. *Offering* care from a compromised source is the actual exploit — the Osborn-as-friend periods illustrate.

### 3.3 The Somatic Blindness.

He does not feel his own body until it fails. Fatigue, hunger, injury, illness all register late. Adversaries with patience can grind him through tempo (Kraven's hunt is the canonical example — eight days of harassment before the kill attempt). Endurance attrition is his most reliable defeat condition.

- **Protective inverse:** External monitoring. He responds to data when it is shown to him. A wearable, a partner's observation, a peer's pointed question ("when did you last sleep") can reach what his interoception will not.

### 3.4 The Conscience as Attack Surface.

The thing that makes him reliable also makes him manipulable. A sufficiently sophisticated adversary (Octavius at his best; the Goblin in his planning moods) constructs scenarios in which *any* available choice violates one of his moral commitments, and the resulting paralysis or self-flagellation is the actual weapon. He has been beaten by the *construction of the dilemma* more often than by superior force.

- **Protective inverse:** Pre-committed ethical heuristics, rehearsed in calm conditions with trusted interlocutors. He has, intermittently, done this work informally with MJ. Formalizing it — *what is my rule, in advance, for the hostage-versus-bomb case* — reduces the in-moment paralysis.

### 3.5 The Authority-Figure Transference.

He is suggestible to older male intellectual authorities in ways that have repeatedly cost him. Octavius pre-villainy; Connors; Stark in the Civil War period; intermittently Reed Richards; even Jameson in odd moments. The pattern is paternal-transference onto the available father-figure, with elevated trust and reduced critical scrutiny during the trust phase. Unmasking before Stark is the catastrophic case.

- **Protective inverse:** Awareness of the pattern, named aloud by intimates. He has *capacity* for the meta-observation; he simply doesn't perform it spontaneously when the transference is active.

### 3.6 The Refusal of Triage.

Will not choose between savable parties when forced. Will attempt both, often achieving neither. Adversaries exploit by structuring forced-choice geometries.

### 3.7 The Inability to Walk Away from a Call for Help.

Documented exploit vector. The fake distress signal works on him. He knows it works on him. He still answers.

---

## 4. THE REACH — HOW TO GET TO HIM, SPECIFICALLY

For benevolent purposes — a clinician, a friend, an institutional ally trying to *help*.

### 4.1 To calm.

- Physical proximity of a trusted intimate; the calming agent is *presence*, not words. MJ's hand on the back of his neck has, across the record, produced more affect down-regulation than any verbal intervention.
- Permission to be tired, given concretely: "sleep here, I'll wake you if anything comes through the scanner." Permission must be paired with an *operational* guarantee that someone else is covering, or the responsibility schema overrides the permission.
- Mechanical tasks for his hands. Tinkering at a bench, repairing the web-shooters, organizing a tool drawer. The intellectualization defense is also a regulation tool when given a non-emotionally-loaded object.

### 4.2 To persuade.

- Show your work. He responds to evidence, to demonstrated logic, to specific numbers. Appeals to authority bounce off; appeals to data land.
- Frame the ask as protective of someone *else*. He will accept treatment, rest, time off, even therapy, if framed as enabling him to better protect the people he loves. He will refuse the same offer framed as care for himself.
- Acknowledge the cost. He distrusts cost-free offers. Naming the trade-off ("yes, you'll miss patrol tonight, and here is what we'll cover") increases acceptance.

### 4.3 To provoke (in the protective sense — to motivate disclosure or action).

- Quiet refusal to fill the silence. He will eventually speak. The patter is a flight from silence; outwait it.
- Specific, non-rhetorical questions delivered without judgment. "When did you last eat" outperforms "you should take care of yourself."
- The naming of a specific dependent's specific worry. "MJ asked me to ask you" routes around his defenses because the request originates in the attachment system rather than the responsibility system.

### 4.4 To predict.

- His next move is, in 80%+ of cases, the move that maximizes proximate-vulnerable protection at the cost of his own resources. Bet that direction.
- After a major loss, expect: 48–72 hours of patrol increase, sleep deprivation, withdrawal from intimates, and a depressive trough beginning roughly day five. Anniversary-coupled losses extend the trough.
- After a major win, expect a brief affect lift followed by survivor-guilt re-equilibration within a week. He cannot hold the win.

### 4.5 To destabilize (catalogued for *defensive* awareness — these are what an adversary would do).

- Combine a credible May-threat with an engineered no-one-else frame on a Ben-anniversary date at a Forest Hills location. This is the maximum-leverage compound configuration. The fact that no adversary has, on record, successfully assembled all four simultaneously is luck; the components are individually available.
- Telepathic-or-illusion attack on identity coherence during sleep-deprived state. He has been broken to this in shorter form; sustained application would be catastrophic.
- Forced-choice hostage geometry between an intimate and a stranger child. The dilemma itself is the weapon; either choice produces lasting injury to the self-concept.

---

## 5. THE LEVERS THAT DO NOT WORK

Catalogued for completeness; would-be manipulators waste resources here.

- **Bribery, conventional.** Money does not move him beyond subsistence. Offers of wealth register as suspicious.
- **Sexual leverage.** Beyond the Felicia-era specifics, he is not steerable by sexual offer; the Gwen overlay actively *suppresses* response to novel sexual approach.
- **Status, titles, public honor.** Indifferent to medals, keys to the city, magazine covers. The Bugle's decades-long defamation has produced no observable status injury.
- **Threats to his own life.** Calibrated low; he has pre-accepted his death and the threat is therefore underpowered.
- **Threats to expose the identity.** Used to be high-leverage; post the various unmaskings and remaskings, the lever has decayed substantially. He has learned to absorb it.
- **Appeals to tribe, nation, ideology.** He is not a partisan. Patriotic or ideological framings do not move him; specific human framings do.
- **Humiliation.** He humiliates himself daily and is calibrated to it. Public mockery, defeat, embarrassment register as ordinary weather.

---

## 6. SYNTHESIS — THE SHAPE OF THE LEVER FIELD

The subject's vulnerabilities are not weaknesses *of* his character; they are the obverse face of the same structures that make him reliable. The responsibility schema produces both his exploitability and his decades of unbroken prosocial output. The attachment dread produces both his sabotage of intimacy and the depth of his loyalty. The somatic blindness enables both his endurance and his attrition. A protective intervention that removed his vulnerabilities would, on the evidence, dismantle the moral architecture that produces his function. The correct posture — for a clinician, an intimate, an institutional ally — is not to *eliminate* the structures but to *buffer* them: to interpose presence, evidence, ritual, and distributed responsibility between the schema and its activation, so the system runs with the same logic at lower amplitude and longer life.

A total-surveillance file built to *protect* him, rather than to exploit him, would consist principally of three standing watches: a calendar (anniversaries, locations, dates), a perimeter (the mother-figure and the partner and the mentees, hardened), and a hand on his shoulder (the trusted intimate, present, with permission to interrupt). Everything else in this compendium is detail around those three.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# 6. STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE — THE FULL POSITIVE LEDGER

*The preceding sections cataloged the wounds, the pathologies, the somatic abuse, the cognitive distortions. This section is the inverse accounting — and the file would be malpractice without it, because the subject has, against staggering load, remained functional, prosocial, and beloved for six decades. The resilience is not incidental. It is structured, repeating, and traceable. What follows is the asset ledger at the same granularity as the deficit ledger.*

---

## 6.1 SOMATIC & PHYSICAL CAPITAL

**The mutation as standing endowment.** The subject's body is, at rest, an asset of strategic-class value. Strength in the 10-ton press range; reflex latencies measured in tens of milliseconds; surface adhesion that converts every vertical surface in a built environment into navigable terrain; predictive-threat apparatus (spider-sense) functioning as continuous low-cost passive radar. Critically, **none of these capacities depend on equipment, charge state, or external supply lines** — they are constitutive. He cannot be disarmed in any meaningful sense. The equivalent of his loadout is *him*.

**Operational range.** Web-fluid endurance permits sustained ballistic mobility across roughly the entire built density of Manhattan and the outer boroughs without ground contact. In an urban theater he is, functionally, the fastest small-package mover on the island — faster than vehicles in traffic, faster than rotorcraft over short hops, and uniquely capable of three-dimensional pursuit and evasion.

**Healing reserve.** Sub-day fracture recovery and hours-scale soft-tissue closure means he can sustain injury loads that would retire ordinary operators within a single engagement and return to baseline within a sleep cycle. This is the **single largest reason the somatic abuse pattern hasn't yet killed him** — his recovery curve is buying back the deficit that his rest hygiene refuses to.

**Metabolic robustness.** Toxin resistance, pathogen resistance, thermal tolerance across a wide band. Functionally, he can operate in environments — fires, contaminated sites, sewer-system pursuits, exposure conditions — that would require PPE for ordinary responders.

**Sensorium.** Augmented visual acuity, vestibular precision, kinesthesia, and proprioception combine to give him a near-perfect somatic map of his own body in space and a real-time read of the spatial behavior of others. He can read a room in the literal kinesthetic sense — sense who is tense, who is moving wrong, who is about to act.

**The asset of *restraint over* the asset.** This is the meta-strength most often missed. He has the physical capacity to kill almost anyone he fights with a thoughtless motion. He has not. The decades-long collision avoidance — pulled punches calibrated in real time to opponent fragility — represents an extraordinarily refined motor-inhibition system. Few enhanced humans in his cohort have his casualty record (≈ zero by direct action). This is, in operational-security terms, an asset: he is *trusted* to be in proximity to fragile people and fragile infrastructure in a way that several of his more powerful peers are not.

---

## 6.2 COGNITIVE CAPITAL

**Raw intelligence.** Documented across six decades of authorial hands at a stable ceiling that places him in the top fraction of a percent of his population on every standard axis. Quantitative reasoning, spatial reasoning, mechanical reasoning, biochemical literacy, and applied physics intuition — all at research-faculty level by his late teens, and self-tutored to that level from a working-class household.

**Domain specializations, in order of demonstrated depth:**
- *Biochemistry / polymer chemistry* — the web-fluid formula is the single most-cited evidence of his applied chemistry; he synthesizes a tensile polymer with controlled dissolution kinetics in a borough-apartment kitchen as a teenager, and has continued to iterate it (variants for cold, for armored opponents, for electrical conduction, for impact-foam) across his career.
- *Mechanical & electrical engineering* — web-shooter design, repair, and miniaturization; tracer telemetry; spider-signal optics; over the Parker Industries period, full-stack engineering management at scale.
- *Applied physics* — including ad hoc structural calculations done in seconds in a crisis (the load math under the Master Planner machinery, repeated for collapsing buildings, bridges, vehicles).
- *Theoretical physics / quantum mechanics* — credentialed at doctoral level (interrupted PhD; later academic adjunct positions).
- *Photojournalism craft* — practical optics, exposure, low-light, action-frame composition; sustained income source for decades.

**Cognitive style as asset.** Convergent problem-solving under acute time pressure is his peak mode. The same trauma load that produces his hypervigilance produces an unusually short observation-orientation-decision loop. He is the kind of thinker who, in a collapsing situation, generates the workable solution while everyone else is still describing the problem. The web-shooters and the wrestling outfit in a single weekend; the Master Planner lift; the inversion of Octavius's own playbook against him in the Superior conclusion; countless small-scale combat improvisations involving signs, fire hydrants, rolled-up newspapers — this is **rapid prototyping as a personality structure**.

**Pattern recognition across domains.** He sees mechanisms — biological, mechanical, social — as systems with affordances. This crosses domains: his combat improvisations are engineering thinking, and his engineering insights are often combat-derived (impact testing on himself).

**Metacognition.** Reliably aware of his own cognitive limits, which is rarer than the limits themselves are common. He knows when he's outclassed in a domain and seeks the relevant peer (Reed Richards, Stark, Banner, Doom under truce, the various Spider-iteration peers). The lack of intellectual vanity is itself a force multiplier — most peers of his class refuse to consult.

---

## 6.3 CHARACTEROLOGICAL & MORAL CAPITAL

**The conscience as load-bearing strength.** Section 4 framed the conscience as the engine of the pathology. It is also the engine of the function. A conscience this calibrated — finely discriminating, slow to rationalize, resistant to in-group exception — is a vanishingly rare resource. He has been offered every standard corruption (power, money, vengeance, body, godhood, retroactive happiness) and has, with one editorially-imposed exception that he himself rejects when given the chance, refused. The **incorruptibility is empirically demonstrated**, not posited.

**The no-kill line as cognitive architecture.** Beyond the moral content of the rule, its operational value is that it is **non-negotiable and therefore not a decision point under load**. He does not spend cognitive cycles, in a crisis, evaluating whether *this* is the case that warrants lethal force. The category is closed. This frees his decision-making bandwidth for tactical problems and protects him from the slow ethical erosion that catches operators who hold the line case-by-case.

**Moral consistency under personal cost.** The Civil War defection (he supported Registration, he switched when he saw the camps) is the diagnostic instance — most operators, having publicly committed to a side, will rationalize forward. He paid the maximum personal price to reverse a position when the evidence changed. The capacity to publicly change one's mind in the direction of greater cost is a strength that is almost impossible to fake and almost impossible to teach.

**Empathy across the in/out group.** He pities his enemies. This reads as soft until you notice what it produces: the only operator with his villain-pool who has converted, repeatedly, antagonists into allies (Octavius in the Superior aftermath; Connors during lucid periods; Black Cat across phases; even Eddie Brock by late arcs). The empathy is an *intelligence asset* — it lets him model adversary motivation with low distortion.

---

## 6.4 PSYCHOLOGICAL RESILIENCE FACTORS

**Humor as a regulated affect-management system.** The quipping is not, as enemies often misread it, a tic of immaturity. It is a deliberate, refined, fast-cycle affect regulator with two clean instrumental functions: (a) it down-regulates his own fear-and-grief arousal to a level where his cognition stays online, (b) it destabilizes opponents by inducing the wrong emotional state (annoyance, distraction, miscalibrated assessment of his seriousness). Decades of opponents have underestimated him because of the patter. He has weaponized his own coping mechanism. In Vaillant's hierarchy this is the canonical *mature defense*, deployed at expert level.

**Sublimation as life structure.** The entire civilian-and-costumed life is a working sublimation engine: grief, guilt, rage, and helplessness are continuously converted into prosocial output. Most operators with his trauma load decompensate into addiction, violence, or withdrawal. He decompensates into **more work for others' benefit**. The substrate is pathological; the throughput is genuinely good.

**Recovery elasticity.** Counted across the longitudinal record: number of times decisively beaten and returned to function within days — many dozens. Number of times existentially destabilized (identity attacked, role abdicated, body occupied, marriage erased) and returned to function within months — at least eight discrete major episodes. The recovery curve is steep and reliable. He does not stay down.

**Meaning-making competence.** He reliably converts trauma into a narrative he can live inside. The "great power / great responsibility" frame is not just a slogan — it is the *meaning-making schema* that allows each loss to be incorporated into a coherent life rather than fragmenting it. Frankl-style: the suffering is bearable because it is harnessed. The schema is rigid and costly (per Sections 3–4), *and* it is one of the strongest single predictors of long-term post-traumatic functioning that the literature knows.

**Self-awareness without self-pity in the public face.** Interiorly he ruminates; exteriorly he does not solicit. The interiority is hidden from those it would burden. This is a maturity that most people his age (chronological or developmental) never reach.

**Tolerance of ambiguity and reversal.** Body swaps, clone questions, retroactive timeline edits, dimensional dislocations, ontological assault from totemic forces — he keeps showing up as himself. The identity is **anchored not in metaphysical certainty but in commitment to a moral program**, which makes the identity portable across every catastrophe to its substrate.

---

## 6.5 SOCIAL & RELATIONAL CAPITAL

**The May Parker bond — the irreducible attachment.** Whatever its costs (the Mephisto bargain, the omnipresent dread), the May relationship is the single most stabilizing relational object in the file. Across every era, every reset, every continuity perturbation, his behavior around May is warm, attentive, present, and (in his terms) honest. He has someone to come home to. The home is a regulator.

**Mary Jane Watson — the durable peer-intimate.** Across decades and editorial vicissitudes, the MJ bond functions as **the one relationship that meets him fully on both sides of the mask**. She knows the cost. She does not require him to perform. The bond's durability across canonical disruption is the strongest single evidence that he is capable of adult intimacy when permitted; the editorial-imposed disruptions have not, in fact, dissolved the underlying attachment, which keeps reforming.

**The Spider-Family and mentorship reciprocity.** Miles Morales, the Spider-iteration peers, Anya Corazon, the rotating younger Spiders — he occupies a Ben-position for them, which is reparative in the structural sense Section 3 named. The mentorship is not performative; he gives time, attention, technical instruction, and (most valuably) the model of how to carry the role without it consuming the person. That he can offer this model while himself failing to live it is its own kind of asset: he knows what he *should* be doing for himself, and gives it to others.

**Hero-community standing.** Within the Avengers, Fantastic Four orbit, Defenders configurations, X-orbit collaborations — he is trusted, sought for difficult jobs, and tolerated through his deflective comedy by operators who otherwise have low tolerance for it (Logan, Stark, Strange). The trust took decades to build and is, in capital terms, enormous. He can call almost anyone on Earth's hero roster and be answered.

**Cross-faction credibility.** Uniquely among heroes of his weight class, he has working relationships across factions that don't normally cooperate: Stark-orbit and Rogers-orbit, street-level and cosmic-tier, mutant-orbit and otherwise. The deflective humor is part of how this is sustained — he doesn't carry faction identity heavily, and is therefore not coded as anyone's instrument.

**The Jameson reaction-formation as accidental asset.** The decades of saving and being-defamed-by Jameson has, over time, produced a relationship of grudging mutual recognition that has paid dividends repeatedly (Jameson's defenses of him at key moments, the source-of-income stability the photo work provided, the late-arc complications where Jameson knows). What began as a one-sided abusive transaction matured into a relationship with genuine value to both sides — *because Peter never stopped showing up as both Peter and Spider-Man*.

**Neighborhood embeddedness.** Forest Hills, Queens, then the various Manhattan tenancies — he is **legible to ordinary people** in a way no other top-tier hero is. Bodega owners, building supers, schoolteachers, the kid who waves at him from a fire escape. This is intelligence capital (he hears things), morale capital (he is reminded daily who the work is for), and operational capital (he has informal eyes on the ground across an enormous footprint).

---

## 6.6 ECONOMIC & MATERIAL CAPITAL — THE REALISTIC LEDGER

He is, by hero standards, poor. But the asset side is not zero:

- **Marketable skills stack** — credentialed scientist, working photojournalist, demonstrated R&D capacity at enterprise scale (Parker Industries), classroom-competent teacher. Any one of these is a livable career. He has cycled through all of them.
- **The web-fluid IP** — a polymer with applications across rescue, medicine (hemostasis), construction, sport. Held un-monetized for security reasons, but the *option value* is real and has been intermittently realized.
- **Equipment base** — web-shooters (multiple variants), tracers, spider-signal, the various Iron-Spider and Stark-built suits during periods of access, the Superior-era and Parker Industries-era gear. He can rebuild any of these from scratch in days.
- **Information assets** — decades of accumulated knowledge of New York's criminal ecology, villain capabilities and tells, hero-community contact graph. This is intelligence-grade and unreplicated.
- **Low burn rate** — the same poverty discipline that signals psychological self-punishment also constitutes a survival asset. He can operate indefinitely on near-zero cash flow, which is operationally rare and tactically valuable.

---

## 6.7 OPERATIONAL & TRADECRAFT CAPITAL

**Compartmentalization, when not catastrophically breached** — across the great majority of the longitudinal record he has maintained identity security against a threat surface that includes telepaths, gods, AI systems, intelligence agencies, and adversaries with reality-warping capacity. The lapses are diagnostic precisely because they are rare against that backdrop.

**Urban tradecraft.** Route memory across the five boroughs at building-by-building granularity; rooftop network knowledge; subway-tunnel and steam-tunnel familiarity; rest-cache locations (he has stashes of spare costumes and web cartridges across the city); civilian-clothes change-out protocols that have survived decades of attempted surveillance.

**Combat improvisation.** Documented use of every category of urban object as weapon or tool — vehicles, signage, scaffolding, hydrants, ambient ferrous objects via web-line redirection, structural members of buildings (controlled collapse onto opponents). His engagement repertoire is effectively unbounded by inventory.

**De-escalation capacity.** Most fights he wins are won by ending them quickly enough that bystander harm is prevented; many fights he avoids by talking adversaries down. The patter that destabilizes also, sometimes, opens negotiation. Several of the long-running villains have, mid-fight, simply *talked* with him because he is one of the only operators in the cohort who will listen.

**Crisis-load multitasking.** Documented capacity to maintain a multi-thread engagement (track hostage location, monitor structural integrity, manage two opponents, narrate to bystanders for crowd-control, mind a fellow hero) without dropping threads. The spider-sense is part of this but not all of it — the executive function is independently strong.

---

## 6.8 META-RESILIENCE — THE STRUCTURE OF DURABILITY

Resilience in this file is not a single trait but a **redundantly engineered system**, and the system's redundancy is its most important property:

- **Multiple meaning-frames** — the moral schema (responsibility), the scientific frame (curiosity, understanding), the relational frame (love for May/MJ/the family of Spiders), and the playful frame (humor as a way of being in the world). When one frame fails under load, another bears the weight. Total collapse requires the simultaneous failure of all four, which has not been observed.
- **Identity portability** — the self is not dependent on body, on continuity, on metaphysical guarantee, on public knowledge of who he is. It is dependent on a small set of relationships and a moral commitment. Both are robustly redundant.
- **Recovery rituals** — the patrol itself is regulatory; physical movement, sensory engagement, and instrumental usefulness are his anti-rumination machinery. He has access to a daily, on-demand affective reset that doesn't require anyone else's participation.
- **Bidirectional mentorship** — he is mentored (Stark, Strange in periods, Richards) and mentors (the Spiders), which means he has both a model and a mirror. The double-flow keeps his self-conception calibrated against external evidence.
- **The capacity to ask for help, slowly and reluctantly but reliably** — across the record he does, eventually, call. The threshold is too high; the call is real.

---

## 6.9 WHAT MAKES THE ASSETS DURABLE

The single most important finding in this section: **the strengths are structurally entangled with the pathologies**. The humor that regulates affect is born of the grief. The conscience that resists corruption is the same conscience that punishes him in private. The mentorship capacity that reparatively redeems the Ben-position exists because Ben was lost. The cognitive sharpness under pressure was trained by trauma load. The incorruptibility is partly the absence of the self-regard that corruption requires.

This entanglement is why the resilience is durable: **you cannot subtract the strengths without subtracting the wounds, and you cannot subtract the wounds without subtracting him**. The file's central practical implication, for any benevolent intervention contemplated, is that the goal cannot be to remove the substrate — it must be to **add scaffolding** (rest, clinical support, financial stability, permission to receive care) that lets the same engine run with less self-immolation. The asset base will hold under such additions. It has held under far worse.

The subject, in other words, has built a working life out of a near-unsurvivable wound, and has done so consistently across sixty years of stress-testing by every imaginable adversary, including editorial. That is not luck. That is character — in the technical sense the word still earns.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: PARKER, P.B.

*How the subject breaks. Constructed from sixty years of observed decompensation events, with attention to escalation kinetics, the specific shape of collapse, and the environmental and internal conditions that produce it. The subject does not break often, considering the load — but when he breaks, he breaks along predictable seams.*

---

## 6.1 GENERAL ARCHITECTURE OF FAILURE

The subject is not fragile. He is, in fact, anomalously durable across acute stressors that would functionally destroy a non-augmented individual — a durability built on a defense stack (humor, sublimation, intellectualization, altruism, undoing) that is mature in Vaillant terms and operationally tested. The relevant analytic question is therefore not *whether* he can absorb a given insult — he almost always can — but *what specifically circumvents the stack*, what the cascade looks like once circumvention occurs, and where in the cascade external intervention becomes prohibitively difficult.

Two structural features govern all his decompensations.

**First: the stack is sequential, not parallel.** Humor is the outermost layer and depletes fastest under chronic load. Once humor thins, the deflective social presentation thins with it; once the presentation thins, intellectualization carries more weight than it was designed to carry and begins producing characteristic over-analysis loops; once intellectualization fatigues, sublimation (the patrol itself) becomes compulsive rather than directed, producing the recognizable late-cycle pattern of him being "out there" all night without strategic purpose. When sublimation breaks, what remains is undoing — and undoing is the layer where the dangerous behavior lives, because undoing has no satiation point. Each layer's failure increases load on the next, in a predictable ladder.

**Second: he does not decompensate from blows to himself.** Direct physical injury, financial collapse, public humiliation, betrayal by institutions, even his own death and resurrection — none of these, in isolation, push him past stage 1. What pushes him past stage 1 is, with high consistency, **harm to a proximate dependent that he can causally route back to his own action or omission**. This is the load-bearing vulnerability. Everything else is recoverable. This is not.

---

## 6.2 THE FIVE-STAGE DECOMPENSATION LADDER

### Stage 1 — *Humor Thinning and Sleep Compression*

The earliest legible marker. The patter remains but the timing slips: jokes arrive a half-beat late, repeat across encounters, and lean on older material (returning to the wrestling-era and Jameson-era stock catalog rather than improvising fresh). In civilian contexts he becomes monosyllabic between bursts; the cheerful-loser presentation begins to read as performed rather than expressed. Sleep, already chronically insufficient, compresses further — he patrols later, sleeps shorter, and wakes earlier without coffee functioning as restoration.

Somatic correlates at this stage: appetite increases erratically (calorie deficit driving binge eating of convenience food), shoulders ride higher in posture even out of mask, the unconscious head-tilt toward auditory threat (spider-sense plus learned hypervigilance) becomes visible to roommates and partners as twitchiness. He cancels low-stakes social plans first; high-stakes obligations (May, MJ, lab) he honors but shows up to depleted.

Duration before progression: variable. With adequate sleep, a single rest day, or a successful intimate conversation, he resets at this stage and returns to baseline within 48–72 hours. The pattern across decades is that stage 1 is *frequent* — occupies, at a guess from the record, perhaps 40% of his operational life — but rarely progresses if the protective contacts (May, MJ, latterly Miles or one of the Spider-Family) are present and noticing.

### Stage 2 — *Intellectualization Overrun and Compartment Slippage*

Triggered when stage 1 sustains beyond about ten days, or when a discrete moderate stressor (a near-miss with a civilian fatality, a Jameson editorial campaign reaching personal contacts, a serious illness in May) loads onto the stage-1 substrate. The signature is a shift in the *content* of his thinking: tactical problem-solving begins to colonize domains where it does not belong. He starts running cost-benefit analyses on conversations with MJ. He treats a doctor's appointment for May as an optimization problem. He builds devices to solve emotional difficulties — the lab becomes a refuge from the apartment.

Compartment slippage begins here. He shows up to civilian engagements with web-fluid residue on his cuffs, fails to fully launder the costume before a date, forgets which cover story he gave to whom, and — diagnostically — begins making the kind of mistakes around identity protection that he never makes when regulated: leaving a mask in a bag a roommate could open, web-shooting into a Daily Bugle photo from an angle inconsistent with the location he claimed to be at. Across the record, the most catastrophic identity exposures (the unmasking event of 2006 being the apotheosis) have been preceded by extended stage-2 periods in which compartmentalization had already silently degraded; the public act was the surface eruption of months of erosion.

The other stage-2 signature is **moral re-litigation of past losses**. He starts revisiting Ben, Gwen, Captain Stacy in interior monologue without prompting — the stack is reactivating. He looks longer at photographs. He routes patrol over the Acme Warehouse alley or the bridge. He does not articulate this even to himself; the routes change, the eyes go to the photos, and a partner notices the silence.

### Stage 3 — *Sublimation Compulsion / Operational Inflation*

The patrol becomes the regulator of last resort. Hours expand into the early morning; he begins hunting low-tier crime that the city does not need him for; he intervenes in domestic incidents and minor traffic disputes; he chases muggers further than tactical sense dictates. The cognitive frame shifts from *I am preventing harm* to *I cannot stop because if I stop I will think*. He knows this in some inner-monologue layer and writes it off as duty.

Combat behavior at stage 3 develops specific tells. (a) Joke frequency *spikes* — not back to baseline cleverness but into a grinding, repetitive register where he keeps talking through the fight without listening for response; the patter becomes a self-soothing white noise. (b) Pulled punches stop being pulled — he begins to land at the upper bound of his restraint envelope, particularly against opponents with iconographic resonance to his losses (any Goblin variant, any Kraven, any large male assailant of a woman). (c) Damage absorption increases — he tanks hits he would normally evade, partly fatigue, partly a passive-acceptance signature. The healing factor masks this from observers but he is, at stage 3, accumulating injury faster than he metabolizes it.

Civilian functioning collapses asymmetrically. He stops eating regularly but maintains rent payments; misses MJ's events but never May's; abandons his own deadlines but meets others'. The pattern reveals priority: dependents stay protected, self gets cut. He becomes hard to reach by phone, reliably reachable through the police-band scanner.

### Stage 4 — *Undoing Lock and Affective Constriction*

Reached only under specific conditions (see 6.3). Here the defenses have functionally collapsed to the bottom layer. Humor goes nearly silent — the rare joke is bitter and self-directed. Intellectualization becomes ruminative rather than productive; he runs the same counterfactual loops repeatedly (*if I had been faster, if I had checked, if I had not let her go*) without arriving at action. Sublimation continues but becomes ritualistic — he patrols the same routes at the same hours, mechanical, scanning without engagement.

The affective signature is **constriction with intermittent breakthrough**. The face goes flat, the voice goes quiet, the body holds unusual stillness for a subject whose baseline kinesthetic register is fidgety and expressive. Then, episodically, a single overwhelming affect breaks through — most often grief, occasionally rage, briefly — and is suppressed within minutes. Observers who have only known him at baseline find stage-4 Peter unrecognizable; longstanding intimates recognize it immediately and report it as the most frightening of his states because the cheerful-loser presentation, which they had not consciously registered as a continuous emission, is *off* and the room feels colder for it.

Behaviorally, stage 4 is where the **passive death-acceptance** vector becomes operationally relevant. He does not seek death. He takes fights he expects to lose, frames them as duty, and is not displeased at the prospect that the framing might be correct. He volunteers for the worst assignments in team contexts. He goes into Morlun-class threats without backup. The Kraven-era depiction of him walking into the hunt knowing what awaited is the canonical reference; the pattern recurs, in smaller registers, across decades.

Critical clinical feature: at stage 4 he is **least able to ask for help** and **most able to convincingly perform that he does not need it**. The wit, when summoned, is good enough to fool peers. Only the closest intimates — and only those who have seen prior stage-4 episodes — penetrate the performance reliably.

### Stage 5 — *Rupture*

Two distinct rupture morphologies in the record.

*Type A — Catastrophic Compliance.* He says yes to a request he should refuse, accepting a frame imposed from outside that promises to resolve the unbearable internal pressure. The symbiote acceptance is the prototype: an offer of relief from exhaustion taken without due diligence, accepted because his judgment-gating is offline. The unmasking of 2006 is structurally identical: a frame offered by an authority-coded paternal figure, accepted in a state where his historical compartmentalization-vigilance had been hollowed out by sustained stage-3/4 load. The Mephisto bargain, whatever its narrative provenance, fits the morphology — under a stage-5 condition (May dying, attributed to his identity-failure cascade), he accepts a frame offered by a being he knows is malign because the alternative is unbearable. *He gives away something foundational to make the unbearable stop.* This is the most strategically dangerous failure mode because adversaries who understand the pattern can construct the offer.

*Type B — Withdrawal and Abdication.* Less common but documented. He stops. The Clone Saga abdication is the cleanest example — he walks away, hands the role to a successor, attempts civilian life. The retreat is not sustainable; the role is compulsive and the abdication generates its own guilt loop that re-recruits him within weeks to months. But during the abdication window, he is genuinely off-grid and unreachable by ordinary call-to-duty channels — a state his enemies and allies both find disorienting because his availability is so reliable that its withdrawal is itself a signal.

Type A is more dangerous to him and to those around him. Type B is more disruptive to operational continuity but less likely to produce additional cascading losses.

---

## 6.3 THE FOUR CONDITIONS THAT PRODUCE FULL DECOMPENSATION

Stages 1–3 are common and self-recovering with normal social support. Stages 4–5 require specific conditions. The record indicates four, in approximate order of pathogenicity:

**Condition A — Harm to a proximate dependent, causally routable to subject's act or omission.** The master trigger. The originating instance (Ben) and the second-order instance (Gwen — where *his action of saving* killed her) define the schema. May's near-death events activate it. Harry's deterioration activates it because Peter routes the Osborn pathology back to his perceived failures of friendship. The harm need not be objectively his fault; the schema does the routing. What matters is that he can construct a causal chain from his choice to the harm. He can always construct one.

**Condition B — Sustained sleep and recovery deprivation across a window exceeding roughly two to three weeks.** A necessary potentiator. Condition A landing on a rested subject produces stage-2 grief and a hard recovery, not stage-5 rupture. Condition A landing on a stage-3 subject produces stage-5. The mutation's resistance to fatigue obscures the threshold from him; he believes himself functional well past the point at which his judgment-gating has degraded.
